O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	Oh sons of great fame, I have completed this book which lies behind the science of medicine in assembly, and have finished it for its explanations and by my statements.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in vision that I would complete this book for you, which is part of the work from hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And for this reason that the work of hands is pressed in our region and is strange all around everywhere, it has been lost through science and decay, and nothing remains from the fires except small descriptions in books of the ancient ones who have moved their hands.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this arose the errors and vices, and are closed the intentions, and alienated the science.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems to me that I will live and thrive by following the order of this book according to the way of showing and declaring and abbreviating; and then came together the forms of the cauterizing instruments, and the other tools of work with the adjustment of the declaration and preparation of them, since it is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is extended.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for him who enters this that to study anatomy, as Galen says, until he knows the measure of bones, and their forms and connections and separations, and has knowledge of the marrow, nerves, and bones, and the number of joints, and the movement and rest of veins, and with his new understanding.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And for this, Hippocrates says that bone is most with the non-healthy (or 'non' as opposed to 'nous'), and with flesh (or 'nous') it is little; and similarly in the art of hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	And we say in the introduction of this book, that whoever is not familiar with the things said here, will surely fall into error and make mistakes, just as I have often seen many who interrupt the discourse on this science and abandon it without having any knowledge or sense.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	Because I saw a mad physician who opened an abscess of scrofula or the neck of a woman, and cut into the arteries of the neck; for because so much blood came out that the woman died between his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And I saw another physician who treated a stone of a man, and the stone was large; he took out a piece from his bladder, and died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have seen it happen many times that they call for treatment, and see the condition of the patient and the size of the wound, and know well whether they will die from it.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another case where they took the treatment of our land's duke who had broken his leg, and with the breakage had an injury; and the mired one was unaware and tied the break to the wound with strong binding, and did not leave it alone for salve, and so finished thus; and he commanded that he should not be untied; and stayed like this until the leg became completely infected and his feet were about to perish.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I hastened to come to untie the leg; and when I heard it was loose he was in a peaceful state and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But all corruption was already confirmed in the member, and cannot be cured; and the corruption does not cease to move through the member until the member is completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And there was another cure that destroyed the abscess, enchanted it, and then inflamed through the evil of its power.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a boil, when it is purified of melancholic humor, does not suit that one touches it with iron unless there is some way to remove what is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And dearly sons, you are in need of knowing that the work of hands is divided into two divisions: to know whether there is danger or peril in various situations; and I will show you in each one of this book where there is fear and peril.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Because it is necessary to protect yourself so that the foolish man does not speak ill of you. If you take up your arms in comfort, and gently yet firmly, use the better way so that through God's grace you come to health and are commended; leave the fearsome diseases from causing suffering for your health; and keep away from what causes doubt, and be steadfast in it so that you may come from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	The Gauls said in some of their admonishments: "Do not take ill because you are called a fool.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this book according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters are about fire cauteries and cauterizations of wet medicine, and they are arranged from the head down to the feet; and the forms of bandages, and tools for cauterization, and of all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and the treatment of boils, wounds, and extractions of arrows, and similar things. And these chapters are arranged and the forms of the instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring the dislocations and twists, and similar things. And it is arranged to have the head just as if it were a piece, and the forms of the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Also, as we remember the work, it is fitting to tell which quality of aid and which kind of nuisance each condition has.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of aid and the kind of nuisance are the longer words and subtle science, and the secrets to answering them; and those who are wise have discussed them, and agreed on them; and I am afraid to speak at length because it is a lengthy matter.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that fire cautery helps universally in all complexion, whatever the matter may be; and it is to know that there are two complexions: one is hot with matter, and the other is dry with matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In the hot and dry complexions with matter assembled, some said there was no difference and declared that fire cautery is great help; but the others said the opposite: that fire cautery has no value in diseases that come from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	Because the nature of fire is hot, and should not be cured with heat, nor dryness; and it says those who say the opposite that fire cautery does great help in cold and dry diseases that come into men's bodies.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	Because when you buy the body of a man and its moisture is in accordance with the hot complexions, you find that the body freezes.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	Because I have found it one time through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And every way, do not enter fire unless he who has tried it, and knows by long use the cautery needle, and the diversity of human humors, and the dispositions and causes of their diseases, and remedies, and space of time; for others we have no fear, especially in cold and moist illnesses.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all physicians assembled and agreed on the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, sons, that cautery is made from fire, and contains more healing power than cauterizing with burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	The fire is simple, and does not come from fire to other limbs except those which are burned.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Medicines that burn come from one member to another by removal, and cause the afflicted member to become ill with sickness and healing; and by chance, the fire does not harm the patient because of its high temperature and the kindness of its substance, unless there is excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And this I have found by experimentation and through long service and study, and it is a truth about things; and for that reason I excuse the length of my words, because I do not like to reveal to you the secret of fire, which is replied to in heat, and the quality of the work, how it cures bodily diseases, as the philosopher says when he demonstrates. Now receive this in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, when it will be decided to perform the cauteries, and when you should pray.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cautery is suitable in all times, because the dangers lurking beneath are removed by the aid of cautery; and it is itself a remedy for great pains and unbearable hardships that cannot wait until greater mischief comes to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And do not think ever, dear son, how the foolish people make; because the disease that is healed by cautery has no return; and he says so; but it's not as they think, for cautery is not just a medicine that makes the complexion move, and dries out the humors that cause pain, but rather more like a medicine in its haste of value, and by virtue of its work and its authority.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	In case of this disease, it is said that the illness comes to be at some time according to the complexion of the patient and their natural state of health, and with them are assembled excesses through the acquisition of meat and similar things, unless cautery is administered in their presence when they have little excess and moisture, as cautery for pain on the bones and similar things, and such pain does not return; but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cautery is called the rear of medicine, and it's seeing; but they don't believe that cautery is worth anything after medicine, their understanding is false, and cautery is called the rear of medicine because when we administer various types of cures for no disease, they are worthless, so we give it to them, and it's valuable.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then open well that cauterization is for those with fever, not according to the foolish opinions of madmen.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cauterization with an iron instrument is more effective than with gold, and they did not say it was used for the quality of the metal or because of its height, but rather because of the quality of the metal and because of its substance; and they said that the cauterizing levers do not cause corruption, but this is not true, as I have tried it, and I have found that it's not true in some people; and cauterization with gold is more effective than iron, just like they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And know that when you heat an instrument of gold, you do not see well how it is colored by the color of gold, and if it cools down quickly; and if you heat it too much, then it is done in the fire; and thus there are enough hindrances.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason, we will use fire cautery that we have used before on our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or you have ordered this chapter on the head to be followed with great care, because the vein is more delicate to find.
dou cautere olivaire	when olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is applied to moist and cold surfaces on the head, and there's one we do by the cause of a disease called "soda", and because of many humors that descend onto the head and ears, and into the eyes, and for many pains and discomfort from teeth, ears, and throat, as well as all diseases that come from cold, such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is such that the patient be purged by medicine soluble to clarify the head, washing away the third or fourth evil, according to what the virtues and the age and the habit of the patient can bear; and then apply the cold to the patient's head.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then make him sit cross-legged between your hands, and put his hands on some palms; after putting the root of your palm on the root of his navel between his two eyes; and when you bring your two fingers to meet, if it bleeds from an entry point then take up the cautery called "olivare", because this is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put a small signet ring with ink on the left side of the navel, and make it descend and extract your hand little by little in twisting; then lift your hand immediately, and treat the shoulder if you see a small bone; and if you do not see it, continue the cautery until you see the bone as I told you; after take some silk, and put it on wound and soft cotton inside, and put on the shoulder, and let him remain for three days; after put on a soft cloth in butter; and keep it thus until the scab falls off; after treat the wound of the joint called "tetrafarmaçon", until he is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And if the old said, when longer the wound stays on, more it purges out; and for that he uses.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And any of those said that one must cauterize the wound so much that part of the bone is burnt, and then resettle what has been burned by the bone, and treat it.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And they said that one must cauterize so much above, and pound it so hard when you press down on the bone as large as a turnip, because those humors will come out quickly; and one must cauterize the wound for a long time afterwards, then treat and set.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two ways of cauterizing do not seem to me to be entirely good in every way, because fire can cause fear in some men; and it seems to me that one should leave them alone; for the joints are weakened by the repeated solutions of nature, as we have shown in other members; and so too when the joint of the sick person is weak from nature, and the first sign of cauterization is more salutary and healing for me, therefore I follow this remedy.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	Of ancient pain in the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When all of the head causes chronic pain that lasts a long time, and the patient must use herbs and pills called “cochie”, and purgatives, ointments, and salves; and if they apply fire cautery as we have said before, and it does not help.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Before, if the head of the patient is of great strength and not too cold.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After applying fire to each corner of the head up to the bone, as we have said, and after making the cautery called “vasselz”; and it is this that you put vassellons; and apply pressure so that you do not feel anything next to the bone: the patient feels much more great pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak of this later; and it is fitting that the cauterization of the corners should be more subtle than that of the earliness of the chief, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	Fire cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When there is sudden pain in one part of the head, and the disease is spread to the eye, and the joints are purified by medicines and remedies, but all those other treatments do not help: then it must be done cautery according to two kinds, that is to say, with sharp medicine and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cautery with sharp medicine is this: take an ounce of alum, and scrape off the skin and the scab, and put it on both joints, and then make a temple (place) where the pain lies in such a way that you can place the ounce of alum under the skin; and when it is placed so, bind it well and leave it for 12 hours; and then cut away the sharp part of the alum, and leave the wound for 2 days or 3 days; then put on a cotton plug soaked in butter until it prevents pain.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment of ointment until it is healed; and if you see, then do as I have written for any burning medicine to cure.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery is done according to this method.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heating the cautery of this kind is thus the form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "clos" because the chief is made in the shape of a cloister or has a little bit of horn, and in the middle, there's a small appearance; and place it on the painful place, hold your hand and twist the iron lightly until the smallest part of the iron that cuts is burned; and raise your hand so that the artery does not burn, which is hidden, and drain abundance of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	Instruct the patient to put cotton in the wound after cutting with a needle, and place the wool on the body for three days; then put moistened cotton in butter, and treat the wound with ointment until it is healed; and if you want to cauterize this headache with the cautery called "cultellare" at its tip, be careful not to cover the artery in that headache which is not old.
de emigraine	of a headache
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	Since you cure headaches in the same way as we have said about the diseases, and it does not bring any benefit, and seeing that cauteries beforehand mentioned about medicine and iron do not give relief, then it is wise to heat the cautery called "cultellare" so much that it becomes white; and so apply a half-inch long line of ointment made from linseed oil on the wound, and hold your hand once, and do not stretch the artery so that it doesn't go against the bone; and be careful of the jaw that is frozen when eating, and let the nerves not have sight but numbness, and spasm does not come to the patient, and beware of the bleeding of the artery when it is cut, or after cutting it has great fear and pain themselves as well as for one who is not experienced and skilled; and leave the wound to itself in its natural course; but I will tell you how to stop the bleeding when the artery is cut, and show you to the patient on this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	If you see that this fire cautery does not suffice for the disease and the patient suffers, cauterize the evil in the head just as we have said, and cure the wound until it is healed. If you see, administer the fire cautery that we have said or in the chapter of extracting an artery, with the fire cautery that has two cuts; and this fire cautery is better than the other and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of ear pain from cold.
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When ear pain comes from cold, and you have tried medicines that dissolve and other treatments that we have said in the section on division, and the pains do not subside, then apply this cautery which is called "pins", because it is the form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After poking all around the diseased ear, or in one of the two, where pain holds firm on both sides, and you move a little towards the root of the ear after marking the spot with a needle, and have X points around each ear; after treatment, let it be so that it becomes sane.
de la torture de la bouche	of the mouth's torture
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Treatment of torture that must be cured by cautery is not done on those that come from a cold or phlegm, as we have said in divisions of the diseases; and do not make cautery on similar things that appear to come from old blood and pus.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you cure this semblance of torture that comes from phlegm and dries, and purgatives of the head, and gargling, and these are not enough, then it is necessary to cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one in the root of the ear, and another a little further back at the temple, and the third where the two lips meet; put the cauterium in the part that is open and healthy, and let the cauterium point directly upwards towards the head of the ear above a little below the eyebrow, and another in the temple as long as one knuckle; and let the cauterium burn until it causes the juice of the wound to come out; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it is the same as the one we have before us, but it is a bit more subtle and it is necessary to make the cuts larger; after the cure, let him be as I said before, until he is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have said, and he does not benefit from it, and the patient has no fever, then make four cauterizations: two on each of the two horns of the head, one on the head itself, and one at the "vessel" which we called earlier, and a cautery on the lower part of the belly in the mouth; and do as we have said before.
de litargie	of lassitude.
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this disease it is necessary to give the patient large and pill-like pills for the brain; after cutting off the head of the patient, put the emplaster of sinapis on the occipital bone which is written in the treatment of emplastres; and this is the method of cautery: if he does so as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it is healthy in that way, good is best; and if it isn't, he shall have three cauteries of the ear on both sides when they are just below the neck, and two of these cauteries shall be between each one; and let the healer do as he has done with others, and if you see anything added to him, and the sick man is suffering, then do one cautery in a mile; and when it is time, do two more on both shoulders and the cure until he is healthy; and let the cauteries which are called "olivare" be done as I have previously said.
de la froidor dou chief	of the coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary that the head be purified with years and what we have previously said; after cleansing the head of the sick person, then do cautery on both ears, and the first one on each cheek, and three above the spine of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient suffers greatly, and the disease is severe, then do four cauteries on the spine of the back; let him rest as long as his fever decreases, and take away your hand; after that, let the healer wait until he is healthy, and let the cauteries which are called "olivare" be done as we have previously said.
de l’epilempsie	From the epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epileptics should only use fire cautery on those who are flaky, and it is fitting to first soften the brain with years and other remedies that we have mentioned in the division when the patient is great and suffers from many of the medicines.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is an infant who cannot endure suffering, then make them gargle and chew bone, softening the brain often with sweet meat; after they are placed on their back, and you do fire cautery according to what we have said before, and fire cautery on the headboard, and on each horn; and if the patient is strong and suffers, make them fire cautery as I told the one who had paralysis and softening of flesh, on the spine in the back and neck, with olive oil according to the manner that I said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is sick, if he does fire cautery subtle according to this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When because of melancholy there are superfluities or corrupted moistures and a great flux, then the fire cautery on tender parts as we have said to him who had paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if the superfluities decline due to melancholy and the body of the sick person is moist, then let him drink something so that the intellects be clarified, according as it is beforehand in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After dressing the head of the sick person; after doing the bandage of linen well made, like the circle, if you put it on the head; and the patient must tie crossed, and held tight from all parts; after presenting the bandage, and pouring into him the balm of old sheep fat; and putting hot to fire temperately, so that he can endure being poured into him; after voiding the circle inside the head, and letting it cool off; and doing this to each sick person once a week with another good governance, until they are healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	If you see someone being cautered while making many pricks all over the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This method of cautery causes the brain to swell more, and then cover it with wet cotton in butter and gelatin.
de l’awe des eulz	of the eyes.
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the eye comes first in this way by the signs I have said in division, then begin and do give the patient something that cleanses the head, and guards against all moistures, and make it sweat or take a bath several times daily.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After he repeats the head, and makes him cautery on the skin of his head, and makes two cauteries on both temples, if there are two swellings in both eyes together, or one in each; and cut all over the cautery to all veins and arteries that are under the wound, and make them cautery long according to the width of the temple; and guard against decomposition of blood, and if you see too much blood coming out, stain him with powder as much as possible as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and incising the cause, how to do it; and never at any time have you taken a cautery or hatterel under the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	Of men of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed and are on the veins, or at the arteries that are in the appearance of the head outside; and one sees that it's of superfluities cold flaccid, then do the cautery as I said at the beginning under the eyes: cut the forehead, and two cauterize above the two temples, and two cauterize under the two bones; and if there is need more, so cauterize with a sharp point of the thread over the eyelid.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	Out of the flesh through the eyelids
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper. Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of oil is softened by disease and moisture, then apply the cautery called "olivare".
de coi ci est li forme:	Because of this there is
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see to make two cauteries on the two sores as long as the sores are; and do not hold back your hand unless the third part of the paper is burned, according to the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	One hair which touches the oil
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	There is never a time when the hairs of the oils are converted to wool, and they prick at the oil, and then one makes cauteries according to two manners: that is to say, by fire or by hot medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they are born and have even hairs, then place the patient in a safe place; after that, draw on paper around the eyes a figure like that of the mullet, and so as it begins with signs of the hair growth; then put cotton moistened in ointment of beeswax and musk of pyrethrum on the oil, then take away the cautery by its shape.
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing on the figure that you have drawn little by little several times, so that the key is burned in its proper place; and the signs of the work's health are that you see the paper retracted, and the hairs lift towards the point of the oil; then let your hand go, and leave it thus for III days, then put cotton moistened in butter until the cauterization is removed; after the treatment of ointment until he is healthy.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’ils soient grands et igaux, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la folle de mirte; puis pren de savon français et de viv chalz, de chacun une .Z., et broie ensemble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu'il ne refroide, puis en espant sur la forme que tu es fait comme la folle dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladies tient en l'oil seul, si doit on ouvrir en l', et se en ambedous aussi; et met desoz l'oil coton moilliet en abin de ufe; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton dois mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordiction ausi com de feu.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, if the medicine has come to your death.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the wound has passed, lift the limb up, and examine if it is raised just as it was before, whether by constraint of fire or by incision; and if so, it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If this is not so, then put again on the medicine to the limb or if the medicine has failed, until your work is equal and your eyes are fixed; then put on cotton soaked in butter until the wounds close, after applying a cure called "dyafenis" and others, until it heals.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if necessity requires that you guard yourself well on your work by great care, so that the wound does not occur again.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	If the papers become moist after, and the hairs prick in the oil, then resume the medicine on that person who has been made soft by the paper properly, as you have done before; after the cure until he is cured; and this is the form of the fire cauterization.
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of men are different in size and shape, and according to this be your constraints; and do not return to the straight path for one who has studied this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Of the cauterization treatment of a fistula.
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you cure a fistula as we have said in the divisions of diseases, and your treatments do not benefit him, then it is necessary to cauterize him according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to put his head on a clean cloth; and tie the meniscus of his head between your hands in that manner so it does not move nor do its chief; after putting a moistened cotton wool or persillen juice on the oil; after heating the cautery which is thus: and if you wish, it should be shaped like a pen nib, so that they are assembled as one; if you see, it will be pointed from one end to another; and if you see, it will be so too as an arrow; but however, this is what is shaped, worth seeing for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the abscess it is opened, and pulling out the pus, and drying it; and if it is closed, then let it heal, and pull out fire from the bowel; after putting on the hot cautery shaped like a pen nib, and keeping your hand to the cautery at the part of the neck so that you do not go mad; and put the cautery in the fat of the oil, and corrupting it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of cauterization just after the bone, it would be well.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, start again once more, and if you need it again, and leave it there for three days; after that, put cotton soaked in butter on it, and let the dressing desiccating until he is healed, and if forty days pass without being healed, then put on medicine with corrosive properties until the bone is uncovered; and follow according to what he comes into his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a way of cauterization for an abscess that none of the ancients mentioned.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Then open the abscess and drain it; after that put in the incision a thin thread so that there is this shape:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	Instruct the patient to take 1.3 pounds of horse dung; and hold your hand firmly over the affected area, so that the patient's wounds do not bleed while the dung is applied; it is necessary to put cotton wool soaked in vinegar or oil on the wound: the dung will treat the fistula, and the healthy person through marvelous cleanliness.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have said, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If this is not the case, it is necessary to administer pus into the wound and return the fistula to its proper place in the body as is suitable for each individual.
des crevaices en levres	of fissures in lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Often fissures occur in the lips that are called "poils", and likewise in children's lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these crevices of what we have said in divisions, and the cure does not benefit, then apply a small cautery surgical according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And fix it immediately in those crevices until the juice comes out; after treatment, apply a poultice of ceruse until it is cleansed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess on the throat.
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes in the root of the throat or in the vein, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, after it becomes purulent and rotten and dries up and forms a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in divisions, but it does not benefit: then it is necessary that you apply a cautery according to the size of the fistula; after the removal of the fistula or pus, hold your hand until the iron nail goes into the bone, and observe where the vein is. And do so once or twice, after treating as we have said in treatments, until it is cleansed; and if cured so, this is good; and if not, then it is necessary to discover the vein and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in your chapter.
dou movement des dens	A dislocation occurs of any joint from its place
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you cure it with medicines and it doesn't work, then put the patient's head on a clean cloth; after take the fire cautery which comes from there afterwards in some way so that you put a chain on the tooth; and put it inside the cautery hot hot iron, hold it with your hand until the malady feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; after let go your hand and resume the cautery according to your will; after fill the patient's mouth with clean saltwater, and make him spit for an hour and rich fires.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in some way, the teeth which were moving are fixed, and the gums are restrained, and the moistures corrupted are dried.
de la dolor des dens	Of pain of teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When pain of teeth comes from cold or ice, if the medicines are ineffective, then it is necessary to have cutting according to two manners: and there are two kinds of cauterization: one with butter and one with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cauterization with butter is done thus: if you press butter from the fat, and put the end of it in a iron or horn spoon; then take cotton and wrap it around the point of a tent, and the pus in butter boils, and put on the painful tooth quickly and hold until it cools down; and so do frequently until its virtue comes to the root of the tooth, and if you see that milk-like substance and cotton in butter melt, and put on the painful tooth, and put iron hot on top of the tooth until the heat reaches the tip of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	The fire cautery is assembled with a chain of iron or wire, and it should be heavy enough that the heat does not come to the patient's mouth. After heating the cautery, perhaps its shape will appear afterwards, and put it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery cools down; do this often, because the pain will be removed on the same day or the next day.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is fitting that the patient fills their mouth with good butter in the haste of applying this cautery, and then takes hold of it: and this is the shape of the cautery.
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make the cautery to whatever head you want, and according to your power; and this is the shape of the chain:
des scrophules	of tumors.
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the swellings are from moisture and cold, and do not obey digestion by medicines, then take fire cautery, following this after it happens, for this comes next. Take two openings for the fumes to come out with the fire cautery of the other side; and put the cautery hot on the abscess once, or until its size is, so that it comes to a head of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, put cautery according to the quantity of the abscess, and leave it thus for three days; and cover with moistened cotton wool in butter until the swelling is opened.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the cauldron
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When the moistures conquer on the channels of the blood-forming [organ], and when this comes from cold complexion, then it is necessary that the patient be evacuated first by medicines soluble; after take fire cautery at the root of the throat, and guard that you do not come to just there at the throat, but rather beware of burning the wound with little heat.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the fire cautery, instruct the patient to perform another cautery on the joint of the neck at the head of the spine, and those who are called "clavile" because we have a shape before; and cure the patient as we have said so long as they be healthy.
de la toust	of the throat.
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all and disease of the groin are caused by cold moisture, and the patient has no fever nor sweating, and it is an old illness, cut two cauteries on the tonsils in their mouths; and another cautery between the two testicles; and those who are called "clavile" according to the shape which is said before.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see, perform a cautery by pricking all the cauterized area which is called "poins" because the form is as before in the illness of the ears; and prick the poins to the depth of 30 or more, whenever.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After the treatment according to what has been said, and if the cautery is applied at three points according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And because that way the cautery is lighter, because you do three of them at once.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder joint.
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	After, lift the patient on their back and on their side; after, relieve the wound that is inside the swelling, with your left hand only; and if the joint is dislocated inward, apply the cautery to the two inner points as this form.
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	Instruct the patient to cauterize his heart as long as it is pierced with an arrow on the right side, and four cauterizations will come together; for that is made by cauterizing with the cauterizing instrument having three nerves, because of the shape of the cauterization figures are these cauterizations; and the nerve according to the subtlety of a tent and this is the form of the cautery which has three nerves:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And sometimes, you press against this nerve because it is with eight cauterizations.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After placing the cauterizing instrument with pearl broth on it; after making the patient rest, and not letting the limbs be moved for a long time until they are well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if they dislocate again, little things happen then; afterwards, make cauterization on the thick cauterizing knife, or many cauterizations in a point.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joints are closed up, and the moisture is removed and the patients are made healthy.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When there is frost in the stomach and much moisture so that they extract it to its condition, and many cathartics are multiplied upon him, and all the usual treatments do not benefit him, then it is necessary that the patient be put on his back, and extend his legs and hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	From this, after the third cauterization I is performed under the spoon of the fish in a quantity equal to two doves, at all the cauterization knife, and the second cauterization is done on the other two sides so that the figure of the cauterizations forms three angles, and there is an interval between one and another equal to the space where they will gather pus; and the cauterizations be made so that they bleed the two parts of the vein, and the figures of the cauterizations according to this form until they come close together.
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	If you cautery with a great cautery in the stomach according to this form; and if someone has fear of this cautery, then cautery by pricking and sign above the stomach at the point according to how much you see there of 'enche'; then cautery all the cautery that is called 'poins'.
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the treatment we have had before, until it is cured.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	As for the liver, when it suffers from heat and moisture and great ventosity, until it is returned to its natural disposition through purging; and the patients are cured of that which we have mentioned in divisions, but they do not profit from it, unless the patient lies on his back; signifying 3 cauteries according to this form and figure and quantity on the liver, excluding the hypochonders, at the top or at the cost of the spleen comes; and leave space between each cautery the growth of a doe; and be the cauteries long on the body, and not press hard at all the cautery; and only burn the moist parts of the touch; and let the patient lie right on his feet; and if he cannot, then sit up straight, extend his legs, and lift his arms; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	If you wish to, cauterize these cauteries with the cutlery, if you are subtle and wise in the art, and beware that you do not burn your skin entirely, for you would dry out the whole body; and if it were to boil suddenly, because the blood is very sensitive near the spot, and your knowledge allows you to see.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When it has an abscess in the liver, and you see whether it is in the flesh of the liver or on the membrane: if it is in the flesh, the patient feels a pain that is not very strong; and if it is on the membrane, he feels a severe and piercing pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And when this cure requires the application of poultices, it is advisable that the patient be propped up on his head; then apply the poultice to where the abscess is, and then apply the cauterized thing which resembles the bone, because this is the shape.
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	Instruct the patient to burn with fire as long as the hairs are dry, and it comes into that sphac, until the pricking is completely burned; after the cure according to the cure of the wounds so long as they are healed; and it is not advisable to use any fires from this cautery except by one who has studied for a long time in the art of medicine, and whose hands have cured these diseases some times.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	And so it can be done with great courage, and I think it's more valuable to leave it.
dou cautere de pleuresin	How to treat peritonitis
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that for peritonitis you should perform cauterizations of aristeia roots, and in this way: take an aristeia root as long as you can find, the largest one, dry it, and make it as big and long as your elbows; and pour olive oil on it, then heat it up and do a cautery between the navel and the neck, and two more in descending order from below the chin; one between the fifth rib and sixth, leaning back from a little; one at the hips, and one above the stomach, and one between two shoulders, and two on each side of the hip with the cautery between two shoulders; and do not press hard with your hand, but make it open as if you were smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And they said that no old man uses cautery of fire like the razor, and the cauterizing tool, and puts it between the ribs, until it comes to the affected area; and it sears the pain, just as we have said in the apothecary of the stomach.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear or the patients die now, or a fistula comes that cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the abscess.
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the abscess as we have said about the divisions of the treatments, and it does not profit at all, then they mention three kinds of cautery that are all good.
