Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Of which one is that you do three cauterizations, or four, in the same manner as linking according to the length of the abscess, according to the figure of the cautery of the stomach that we have said before; and do not press your hand at all during the cautery, and let the patient lie on his back; and another way of cautery is that you cauterize the cautery with two nails, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the wound which is right over the abscess, or if the wound comes from the left side, do so according to the wound, according to the length of the body, and the cauterizations be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	After the fires have burned for two periods of time, and you perceive the colors to be clear on the other side, then take fire to the cautery, and so on for four times; and if you see it, cauterize all the cautery to three times.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the treatment when it has been exposed to rot for long times, and this applies to those who have already received other treatments said before.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cautery is not effective for dropsy, except when applied in the manner known as "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you treat it according to the methods we have said in divisions, and your cure does not profit, then it is necessary that you make four cauterizations inside the wound, and one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the muscle, and two behind the back on the spine, and one towards the rectum; and so should the cauterizations be placed close to the spot where the pain is felt.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After the fire cautery, let it be opened for a long time to show its putridity; and do not stop the cure of the patient after the cautery; for healing would hasten, and there will be two sorts of opinions with the help of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The form of the fire cutting for the belly is like an axe that we have shown before; and on the back it should be olive oil, as he has been put in before.
de l’enfleure des piez	of swelling of joints.
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the joints are swollen in one who is suffering from dropsy, and are filled with a citrine color, it is necessary to cauterize on the back of the foot between the auricle and the ankle; and lift your hand with the cautery so as not to turn.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deeply in this method, lest they suffer like the one who was burned by fire, and so should you use cauterization according to this form:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After thus cut the two legs twice, cauterize one at the point of the cutlery in each leg; and cauterize the long one in front of and behind it, inside the thigh; and let the cauterization stay for a long time to cure the wound. After the other cures that we have mentioned.
de la menoison	of the house.
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	When a solution of the belly comes from cold and moisture, so that the virtues retentive and digestive which is in the stomach and intestine are reduced, and cannot be cured with other remedies; and you see the patient suffering very much, if you do four cauterizations on the stomach according to what he spoke about it before or cauterization of the stomach, at the cauterization circle; and four cauterizations near the subtle bone beneath all cauterize the subtle needle, and two cauterizations above the joints.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	If you see the moistors abundant and the patient suffering, make fire cautery on the nail, and do fire cautery on each joint, and two cauteries on the stomach with the great one, because the cure is beneficial when it has good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	About the treatment of hemorrhoids.
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When hemorrhoids are at the base, or more than one, and have been old for a while, and are of thick, cold, moist humors that are corrupted, treat them as we have said in divisions, but if you do cauteries: three on the spine behind the back, where it is all towards the armpit, in triangular fashion, and one below the belly; and two beneath the buttocks. If you think his stomach is chilled, and his meat does not cook, and you see swelling of the face, then give him a cautery on the stomach, as has been said, and one more on the liver, and one more on the liver's opposite side with all the cautery; and leave it open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After a cure, the limb must be made sound again.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshiness which is named "theleul
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut the flesh (thelul), if it simulates a razor and then is set on fire, and leave it until the cautery comes to life at the birth of the vein, so that it does not dry; do this once or twice, and if there is much flesh (thelul) left, cauterize each one as we have said; after the cure with ointments, profit from them until they are sound, and if you cauterize a large cautery on the cartilage, it will have more aid.
de plaie mal curee	of badly treated wounds.
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot bear either a dressing or an opening, that is what we will tell in his case, if it comes to such a sickness that can only be cured by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When there is no fistula, and it has grown old and swollen with putrefaction and moist corruption, if you wish to prove the depth of the wound, and guard so as to know how far it goes.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After applying the cautery that seems like a razor, and pour it into the fistula according to the quantity that it has entered, and continue the cautery until the flesh and corruption are burned away once or twice, or three times, depending on the quantity of blood required; and beware not to burn the nerve which is in danger, and great veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the fistula is in the body of the testicle and in the intestine, so watch out for those things, and do not perform such operations only on a wooden chariot, and think they are not poisonous; after cure let them be watched until they are healthy, and if their testicles are swollen, and the materials are hardened long time, then know that the testicles are fully healed; and if the materials are not hardened, know that the testicles are rotten, and corrupted the bones at the foundation; and in this way as one of those which we will tell later in his own case.
de la maladie des reins	of kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain from cold comes to the kidneys, and great swelling, and does not take effect with a woman, then it is convenient that you make a cautery on both sides of the kidneys of one part and on the clavicle as we said before; and if the cautery opens in the middle, three cauterizations will be necessary in line, and more aid will be required.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is swollen and weak from injury and moisture, if the patient retains urine, then he cuts the bladder in the part where the hairs of the navel meet, both on the right and left, and cuts each as long as the distance between a thumb; and he cuts behind the back, wherever it may be needed; and so cut they like clavicle according to what was said before.
de la marris	of the marrow
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the marrow is cold and moist, and cannot conceive, and the flowers are corrupted and their ends are late; and when they come, it pains greatly: then it is fitting that one makes III cuts around the boil, just as we said for cauterizing the bladder, and II cuts behind the back; and so make the cuts like clavicle, as we said.
de la hainche	of the joint
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the moist viscous fluid descends to the cheekbone of the joint, and because of this it moves out of its place, and the signs are that the knee is longer than the other when measured together; and if you find the tendons loose in the departure from the area, then it is suitable to cauterize the patient on the cheekbone of the joint with a cautery similar to the circle, and point forward towards the joint so that the cheekbone is within the circle; and if the cautery is done such as those that we have cauterized the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not present, do three cauteries with the olive oil large, and let them be as deep as all the joints.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain of the groin
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain occurs in the groin, and it's caused by coldness and moisture, and those who are afflicted with this condition are cured according to what we have said about division, and the cure is not effective, because the disease is ancient: therefore, it is necessary to purge the patient of thick humors, or pills fetid, or other hard pills that resemble them.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After having made the fire cautery; and the manner of cautery is according to two ways: that is to say assembling hot medicines, and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cautery is according to many ways, of which some are such that you cauterize on the groin area; three cauteries are made triangularly according to this shape, and with great depth and width, and between each cautery there is space equal to the size of two fingers, and olive oil cautery; sometimes it is done in the middle of the head of the groin, because four times according to this shape:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	If you see that the fire cautery is applied to the cautery in a circle as we have previously mentioned in the dislocation of the hamstring; but do it in such a manner that the circle contains all the hamstring and all the spices on which it burns.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the manner in which one does it when applying the sciathe (a form of treatment), as the pain stays in the hamstring and cannot reach either the thigh or the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it comes down to the thigh and leg, he makes two fire cauteries on him where the patient says that the pain stays; one cautery above the ankle, both on the left side a little (and whether it is cut with a blade or burned by the spice), and if the patient feels that the pain extends beyond two feet or near a joint, he applies cauterization there where he feels the pain three times or four at the cautery which is called "poins".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	Instruct the master to do more if needed; and if he sees that the pain is below the kneecap towards the thigh, then do fire cautery with the curved or circular cutllet. And take good care in all your cauteries not to burn too much and cause nerves and great arteries, and so do not make the patient suffer more pain and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen others who did fire cautery on the ankle of the foot, and they burned so much that the leg was completely swollen, and the toes as well, and it became consumed and corrupted all the toes.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a stomach solution in which he died.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pains are in both legs together, do fire cautery in one and the other, according to this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	Instruct the sages in the fire cautery of the hazelnut as thus: Make this iron rod and it should be as large as our finger in breadth, or a little less, and let it pass between them with equal space, as the width of an almond; and let there be iron rods like these, two parts each, and they are to be like nuts, and it has one iron rod well made; and this is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it be heated so that it is completely red and pour out sesame oil, and then place it on top of the sick hazelnut's boar, and turn it on its healthy side; cut off once with the cautery and leave three days; then apply butter plaster and let the wound open long time; after the cure of ointment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we should use little of this cautery because of the fear of its burn, and if one sees little who uses it; and let us consider all these good cauteries which can suffer it, and where he is feared.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The cautery of medicine burns if you make an instrument between the crossroads, on which it descends down to the edge of the wound, and is either made of iron or of fire, with a length that is visible, and in the center there are two, and between each one is the quantity of the thickness of two shillings; and on top and below, and they join together as this form:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After applying the bough of hazel on the patient lying on his chest side, and pressing your hand very much on the bough of hazel; after putting between the two circles of the hot water which is heated in a little fire, and letting it rest for an hour and ten minutes, and suffering the patient the heat and the burning of it.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is found to be mordication just as from fire; and when the mordications do not pass, lift the hand with the instrument and raise the heel of flesh tenderly, and leave thus three days, and put butter so that what is black from the ash may be extracted; and let it remain three days until putrefaction begins; and this would be the rear aid after the treatment of limbs until he is sane.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain has spread just to the thigh or just to the leg, make an instrument that is similar to what you have made on the heel more frequently; and this is the way of hot flesh, and I have written it in treating of medical correction.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alum and vinegar alive, equal quantities of each, and grind them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	If the point of an arrow can enter through a small opening if not blocked, then put another pot on top well and heavy, and place acid and chalk and softness above, as much as you have two powders until you press it firmly to your hand; and leave it like that until it comes out acid and chice or pot lead. Then take all this away, and place chalk and acid there as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And if it is very hot and it has taken the form of work in medicine and cautery of other limbs because fire does all this, and other medicines from which one cauterizes well the vein like cauterizing with treacle and myrrh and chalk with soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And the Galen tells us of a cure in which one man was cured of the pain of the vein and sciatic pain, and great praise for it, and he says that there was no other cure needed, and he became whole once after this cure, and he bathed himself as he teaches it here afterwards.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	Instruct the patient to take a small dose of fresh and dry green herb and break it with a little bit of fat, and place it on the hinch and on the thigh or where the pain is, and bind; and then leave three hours, and by the quantity that the patient feels no more pain.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then put it into a bath until the body is slightly swollen, and put it into the bed, and the pain will go away entirely and be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And knows that no one should use cauterization with such medicines unless it is after the evacuation of blood.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dyascorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with horse-tail ligature, it will not hinder much; and in this manner must be made the cauterization.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take a linen cloth and anoint it with old oil, and place it on the fossa which is between the big toe and the small toe.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After taking dried cheese, and anointing it with fire until it becomes charcoal-like, and placing the linen on it, and letting it stay till it is stained; and repeating this so many times, and not stopping until you think that the pain has reached its peak, and the hurt is gone; for this manner of cautery is called "cautere de chievre".
de la dolor dou dos	of the great pain in the back.
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether by falling or by percussion, or by great evacuation, or because it seems like material is spread out cold, none of these symptoms are worth cauterizing, except for those who come from an infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	Instruct the patient to be void of fetid pills or other such things, placed on their back, where the pain resides, three lines signed of encaustic, and in each line V cauteries or more according to virtue and quantity that the patient can endure; and let the cautery be done as is called "poins"; and if you see, do III cauteries or IV according to the clavile pierced midway in this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This malady often comes in small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a straight line when they lift up, and fear; and you find in the lower spine on their back and in the appearance that comes above the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you see them being cured, if you cut him with the cautery of a cell according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the fire cautery affects each part of the spine equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see that when the fire cautery cuts into the spine at two or three points and the wounds are close together.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After treating the patient so that he is healthy again as we have said, and take care not to apply fire cautery in gangrene which has inflammation of nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	of pain from the joints.
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When pain from the joints is caused by moisture that spreads to each member of the body, and when pain comes from the foot, called "podagre" precisely, and when it is due to cold cause and medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured with cautery in this way: make a mound of cautery inside the joint on the foot, and apply olive oil in that shape:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if he has need to prick at the flesh of the foot, then let him perform fire cautery on all the cautery as we claim "a point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come just to the genitals and other joints, and this happens often, let him perform fire cautery on each knee three cauteries or four of each one part, all the olivary cautery; and if you have need of more, do more, but do not hold your hand in the fire longer than until the speculum is burnt.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend just to the knees and back, let him administer the cautery as we have said in this chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, let him prick into the flesh two lines; and if there remains no pain afterwards, he must prick each joint and the skin of the hand; and if pains come to the elbows or armpits, let him cauterize each part, and give good governance to the patient and prescribe medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	If you do good governance and purge the phlegm, so will you be cured by God.
de la routure dou syfac	from the cutting of the abscess
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When an abscess comes with pus, and the bowels descend into the veins and it is new, so if you want to cure his eyes, do not use it the next day; and use things that lighten his belly, so that the fever descends from his belly; after that make him lie on his back between your hands, and he commands that he should pull on his ankle until his boil is healed, and he takes it away with your hands, and signs to cut the abscess above the bone of his finger, and at a visible sign so that it appears like half a circle above the body; then take out the cautery as this form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	As long as they are white and senselessness.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then remove the swellings at their place; and the servants will tie a bandage around your hand so it does not return to its original state; and work well on the patient, putting cussels and servants above the knees, and another under the leg which ties up the hands; then put the cautery on the mark with all your might, and your right hand and your thumb until you strike the bone, and if you do not hit it the first time, so it recurs again in another place until you reach the bone; and be careful not to let the swelling escape while you make the cautery; lest you burn it; and that the patients may not die, or from some other evil.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not come to the bone with the cautery, your work is worthless.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	Instruct the cautery for children to be subtle according to their measure and the great men also as much as they are; after three days cure them with butter cautery until the wound is removed; after curing other ointments until they are cured, and lie down the sick man forty days on his back so that the wound is well closed; and it is necessary that their movements be relaxed long enough, so that the boils do not appear when he will get up to go into rooms.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wishes to rise up, and he binds him with a well-made bandage, and presses it for forty other days; and has good rest, so that he works little and guards against excessive drinking and eating, and too high breathing; and when he follows this teaching, then is completely cured.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say this after your operation on cutting with a cautery.
de la routure dou ventre	of the operation on the stomach
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When other operations come to the stomach and are known, and you see that they do not grow again, you will cut them according to their quantity, and burn one-third of their thickness; after the operation as we have said; and none of the ancients has said that it should be cauterized on three angles according to this shape:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first mark the size of the opening in the incision, and make a line for its width, and with your thumb press all around the cautery nail.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauteries are lighter and more gentle.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	Of old pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes to any limb, whether from a fall or an injury, and that pain persists for a long time, and the medicine cure is not helpful, then it is necessary to cauterize with the cautery called "poins", and do the cauteries according to the length of the limb and its smallness and weakness and its virtue and its location of twists and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If it is a saneness from the first cauterization, that is good; but if the name remains, repeat another cauterization on that part, because twice is the custom to do so in order for the member which is nearest to be cured, for this reason you should make the cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	Of clumsiness or ineptitude
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The problem is not helped by cautery for a great amount of time, and the disease itself that comes from the rotting of pus and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	You can see the cauterizer, take care to treat the disease if it's at its beginning, and cure it according to what we've said in division, and don't leave or stay there, and you doubt that corruption will infect the entire patient, so do cautery on the head: I cut the top of the head new, and the other towards the front at the end of the hair; and II on the two horns, and I behind under the ear; and let it be so long with your hand until the cauterizer comes to the bone, and until the scabs come out so much that the vapors of the big humors can get out; and cauterize on the mouse according to what it is before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And he knows that the more you do of cautery, the more it brings aid, and the patient benefits; and he knows that the sick person feels no pain from cautery as if they were still healthy, because their body is already completely corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	It is necessary that the cautery be large or small according to the members and joints, as you will find in various iron instruments.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After treating him with the lead of flour mixed with honey and other remedies until he is cured.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When an inflammation comes upon any member and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, and it does not heal, then you must perform cautery on the member according to its size and size of the part; and if the cautery enters a little into the affected area when inflamed, then treat him with ointments until he heals.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And never is cautery done with the hand and foot and back, to quiet the nerve that makes the member mute, and so if it is extracted the swelling; and none dare come near without knowing the limbs and the exit of the moving body.
de albaras	of wounds.
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "wounds" is old and the art of medicine is worthless, then cautery with a cautery stick, one point after another, according to the quantity of the pain in the wound, until the bleeding stops and the color changes; then treat with flour mixed with vinegar and lentils oil, and plantain leaves, and gall of colon and gall of alondre, each part separately; mix all together, tie it up with a bandage, and let them be for as long as they are healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment for the chancre by fire cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When the chancre first appears and you want to stop it from growing, if you burn it with fire cautery, around the entire circle of the chancre.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And the wise people said that you should also burn it at the center of the chancre; and I don't think this is a good thing, because I fear that it will cause ulcers and corruption, and I have never thought it would happen again; and there is no surer thing than being burnt around, with fire called "circule", as we have said in many cases of cautery.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the inflammation which cannot be killed
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When some people have a disease called "adubelati", which is slow to die from the inflammation it causes, or because of its abundance, or because the patient is old and decrepit (which means very old) with little blood or age, and you see it hastening to death: then burn around with many small cauteries in piercing; after that.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	It will happen to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierced with the cauterization at all, then this heat will be the form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand at the middle of that illness called "adubelati" until the cauterization pierces the vein, and so arrange the cauterization that the patient feels pain in that manner that the course of the putrefaction is delayed.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the treatment until it is completely healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	the cauterization with iron.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another kind of illness that is called "corrodens", and it's nothing but an infection of a member, because it corrupts the flesh just as fire burns.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this sickness in a person who can suffer fire cautery together, then make the fire cautery clavicle small and great, according to what it is needed for the patient or the disease; after cauterizing all parts until you remove all the corruption, and nothing remains, that which is corrupted must be cut out.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it for three days, and put on the patient's cauterized wounds so that they suffer bruising with oil until the scalded areas are cut out and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After this treatment, generated from the use of medicines.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after three days that no healthy child is born, it's good; and if not, then repeat the cauterization on those who remain corrupted.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this malady is sometimes cured with a medicinal drink in place of fire cautery; but all methods of fire cautery are more effective aid, and I have said the remedy for the medicinal drink in cutting: take what you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of porridge that comes from the bones
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times, from the bones due to lack of care, a disease called "closure" occurs according to our understanding, and it is a serious thing that causes great pain.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the fire cauteries for this disease are according to two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say, fire cautery and hot water cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cautery is that you shave the head like a pinhead as well as one hair from each side, and it should be made of good iron to the measure that it can penetrate all parts, and have subtle margins; after put it hot on the nail, and turn your hand around the nail until it becomes hot and swollen; then let it sit for three days so that it begins to rot; then make an emollient from sage leaves crushed with fat, and put the emollient over the whole nail, and let it stay overnight, and the nail will come loose and be dislodged from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the joint with puncture and care until it is clean.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are infected by the bodily humors, and many times it occurs in hands and feet, so it is advisable to apply hot cautery; and it is done thus: take a hollow tube of iron or wood, or a pen of vulture's beak, and place the nail and splint, that is, to cauterize warts; and put the tube on so that it pricks through all, then put a little cold water, and hold well your hand, and press your hand in turning so that the edge of the tube comes to the root of the nail, and can find the hot water deep down to the root; and let the patient suffer for an hour under the heat of the cauterized area.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	So let the hair grow after another, until you are searching all those who are in the body; then treat with ointments that inflame the flesh.
li cure dou trembler	the treatment of trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some people are trembling from cold or fever, or from another cause, if it pleases you, do four cauteries above the spine on the back, four below, one between each spine; and one more near the joints, and one near the stomach with an olive oil cautery; thus they will stop trembling, and hasten to recover from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of festering pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Never do they appear by chance on the body without baths or festering pustules, which come from gross, corrupted matter.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	It is fitting at first when they appear that we are making cautery on each head of the pustule: a subtle cautery of fust from myrtle, so that the point may be gripped by the fire, or from the root of arborolea long, or in the lenticular cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And at no time are the cauterized until they appear, following this manner, and they cannot increase in size forward, but the superficial things that come out are broken, and they recover; but it is fitting to do this after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the arteries are cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times, there are great bleedings of the artery that is cut at the wound that comes to the surface, or at the incision of the abscess, or at the cautery of the limb, and similar things; and it is a very grievous thing to smell.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	Instruct the patient if it happens to them at any time, so that they hasten to put their thumb on the wound of the vein, and stretch it very much so that the pain is not present again; then put more olive oil cauteries small and large until they are all red; then take one, either great or small according to the wound and let them see in which place the arteries run, and put the cautery on that vein where you hold your thumb, and hold it so that the pain does not remain.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	If the fire escapes when you lift your thumb over the vein, and the cauteries are extinguished, then take it hastily another of the cauteries that are on fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease doing this one after the other until it does not cause him to die from bleeding; and be careful that you do not burn the nerve that is near, and that no other harm comes to the patient; and know that when the bleeding will not stop without cutting the artery, it cannot be done well by oneself when the artery is large, unless it happens one of the four ways that we have said: either by cautery, or by extraction since it has not been treated, or by tying it very tightly with a thread, or by medicines placed on which have power to stop the bleeding; and so he will be bound and strained as a consequence.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will put on a restraint of tight binding with cloth or tying things tightly above, or other similar things, unless it does not benefit.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if it happens without any binding and he has no medicine present, he must put his two fingers on the vein wound as we have said, and well bandage so that they are bound down above the wound and above the vein; and he should not move him, but apply cold water frequently until he is frozen stiff and thickened, and thus do the incisions in front of what he needs to cauterize and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	This begins the second book on treatments of wounds.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	As we have said in the first chapter, about all diseases for which it is necessary to cauterize with fire, or apply medicines, plasters, and ointments, and the causes and forms of cauterization; and I have put that chapter in the head of this book, and I will go through this same route to find those things, because it is easier to find them by this way.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so that I begin this, it is necessary, dear child, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than with the first cautery, and therefore you must be more cautious.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you not to act foolishly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many kinds of people come in for treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	For those who have come to see them with such great severity in their sickness that they die quickly because of the harshness of their disease, and from the great danger of their malady; and for this one must be afraid.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And of those who tell you their meaning, and say: "Wait, I am cured"; and the sick person is deceiving.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not wise only to allow those who come to you who have this kind of treatment, but put more great caution in your honor than in your wealth, and do not be weakly but wisely from what you are certain, from what you have taken, and use prophecy and indication for the care of your sick; that will help you to achieve good reputation, glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Three dear children, Our Lords give you good understanding and integrity, and if you wish to aspire to the holy inspiration of His hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have ordered this chapter in the form of chapters, according to what is before or behind a cautery chapter, which I have devised for you from the head right down to the foot, because you will find it easier to know those things that you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	The full head is filled with water.
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Those who know that this sickness comes to the children often at birth, and when holding them too tightly strangles the child's head; and sometimes it happens because of a repeated cause that no one knows.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this sickness except in children, and among all those who I have seen it has caused the death; and therefore it seems to me that I must use this chapter for similar cases.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	In the child, because the shoulder joint is full of water, and the head becomes swollen every day until it cannot be supported; and the patient so feared that he was dead, and this moisture is assembled under the bone above the sinew, between the skin and the bone; and such wounds are made as if the moisture were between the skin and the bone, and the abscesses are small, which you need to cut open with an incision in the head a large one; and be just as long as two of us, so that the moisture runs out; and look at this form of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more crusted and the abscesses are larger, then make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and you see signs that the commissures of the head open on both sides, and the water spouts when you press with your hand into it, and it does not return: then it is fitting to make three incisions in the head in this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision extract all the moisture completely.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After holding the incisions of draperies and powders tight, and putting wine and oil on them, and letting it be so for five days; then loosing it, and curing the wound by applying poultices and ointments, and letting the head drain freely, and then serving dry meat to the patient in small amounts until the limb is comfortable and healthy.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you look at or open the size of the abscess and its assembly, because it is sometimes in front, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right, and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Therefore look at or open the abscess and its filling, and make a cut according to what you have the skill for; and be careful not to cover the artery; and seek a vein that is full of blood, if so that the patient may die from the evacuation of blood and moisture.
de reume	The head of the shoulder
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When it happens that a person suffers from a disease called "cataract" in the eyes or at the worst, and the patient is old, and medical treatment does not work, then the last resort is to cut with cautery using what they will cut off both arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is therefore necessary that when you cover the eyes, the patient makes a face towards his head; after he rubs it with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then extracts the patient's neck from all the cloth; then looks where the vein swells, and the veins are behind the ears, and do not return quickly; then binds the eyes tightly, then cuts one and both of them with a good spoon-like instrument in two parts, so that they touch until just to the bone, and this should be done by the width of his forehead.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	If you see, pour out the spatumile under the artery and cut on top, in the same way as it should be cut through.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, if its blood flows without any upward continuity of fire.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the arteries do not open with feeling, it is to be decided that you measure the size of the space three times as long as it should be, then cut from the bone; and since what is needed for the wound is six cubits, and by chance a little more or less, according to what the patient can bear, and the replenishment of the artery; then examine the wound: if the bone point remains above the syphac, and does not open with the knife, then strain the wound and tie it, and provide treatment with ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	Let goes
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When a head pain comes from old times, and cough is bad, because of moistness in the eyes and heat in the temples and an old forehead swelled up and similar things, if they are treated with medicines and all those cures don't help, then we extract the arteries from the temples and cauterize them, as we have told.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the way to extract them is that the patient makes his hair on his temples, and listens carefully at the artery which opens in the temple, because it opens well when beaten, and is not replenished with heat as in some men who are too cold; and if it is replenished, then strangle the patient's neck with some cloth, then rub him with some rough cloth, and cool him down with hot water until the artery appears clearly; then take out a spatula of the shape:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Instruct the patient to scrape the leather lightly until you reach the artery, then pull it up towards the head with needles, and separate well the threads that are under each of these parts; and if the artery is fine, turn the needle to the point of the pin, then cut from that part according to the size of two joints.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	But if it is not cut, do not jump at it without causing damage all over.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And pull out the vein of six fingers, just three at a time; and if the artery is large, it is wise to tie two ligatures with a strong double thread of silk, that no discharge comes in front of the wound's sound, and keeps coming from the vein; then cut the excess that lies between the two ligatures on the same hour, and if you see, then cauterize with cold cautery as long as the joints are cut; and this is the most effective work, if the patient has no fever and it belongs to a hot constitution.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the fire cautery is aid to finish the moisture: for this is he of greater aid than the moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Where it is necessary to extract the arteries, he fills him with his own blood, and puts on well-made bandages; and when they are removed, if you heal them with dry medicines that produce charcoal, and with bandages, until they are cured; and if without any cut of the artery, as you work, you are in danger of being burned by fire, or you have no vinegar to apply, then put vinegar on the wound so it does not freeze, and warm up the wound with cold water so that it is congealed, and tightened so that it suits; for what is more tender and lighter in extracting the artery is to cauterize the vein of this cautery by cutting two parts, but the cuts be well-spaced to last longer their heat.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instruments are too dark, they hold less their heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it must have two large nails, one in each hand, then when you apply heat to both, until they reach the bone, and cut the vein at two places; and let them be separated between the two fingers because there is no binding of this cauterizing from head to toe; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	from tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes are flowing down into the veins that are under the forehead bone and do not benefit from any medicine that we make, and you see the face of the sick person reddening, and feel the pain in his front as if it were a flame; and the oil is cold and moist so that the hairs of the scalp fall out, and burn the paper, and get scorched by the heat of the tears, if this cure must be done.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	Et the old people called him "cure contused", and you should make a retouch to the patient who has this disease the hairs on his head or front; then you do III cuts or front equally according to the length of the forehead; and let one of the cuts be as II do two, making a cut downwards from the nose to the chin, and the other II cuts cost each above the papers, and keep away from the incision of the arteries that are in those cost each above the papers; and hold your hand away from continuing II mandibles, and let each wound have III dollars through it; and take a piece of sponge and much cloth to soak up the blood, then apply good spatumile with II parts of the shape
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.
