And from the cut at the temple just above the second cut; scrape all the wound that is between II cuts to expose the syphach, which is on the bone, then make another part of the middle incision just above the other second, and then pull out that spatumile.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If you prick at the base of the hairs with the "cultellary" instrument, and it is sharp on one side and soft on the other, do not prick too deeply, and this is the form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the cutting edge towards the raw flesh at the puncture, and the soft part towards the bone, and let it stay until it comes to the middle cut.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut off the blood vessels that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous just as much as it opens at the puncture, and then make another cut in the middle until it reaches the other opening; and then extract the pus equally, press out the liquid from the wound; put a clean bandage of wool cloth in each cut, and place wet cloths soaked in wine and oil and ashes, and take care that no abscess forms again; and on the third day, untie the sutures, and administer many pints of fresh water to the patient; then apply the basilicon treatment with olive oil, and other treatments for wounds, until they are healed.
dou reume des eulz	Do not move your eyes.
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When a cough comes up with good habit, and you see the eyes clouded and small, and weak the sight, and burnt papery; and the hairs fall out, and the head hurts in the forehead, and the patient is troubled; then recognize by these accidents that such materials and this cough do not come but from many veins, and how much the mother heals it if it is so.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And instruct the patient to look at their forehead, then make a deep cut on either side of the forehead and another small cut.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And begin from the cut on the left temple to the right temple, and make the incision until the bone; and keep your hands away from the temples that move towards the side; when the bone is exposed, sooth your wounds with a sponge; then squeeze between the two lips of the wound and put cotton wool, linen cloth, and wet strips in wine and oil; be careful not to touch an abscess; once the bone is healed, it is suitable that you rub the bone until it starts to come out; then cure the things that make it inflamed, which make it worse.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	Take two parts of wheat flower and four parts of colocynth, and make it into a paste; and administer it to these wounds for the purpose of drawing out the gallbladder throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of ear stopping.
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into the ears is one of four things: dust, or animal matter, or a stone from the mine, or something similar as iron; or seed, like poppy seeds, beans, fumitory, or similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it falls into the ear, stone or some other thing that does not adhere to the ear or grow in the ear, if you put the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, then take a little bit of violet oil or wormwood oil, and apply it to the extraction; and let it make him sneeze. Then stuff the nostrils with cloth or wool, and put a piece over the ear.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Often comes force by this cure; and if it does not come, then they extract with subtle fingers, because this is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If they cut with fingers, it's good; if not, extract on the wart with subtle pinches; and if that doesn't work, make a ring of resin and put the head in the ring or ear canal very tightly, so that the blood can't enter through the ring with the needle; then pull out the blood, because often comes force like we said; and if it doesn't come in this way, take advantage of the fact that you get the hairs, and attach some device that has a point for that purpose, and put a little cotton around; then press the glue onto the bone or whatever thing is there, and pull out the blood.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she cannot escape all of those things that we have said, then hasten to cut the ear so that it does not sprout an abscess or vein and spasms; and the manner of cutting is such that you first make the patient healthy again from the head, and extract the blood according to its virtue, then place the patient between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut at the root of the ear towards the fat or what depends on it; and let the cut be as long as a moon, until you reach the bone, then pull out the bone according to your power, and suck it hastily into your mouth; and the cure will last until they are healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is grain that is swollen and inflamed, then administer extraction; and if it cannot be extracted, then apply a poultice made of subtle powder according to this shape:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make an incision from that spot.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not make the cut when you think the grain is moist from the moisture of the ear, until you have made many cuts; then extract with fine needles and like we said, so that the extraction be quick.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In water therefore it is said that one should spit into the ear and use sternutine of composites first, and fill the ear with thick cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And be careful on that same ear or in water.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	But if it bursts because of this, it's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If that does not happen, then pierce many times according to the length of your nose should you observe and be gentle, and apply heat to one part; and put one or two needles in your ear, and walk on both sides, and face another piece on the piece that is in the ear; and do not cease to make this of nail to nail until the water has all become still, and so it will burst completely; and if you see, pierce a joint, and burn one of the needles with fire, and the other pierces from head to toe until the most tender joint is burned; then repeat another part of joints until the water becomes still, as we have said in the needle.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the best, if it is of small body, like a worm and similar things, cure as we have said in division; but if it is of great body which can be felt, extract with pincers; and this is the lighter thing to remove that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	When extracting worms from the ear, while curing, do so as we have said in division and when treating distillations; but if the cure does not profit, it is to be observed that you look at the ear towards the sun: if no worms appear, take a fine needle; if none are found, then use a small iron pin; this is the form.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it may be narrow from below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And pour in the needle into the ear according to the quantity of the patient's pain, then suck until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	If they do not obey this, so that the pain enters through the cotton cane as I have said in the operation; and if it does not come out like we have said, administer dilutions such as the ancients have tried in the application of ointments, and you will find them or treat with dilutions; and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear with this instrument, because there is the form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And if it is silver or arsenic poured into the small passages, and above the overflows for distillation; and to press within the distillation instrument well-made of arsenic for this, and if you see a razor and push it towards the cotton thread as soon as it appears, then pour your oil or juice into it, and what you see of your medicines in the cotton, and let the cotton be in the ear; then put the razor into all the cotton, and press your hand at the right time until the oil is distilled or almost out of the ear; and feel that the patient is within, for if the distillations are made with a fire as well as when they are in the ear, and guard so that they do not become too cold, because the medicine would be quite bad.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the rupture of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without some perforation in the ears; and this same thing happens to adults by rupture of a wound or a piece of bone inside the ear; and these perforations come from within the ear if one cannot see it; and sometimes they are quite deep, and do not show themselves until later, and then one can see that there is a hole.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore the one that comes from within and cannot be seen is due to the inflammation in many places, and in this case it is wise to put the ear of the sick person towards the sun; and look inside: if you see the opilation (a whitish appearance) immediately, then this is probably caused by a blood clot.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let the eyes and ears be opened before and behind all surfaces, if they are not pierced in the ear; if the incision is made on bone or flesh of the ear, if you have fine fingers, and cut lightly, until that bony part is completely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the incision goes all the way into the ear, take a fine razor and light it over a small fire, then put it on the bone of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the incision where the patient feels great pain in the ear, cut lightly and keep from irritating the nerves of the ear; then put into the ear a tent according to its size and puncture with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this on any day until the wound is healed, or you take a tent and rosewater ointment, and powder with vitriol crushed; and if you see the ear swollen, coat it so that you smear and move another tent moistened in rosin made of oil and wax, until the swelling is removed; then cure as long as he is sane.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if it comes out of blood, plunge an sponge into cold water and wrap it around the ear, and apply other treatments to remove the blood that are in treating hemorrhages.
de la char des papieres	of the fat of paper.
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This applies to the eyelids when they become moist and dry again, so you must stretch them with tweezers and pincers, and cut off its roots with a small spatula; then put vinegar on it.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if not cut off, so that the cautery is applied to the lenticular part with great subtlety, and cuts after the incision makes no sense; and it must be repeated many times, so that nothing remains of its roots; and when those roots are cauterized by fire, they will be burned and never return.
de la gresle	of the flesh
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Often come in the eyes papers some things that resemble flesh in shape and hardness, and because of this disease is called "grandine", which is a great mass of moisture in the paper above and below; the wounds are such: take care if the grandine moves from one side to another, it's a light thing to know. Do then make them thick, then scrape off gently from each part, then take them with pincers, and strike.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cover it with striking the paper, so that there is no pain to the patient; and if the wound is large, if the assembly has a seam, and treat until it heals; and if it's small, do not make any force, for the ligaments restore it at once and cause the inflammation to cease.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	Et se li grandine is falling down inside the ear towards the upper part, so take paper and push it, and let the dust settle at one spot, and press and squeeze from both sides; and if the paper is pushed away by the incision, nothing will hurt; and when the dust is pressed, wash the oil of salted water, and cure the ear until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	from the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Then there is a grease that is tied in the webs of paper above, and this has happened to many children with no one to care for them, and it causes great pain to their eyes, and they come with cataracts in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because tears are pouring onto their eyelids; and therefore they lie down on their faces always, and sleep there, and their papers above their eyebrows are moist that the inflammation has uncovered which appears in the oil.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the lock of meat with your hands and feel the swelling between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the way of applying this is that the patient puts his head in your care; and then take a linen cloth, and prepare a tent shape with it according to the quantity of swelling between each part; and put it on; and press with your hands from one side and the other so that the swelling is assembled at the center of the circle; then make an incision at the midpoint of the swelling near the vein's cut, not larger than the wound you make in the vein; and sew tight enough until you reach the swelling; and in various positions, the swelling comes out through the incision according to the shape of a white fatty piece.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Extract the bandage to its entirety as a single piece of charmed cloth between your two shoulders; and turn your hand so that it is spread out both on your right and left side; and be careful not to add anything to the wound, lest you come to all the splintered blood at least up to the oil, lest you bleed.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the edges do not open at the beginning of the wound, then tie a little piece of cloth on it so that it appears; then extract as we have said, then bind with bandages in easy and clean manner, and put the linen on, and secure with a belt.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who crush wool and put it on to corrupt the moisture that is left behind.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the physician, so as to be healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it comes to a joint with abscesses hot, so the cure of splinters satisfying as long as he is healthy.
des poilz des papieres	of hairs from paper.
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	As hairs from paper are born, not in their natural state, and are infected, so they annoy the eyes, and cause various types of diseases such as excessive tearing and swelling of the papers and albugen, to the point that it's a cause of destruction of the eyes; and there is treatment according to four ways: either by cauterizing with fire, or with medicine cold, according to what is in front of or the chapter of cautery, and done either by incision and stitching or by tying, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you put the head of the patient on your healthy one; then turn the paper with oil from your left hand; if it's converted, it's good; if not, then prick an arrow at all the thread above; and either cut along the edge of the paper or where the hairs are growing near them, and take out the thread, and place over the paper a small cloth of cotton and fabric, then sew on the paper a figure of engravings, like the handle of myrtle wood, and whatever quantity you see to lift the paper that is divided into all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	Et if to one who has need be applied a great quantity of paper according to the condition of the paper being moistened; then make at all the surface of the skin below the two lines that you have signed off on, and beginning with a large lance just as it is small; and let one of the incisions near the natural hairs in the size of a finger root, then pour the liquid on one of the two angles of cut, then scorch everything; then assemble the two lips to a stitching of a needle with all the fine thread of wool, and squeeze the wound, and dry the excess on the two eyebrows as in any sticky thing, if you have seen this done; and if not, do not bother, then leave the stitching and the thread just for three days or four; then treat the wound with stitched bandages of dried and constricting things, because the paper relives at the moment of the wound and its assembly, but the stitch is weak (as they have said the ancients), and this is a work with fear.
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then cut off whatever is standing above with equal force according to its shape.
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the tongs, and it is not even, then prick an arrow or take a thread of some kind, and sew to the figure; and sew another thread through the large limb, and the second through the small one, and assemble the threads evenly between your two hands; then lift your hand evenly, and cover up all the skin where you have stitched, as we have told, then assemble the two lips of the wound by suture, and cure until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, then soothe it with cerote and similar ointment soothing; but sometimes happens that the hair of the scalp are converted: so you should use what we have said about the incision; but the suture in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of the neck is according to this form: and it is that you convert the paper and the flesh inside according to what I have said, and then make II joints by art, and II subtle ligatures as long as the paper and the broadening of the spanilla are; and cut as II heads of II parts wherever you hold the fillets; then assemble one and the other subtly on that which is surmounted by the paper of oil, and strain the II joints from the II parts together; and leave it in this way for some days, and the strained neck will die and decay and wither and turn to rot, as it chills by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is late and you cut with some force, then the cure until he becomes healthy; and when the wound is sewn up and if the paper rises, and no longer will the hair be pulled back; this is the form of the two joints that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	Et if the arrow is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, then you should treat the arrow at the lower part, all along the thread that you have ordered, until the arrow has fallen through the holes above and you see it by the sight of oil; then so treat the arrow and the thread, and close the oil and let it close II days or III, until the hair grows in its place and comes out a char above; and if the hairs are small, then follow one long hair from the cheek nature, and lift them up with that one or another where you leave them, till they are elongated and then put them down.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the oil's spoilage
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this sickness that is called "aleacrati" or when the spoilage comes into the oil, there are two kinds: one natural and another unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And happens suddenly from a wound, or cutting, or cautery, and by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the way of dealing with the wound is that you cut through the adhesive, and open up the lips, and put in linen tents, and tie them so long as they are healthy; and it should not be done in the treatment of wounds of things that dry and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	Because if you do this, the disease will return worse than before; but if you work on softening things, like fenugreek; and boil rose hips in water or oil, and put a cooked seed of flax or melted tallow into any of these ointments, and wrap it up in a cloth, then cure this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the great treasure of your cure is that you guard it so that it does not become like what it was before; and this work which we have said about does not burn with a fire greater than its original form, but returns according to its former form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the blood which comes into the oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This illness that is below, truly called "axacrati", and is a natural and accidental condition.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from a wound and a tear, and cutting and similar things; and the vein of the work in that part is such that you prick an arrow, having one double thread, and the stitch in the blood, and make it pierce on the left side, so much that the thread emerges in two joints of the blood; then pull up the blood to above all the needle, and cut off with one span wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the paper returns according to what it ought, that's good; but if not, take a razor and put it in the tear, and turn the paper, and make two tears on one side inside the paper; and let the joints of the two tears be on the two angles of the incision you made; and let it be so that when they are assembled, the figure will be as the figure of a letter called "I griesche"; then take away that blood, according to the quantity of its sides below, from what suits the paper, then add both parts torn, and the cost of one thread of linen; then cure him as we have said about medicines for mollifying, and bandages, until he is cured.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	Et if the sickness comes from cutting or sewing or cautery, so it is fitting that you cut a plain incision under the hairs of the paper skin, and according to what I have said; then sew between the two fingers of an iron rod, as I have said; and one must perform the work according to the form of the sickness, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters take away all possible means to make its figure return to its natural shape; and the sick themselves, according to what they need from incision and treatment, and many other dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	Suddenly of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	As soon as this suturing has occurred in the hand in a certain manner that the paper above is soaked with white oil, and cannot move or do its natural work, then it is fitting that you cut the tip of a razor under the paper, and lift it up; and let the stent be placed according to the shape of the thing that is applied to the spatumile subtle, which should not be too sharp nor too rough, so that the patient may not suffer from too sharpness or oil staining; and make your incision, scraping off that assembled part, lightly, so that the paper revives according to its natural form; and it heals all that assembled part, and is never done with salty oil, and poured with sweet water, and vinegar; then put a linen tent between the paper and the oil, and place the oil-soaked lye on top of it; and after three days use the collier and other soothing things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	Of fire cautery
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	It is said that the cut is in two ways: it is nervous and seems to be so thin as if it's made of leather, and another which is not nervous but seems like frozen flesh covered with frost, when one touches it with iron and considers its appearance, it does not come out; and both of these seem to converge towards the great vein, and grow little by little until they cover the entire eye and all the light and movement of the oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of the incision is that the patient places his head on the bed, then opens his eyes; and lifts the sheet to one's hand, then cuts the cut like little stitches, and exposes it above; then takes an awl, and puts a horsehair, or a wool, or a beef tendon, into it, strong thread; and doubles the point of the awl a little and punctures the cut all along the awl, and ties the cut with a thread and exposes it above, and scrapes off to the length of the cut the skin along the root of the cut, so that it brings forth the blood and hair to the root, just up to the head, then cuts off the remaining part in the direction of the vein, to the small distance, and leaves nature intact or the vein, if the cutting does not bring forth the blood accustomed to it; and sometimes only stanches the cut with a sole thread, and on the thread, as we have said; then scrapes it all smooth because this is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient to let the spatumile [scraping tool] not touch the charnel skin and break it, and that the prunelle [small needle or lancet] be perceived; and after making the incision apply a little broken silk in oil to the wound, and make the collar made of litargire [a medicinal ointment], and leave it until the next day; then have the cure treat it as he thinks necessary so that the patient may recover.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the inguinal [groin] is not tense and you cannot force the needle, and the incision cannot penetrate, this condition of an inguinal lump is often cured with medicines; and it brings forth similar swellings as I have described in division; and if you see it cover up, apply oil to the patient, and take the scraping tool light and soft according to this form.
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	Instruct the patient to let the hair grow over the wound subtlety, and if you see it does not shrink at all and the reason presses, distill from your mouth onto the oil collar made from litargire and red gall, and pour, and sooth the oil just on the other day; then resume the other operation in the same way as this one, until the whole surface is bald.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If there is no objection to the oil, as with an abscess, then apply the medicine and let the pus, and cure the abscess first until it is healed; then resume the operation in the same way as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	If the appearance of the skin with the wound night in the oil causes great discomfort, and if it is suspected to have become infected, then cut a portion off not entirely, so that no more blood flows; then distill into the red oil collar made from litargire.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the fire that is born on the eyelid
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	For some men there is no fire at birth on the eyelid, covering the eyelid and holding it against the paper and the torn skin without any mark, and it seems like a rose bud; if the patient puts his head on the healthy one, then he opens the eyes, and with all those fires convenient to him, and holds them tight; first he makes the fire by cutting, and then goes to the sharp knife until the end, and be careful not to prick the eye at the injury; and when the incision is done and cut out all the fire, apply oil of silk broken or distilled cologne red and similar corrosive medicines, and put it on top of the oil with cotton wrapped in linen cloth, so that he may be sure of the abscess; and if it stays nothing, and the wound does not heal, then leave the oil and cure the abscess with soothing remedies; then return to his injury until it is healed, and do so for each fire cut into the oil by this resemblance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But it is necessary that you lighten the treatment of each weak person along their natural way and along the accidental way, in the work with iron; and do not put your hand in any of these treatments until you see that this member suffers from the treatment.
des voines des eulz	of the eyes.
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	These eyes are red veins that are covered on the surface of the eye, and they tolerate their treatment on the eye and weaken them every day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	The art is therefore that you first look at the eye to see whether it is swollen, and if so, and there is no other fire-disease except the swelling; then the treatment in this way: instruct the patient to put his head on a clean sheet, then suspend those veins for as long as possible according to his wisdom, and let the subtle veins double in that form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let them be two times one by degree in the form of a circle:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then coil around those veins subtly, and apply the blood hourly after another, until you see remove those veins from the oil; and beware not to prick the oil with the points of the scalpel, and do this operation at noon in front of the sun, and be very hot in your operation so that you only squeeze out those veins; and when you have done this, then distill vinegar green and red into the oil to corrupt what remains in the body.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are unable to coil all of them in that one hour, then apply plaster on the oil with soothing things for the pain of the eyes, and let it rest for some days until the pains are soothed and you can be sure that there is an abscess hot; then resume according to this manner until it is healed.
de la fistule de l’oil	Of the boil of the oil
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The sore which they call "arissati" boil: when you cure it with cautery and medicine hot according to what I have said, and it is not healed, then there must be an infection in it that you cut open above the abscess, where or if it should die, and drain all the moisture that is in it, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed and you see the corruption and darkness, if the abscess has completely opened up, and it is in that form; then they call "aspere chief" or hard head, and make it from fine iron to fit into the hollow of the present head, and pierce it as sharp as a lime so that it is in that shape.
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place on it the new bone of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two hands, and press your hand as tightly as you can until you feel that that corruption has dried; and do this only once, then restore to its proper use with restorative medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the head of the shoulder is soldered and charred by fire, and the flesh of the bowel is soldered, and remains thus for forty days, and it does not renew itself and is not incised, no more accidents happen to him, he thinks that he is healed; if this is not so, there is nothing else to do but to return the fistula to the perforated wound according to this form: and you must uncover again from the bone for the second time with iron, and with medicines sharp, when it is uncovered like this, and take a bow of iron at three angles, and make the fistulas smaller just up to the head as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place him on the bone of the shoulder, and remove your hand from his flesh for a little while, then turn to the whole forest until you pierce the bone and feel that the patient is coming to this if he holds his hand above his navel; and put back the dried medicines according to what I have taught you, as I have said; when his char becomes flesh and hardens the shoulder, the material comes to the navel; it is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	From the issue of oil
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are open all around, and they do not come to clear out the brain, nor calm down, if it is necessary to treat the patient; then apply ointment, then put in ventouses or hatterel to prick with iron for to release, then put on the oil, which is made of ice and aloe and incense and sarcocolle, and then strain the oil, and apply plaster over bandages and cloths; and the way of the cloths is that you take soft cloths, double each one in four, and then put one on top of the other according to the quantity that the eyes have need of; then strain it from above with a hard bandage, and reapply ventouses to prick with iron for release; then remove the ventouses and leave the oil straining day and night, and if it is applied moist, so much the better, if not; then reapply the plaster and cloths and the ointment and the ventouses until they are healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Discharge of the pupil
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a disruption comes to the pupil, then it opens and is filled with paper-like material as if from grains of resin, and one is amazed to see; therefore, if you cover your eyes, such work is done that you pierce an arrow into the root of the part above just below this; then you pierce another arrow in the middle of the eye; pierce it, and let the first needle remain as per the arrangement; then cut off the double thread from the side of the eyelid; tie a bandage around one part of the eye with a circular shape of cloth, so that it remains closed until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is held back by the eye in each part of a circle of linen, so that it heals.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes show great appearance, then pierce at the spot just under the eyebrow where the oil comes forth from, and drive away moisture that is white and yellowish, and let the eye go in so quickly; then take it out as soon as it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the oil of the bowels
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease called "alcunnati" is not like burns from the oil of the bowels that are pouring down, but it's not really a burn; and as for its appearance, it's such that you should sit the patient upright on the bed straight, then take the head between your hands, two parts at a time, and let the bowel come up to your eyes; then put it in its place, don't let it descend or break apart, let the light appear, and see how things are for the patient as they usually are; and if it doesn't descend below, know that it's a burn, and when the bowel is coming down in a shape not like our previous experience, then you must do so.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you sit the patient between your hands, then take the fine spatula and make above the corneal surface as far as possible by continuing the conjunctiva with the corneal surface and the crown; and when it is done, distill in hot oil mixed with honey or fenugreek boiled with honey or fenugreek.
des aigues de l’oil	of hot oil
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	As we have seen similar signs in the division, and that which it is necessary to pierce. if this is done according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you sit the patient between your hands, cross, with fires of light by the sun; then take hot oil and put it tightly on. Then take a piece of paper to your left hand if your eyes are on the right, or to your right hand if they are on the left. Then take in your right hand, if your eyes are on the left, the instrument called "almagda", or on your left hand, if they are on the right; then put the point of the instrument between the crown by the size of a thread in that blenchor of the oil at the lower part of the lesser larmier. Then push the instrument with force and turn your hand until it pierces into the blenchor of the oil, and feel when "almagda" comes to the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the path of "almagda" be to the full length of the measure of the space between the pit and the end of the black spot; and this is the crown of the oil. If you see the bone in that paper for the clarity of the corneal surface, then put the instrument just below where the aloe is, then press with two strokes after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the fever has come down now, so he sees the patient in front of him and the instrument on his table.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting for a little while, and the fever rises again the second time, put the force with the instrument, and when it is stuck and does not rise, gently pull it along with twisting of hand a little by little; and then take off some small silk cloth and clean up that oil inside.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put in place the oil-soaked cloth or a moist linen soaked in rose oil and plenty of rue, and tie it with pure oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Also, and those of our time, let us use a common broth with plenty of rue.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the powder cannot be inserted into the oil because of its hardness, since there are many men with very hard eyes, so you should take up the instrument called "alberit", for it is in the shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	Instruct the patient to prick the conjunctiva only, and do not go too deep, but make it subtle, then give them milk, just as we said; and when the work is completed, the surgeon will come up to the patient, who will be lying on his back in the dark room; and you must keep all movements, and give light meals, and do not move his head or arm or leg, and tie him according to his disposition every three days; then release him from that same dark room, and examine his sight, and show him some things, and then put the bandage on seven days later; and it is not wise to do this in the heat of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary to lighten this, because the water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	For the abscess, if it is coming to a head, you must cut away the oil on the seventh day, and the remedy for purging an abscess; and when it is appeased, you must cut the eye and put on its face with an ointment to cover any day, so that it does not return to that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then it will be in the house a little at a time, and it will change into its case; you know that no disciples should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Ibera region, and he told me that in some other land they used to perform an alchemy operation that caused them to drink the water, but I never saw or read anything about it in our territory, nor did I find it mentioned in the books of the ancients; and by chance, this might be a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the signs of the forms of alum, because those who do not know them see only in vain; and they are made of pure arsenic:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And the head of arsenic from this same subtlety, and the lower parts are in threefold angle.
de la char sor le neis	From charcoal on the nails.
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	They are never born or found in charcoal in diverse forms, because some of them seem like scorpions by the size, and if they have charcoal covered with red or purple color, and soot from black bone.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In which case of these soot-like things that are not covered with charcoal, it is necessary to place the patient between your hands against the sun; and open his nostrils, and sprinkle over those chars, and strike out the fumes; for it is as long as you can sustain this subtle powder on one part until you know that these soot-like things are entirely burnt.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any thing that cannot be covered, so when the wound is completely clean and free of subtlety, if it does not stay; and without falling asleep, or incising the feet, cut as it requires; and if it is malignant abscesses, then hasten and cauterize until they are drained and all the bones are extracted, then let it rest in wine or broth, hot or cold.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the fever does not break and moisture comes just to the throat, say it is sane; and if moisture enters sharply as it requires, say there is a charnel (dead) bone in the bone above, because the humors do not come to cut: then it is necessary to put a thread of flax a little thick, and soaked with hands, and between each one some space should be left; and apply the patient's fingers covered with the thread to the neck at the slightest movement, and repeatedly do this as we have done children in schools, and it is a light thing for him who wants to make it happen. Then hold the head that comes by the thread with one hand, and the other head that comes by the mouth with the other hand, and examine one after the other in so doing as we are with the flax.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Instruct him to do this: as he knows that no one has corrupted the flesh of the child, then take the child, clean the wound, and anoint it with Egyptian balm, and place it directly under the head so as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointments corrode all that remains of the flesh; and then put a bandage of linen some days at a time until he is healed, and if he needs dried medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purify the head, with which one distills oils and medicines in the balm:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be of silver or iron, resembling a lamp cover, like a bandage, and lead it thus; and if you see this, make a bandage close to it, and let the instruments be so prepared to purify the head; take one cloth over the head to hold it while warming the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the shoulder bone on the neck
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Often the head of the neck develops a disease called "telul", and it grows and becomes large abscesses, until one is visible to look at; and therefore you must apply the cauterization or hot medicine to the bone, as soon as possible; and if you delay applying it for too long, so that it is large, then take care of it with the cure of colorpowder, because it has a hard skin, and if you touch it with iron, it is an enchantment, because when one cuts into it once, there comes great evil to the patient; and if the abscess is soft, not colored powder, and you see whether it can be entirely covered, then empty the patient and apply the same treatment, but without fear, and treat the abscess with hot things and restraining it.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nails are struck and scratched
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Knowing that when many solutions continue to come into one of these old cartilages, little profit is obtained in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore necessary to consider this in all cases, if the wound is fresh with blood throughout; and then add two stitches to a strap, then treat the patient until he is healed; and if the lips are deviated from one side and the other, it is necessary to burn all the parts of their skin until they heal, then reattach the two lips to a strap, and tie them up, and powder with powdered dragon's blood and incense crushed; and put on the powders a piece of emplastrum of strong or another emplastrum sealing, and leave it till it sticks to him, then treat with ointment until he is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The way of sewing is that you assemble the suture: either with needles, as we have said in the suturing of the belly; or with thread, as I have told you before.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses on the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	With the fingers inside the lips there is an abscess similar to grains of millet, small and large ones, therefore it is necessary that you return the lips, and break out each one, and take with pincers and strike in each part; then apply the lead after the incision of vitriol, until the abscess is stained, and then wash away the pus, and cure the wound with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh around the gums
