Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	When many times the gum rises up with the jaw joined, as they call it 'albulus'; then you should hold it between your fingers, and strike at its root, and let the blood flow out or the wound; then put on the patient vitriol broken, or other powder restraining and drying; and if that one returns after the incision, and happens many times, as the second time, and cauterizes: if it does not return again after the cautery; and this are the forms of oozings to cover.
des sordens	from sounds
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Never are the teeth assembled at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs that are ugly and painful; and never is a black tooth and citron-colored tooth with pus, until corruption comes to the gum, and the tooth rots; if you should sit the patient between your hands, and make sure their teeth are in order, and remove the scabs when they appear, as long as nothing else appears; and do the same for blackness and green, yellow and other colors, until they turn white; and if it is at the first attempt, good; but if not, then reapply on the second day and the third, until you have removed all of them; and know that each tooth has need of different forms of oozings to be cured, according to what the work shows, for the one who removes the teeth which do not come out easily between the gums have other forms than those who remove them from outside the gums; and these forms and others are with you prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth from its pain that you wait as long as you can before giving it treatment, because this should not be done late. Because this is a very high substance just now therefore we have no excuse to delay further.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore when the patient is constrained to treat it, if you wish to be certain of the tooth's swelling.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the pain of the patient is believed to be from the tooth, and it is treated as if it were a good tooth; and one should not depart from this treatment until the bad tooth is removed, because we have seen it before among those doctors. And when you are certain about the swelling of the tooth, it is fitting that you burn around the tooth with an iron instrument very strongly to protect the gums all around; then grind the teeth on your two thumbs or fine scissors at first and a little bit, until they are thoroughly cleaned; then bind well the fingers of the patient; and tie one's own hand tight so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the right tooth directly into the broken place, and if it does not spring forward, take out any of these instruments and put them inside each part lightly, and move him as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the teeth are pierced and pulled out, it is fitting that you fill them with cloth, in either place where they were broken; and if you carefully bind them with thin ties, so that they do not break when binding; and it is much wise to cover over the gum for to dislodge the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be well guarded that you do not break it, and keep one part remaining, and tell the patient again by the malice of the root for greater pains from the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	Be well guarded that you do not make it as the ignorant masters do, who by their haste and boldness break the cartilage every time, and never bring back what we have told you; but sometimes bring forth some other thing due to the oozing of this great disease through the roots that remain, or because they break the cartilage, just as we have often wished; and when the tooth is weak, wash the root with wine or aise, or salt; and if bleeding occurs, which happens frequently, then apply the leaden instrument.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of ulcers, when one must let them sleep first, are long pointed and broad branches, which do not double up when you pull the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And are broad branches so that they do not fold up when pulled; and are made of good iron well-made, and are pointed to hold the tooth.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root stays in place after being pulled, you should apply a piece of cloth soaked in butter on the patient.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	Until the patient's skin is swollen, because you put on the tongs called "algefri", which seem to be like a surgeon's hook; and are made just as sharp as a file, and this is the shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out from all these ties, so it is fitting that you uncover the entire chariot around the root, and put in the instrument which is called "althali", that is to say, a lancet, for this is its form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And so it is good or great, if it does not break, and if the root jumps at that, it's good; but if this is not the case, then aid with all the instruments, for then the forms will come afterwards:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you help yourself with this instrument that has two blades, for this is its form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are in front of the reason of the teeth, and of this instrument which seems like great pincers, for this is its form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	In case the instrument does not break and you know that many instruments of bone are used; and also other instruments which are not known to us; and the wise masters cleverly devise his own instrument, according to what his works and diseases show, for there are some diseases where the ancient did not teach any instrument because of the diversity of these things and since it breaks on the bone or on another part, if you seek out the instruments which are needed, as I have told you, and assist with gestures, because this is the form.
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	Let them be large and well-held to hold the bone securely, but not so tightly that it cannot be grasped or removed; and then restore him with the appropriate medicines, for if he has putrefaction in the bone and it is small, you may take out this instrument.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not at all according to their natural form, and the shape is ugly, and even in young girls so it is necessary that you know whether the teeth are newly come after the tooth, and it's not in its proper place, and one cannot eat or brush: then take the file; and if it is stuck with the tooth, take this instrument which is like to this small beak, and is made of iron with good quality and shape.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the file is held in hand for a few days to soften the hardness of the tooth, and because one does not move the other teeth, and if it appears that we can fix it, take a small amount of lime as much like this shape.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is just as the lime is used to make needles; and in lime the tooth is held for a few days lightly in hand so that it does not move much until it sticks; then the surface smooths out at the end, and if the teeth are too sharp and bite the tongue, it is necessary to file the roughness so that they are even, so that it does not bite the tongue or corrupt the words.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth are loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the teeth are loose, either by percussion or by falling, and if the patient cannot press on them because they hurt, and you treat them with medicines that restrain, then it does not help; but if they must be restrained with a thread of gold, because threads of silver turn green and rot, but gold never moves; and if the threads are too thin or too thick, according to the space between the teeth; and if you see that the teeth are crooked, take out the thread and put it between the two healthy teeth, if there is one or more loose ones, until you carefully guide the tooth towards the healthy tooth on the other side; then resume covering where you started, and subtilly and cautiously move your hand, so that it does not move at all; and be careful to tie near the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Instruct the patient to cut the nails with a pair of tongs and assemble them, and put them between healthy teeth, so that they do not irritate the tongue; and then leave it tight until as much as possible can remain, and if they come loose, or the thread breaks, take another thread to restrain it; this way, it will serve for the duration of its stay, and this is how you make the shape of the nails and the appearance of the two healthy teeth, and the two diseased ones, just as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, put it back in its place, fresh as before, just like we said; and do not get involved with anyone who is not wise and knowledgeable, for you will make the shape of a tooth made of bone ivory, and put it back where the defective one is, and restrain it so that we have said; and let it stay there and serve in this way for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the joint of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Never is the joint that comes from below the tongue or due to nature, so it occurs; or through an accident of a wound that closes; and the injury is such that you work on the mouth of the patient, with his head in your safe hand, and you lift the tongue; then cut the nervous cord around the large one, until the tongue is loosened from its place, and if there is hardness or noth, and it's sudden from a wound, so pour oil into the vein and cut around the large joint; and beware that the incision is not too deep by the artery which is below; and when you have done this, lift him to hot water and ashes, or cold water, then put under the tongue a linen cloth; and tie each wound each night, so that the swelling does not happen.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	If they bleed from the wound, put vinegar on the wound and break it with vitriol; and if they do not bleed, cauterize them with cautery that is good for this purpose, then give another treatment until they are healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see the pus of a fistula whether it is yellow or black or hard, and if the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, because it is a chancre; and if it inclines to form a blister, and there is moisture, put on a poultice and remove it from one part and another; and if they do not bleed at your work, put vitriol on the wound until it is stained, then return to your work until all is done; then lift the limb gently and carefully, and give another treatment until they are healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	The swelling of the throat.
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	There are no time there in the throat called "godath", and they are properly called "amandres", and when you cure them, as we have said in the division, if they are not cured, beware: if it is a hard swelling of little sense and flesh color, do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch them with iron, for the evacuation of blood; but let them remain as long as they are dead, and then you will cut them out, lest they burst on their own; and if they are of pale color and have subtle roots, then prepare a tool to cover it, but first examine whether the swelling is cold and has subsided.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and his joints be at ease, and he open his mouth and have the squire press the instrument between his hands, and push the tongue under with all the tool, for this is the form; and it should be made of silver or gold as subtle as ours cut.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can you press the tongue at all this instrument, and see the abscess, if take one and insert the needle into the grape, and pull forth above what can be seen; and do not draw anything on the cloths with it, then cut at the tool, for this is the form that seems like a force; and look well at the head which are curved, and one in another place, and are very good, and made of iron or honey.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, then use a pair of tongs, because that is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And so cut one side and the other side; and when you have cut one of the almonds, cut the other in the same manner, and after making the incision gargle the patient with hot water and cold water, and cold and cool water, until blood comes out, if they are cooked with pomegranate rinds or myrtle flowers, and similar things, until the wound is closed; then continue treatment until the patient is healed, but once more, when there are other abscesses in the throat besides the two almonds, cut them like the two almonds, that is to say, tie them together.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was nestled deep in the throat, namely, the small abscess; and I had tied down her whole throat so tightly that she could not breathe through the constricted passage, nor eat or drink, and if she remained like that for just one day or two, she would be dead.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscesses are standing so high that they have been filled with two rains through the two entrances of the nose.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I had therefore to do it soon, and I stitched one of the incisions, then the fire was applied, and a great portion of flint; then another incision was made in the other nostril, and the mouth was closed, and the tongue was pressed; after that, an incision was made in these abscesses, and a part of it was cut off, and only a little blood came out; and thus I cauterized the conduct of the throat for the woman, and now she began to drink water and wine, and did not stop until I had cut into that abscess for a long time; and the abscess kept growing again, and filled up the cavity that I had cleaned, until it became very large; therefore I removed it and cauterized inside the throat: thus it remained silent and stopped growing; and then I departed from those parts, and God be the judge of what happened after me.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When it is pulled down to the eye, and it is lifted up and it is long, if it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is very large and rounded, then it is called an "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cut as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit at all, and you see that the abscesses are eased, and it is subtle; so it seems wise to copy it; and the one that is rounded and does not extend, should be freed from the incision.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	Because there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its blanching and length, you must sit the patient in front of the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument which we remembered here before; then poke the needle into the eye, and draw it out below, and cut at two of the instruments that I mentioned in the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	It is necessary that you not cover more than the natural flow which is over the term; because if you do so, it grieves your voice, and your tongue, and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and cure until she is healthy.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patients have fear of cutting, it is necessary that you use an engine to cauterize the fearful senses.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of cauterization is cool water.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient places his head on your healthy one, and then he presses the tongue onto the instrument that we have said about cauterization, and fixes it with cool vinegar cloth, if it is not too thick or too clear; and with the handle of this instrument, which is this form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient to let a hair or an eyebrow fall so that a medic can apply medicine with a spoon, and place the instrument on top of it. So that the slobber and mucus run from their mouth into the medicine inside, so that they do not spill onto the neck, and into the wound; then hold your hand over the medicine and press down on the top of it for the half quantity of an hour, until you see a change and the biting of the medicine is calmed. And if you see this, take cotton and wipe up any instrument, and soak the cotton in the medicine, and pour the instrument into the canal above, so that the cotton gets on top of the nose; do this often, until the cautery is complete, then let it dry, and cast off after four days or five. And if you have need to renew the cautery with medicine, do this, and after the cautery, wipe clean under the nose with butter, and purify that which is around of the medicine; and drink cold water, and cure yourself of gargles until you are sane.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cautery. If it is treated with fumigation in this manner, take camomile and rue and origanum and ysope and calamant and avronne and similar herbs, and put any one of them in a pot, and add to it and make boil; and the pots should be well sealed with strong earth, and use an instrument like a head according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be of silver or lead, and put one of the bones in the mouth of the sick person until the vapor rises up through the nose by the force of the vomit, until the eye is numbed; after that, resume often until the eye dries, and make sure you do not do this at the beginning of the advent of the abscess, for many things happen; and do not do it only when the abscess has turned yellow.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	If the fire cautery instrument is not present, take a knife and put it in the chief's mouth a piece of iron; so that the patient's mouth does not get too sore; because the piece of iron does not weigh down the vapor much, and this is a good cure for salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Sometimes it is said that the neck swells with a piece of wood or an arrowfish; if so, then therefore you should treat as you see fit, and press the tongue on the sun until you see the thing; and if something does not appear and returns to the throat, it is best to make the patient vomit in order to cook the meat in his stomach; by chance, if it burns the arrowfish with vomiting, or if the patient swallows a piece of sponge, a piece of leather, a root of lettuce, or a dry piece of bread; and tie a string to the sponge, and then cut through it; and when it comes out, it will be swollen, and then you can pull it; and if it does not come out as we have said, take an instrument of the type that follows this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	Instruct the patient to let his limbs bend so that they can more easily enter into the throat, and raise his head to have it higher; and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, lest all his life come out, or push the bone inside with force; and move swiftly until the instrument is clean, for this will prevent its sharpness from causing harm; if he pushes it in too quickly, or takes it out slowly without using it evenly, so that the entire instrument is balanced, until it becomes smooth.
de la sansue de la gorge	about the cutting of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Never is the throat cut when I said so in division, by the cure of medicines; and if it does not benefit at all, then look into the patient's throat to see if the sun has struck, and press the tongue against the instrument that I have told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the wound open, then when there is just one small incision, or with fine tongs that are worth it.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this is not worth it, take a small hairpin, and push it into the throat of the sick person, then pour or give some warmth to the body.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient is afflicted with fever every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take the whole glass of cold water, and open the mouth, and let it flow into his throat, and move it with your hand often; and as soon as the wound feels the fever, vomit.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not vomit as we have said, then perfume the sick person with asafoetida, at the instrument I mentioned for the inhalation of the nose; do this many times, because it will bring relief.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, and the manner of fumigation is that you take a vessel with charcoal or black stones, and place it in the middle, and in that pit are the keys of the instrument; then put the patient's head into the cage, close the mouth, so that the smoke does not escape, but comes just there; and the cough will now come, and if it does not, repeat the fumigation many times; and let the patient suffer from thirst, and eat salty things, and do not drink water; and thus the patient is saved by this government.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument to treat an abscess is that when you can see it, resembling a curved pair of pliers for screws to enter into the throat; and has the appearance of a beak, and has roughness like lime, so that what takes it cannot be loosened; and thus it looks:
li chapistres des apostemes	The surgeons of the abscesses.
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many abscesses resemble each other, according to what is remembered from one and the other in this book, and differ in perforation and size; and there are two manners of them, one being similar to the other, and it is because they hold moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for those that are within them or in their body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	because the abscesses in the head are different from those in the cheekbone, and the abscesses of the shoulder are different from those in the joints, and each has its judgment in the book.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And there are abscesses to which one should not pierce, until the bowels have dried out according to their completion; and there are those of whom it is necessary to pierce when they are believed to be dying, and do not die according to their completion, just like abscesses that are near the joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	When an abscess comes from between the joints, and it is left until it is putrid in the meantime, by chance if the tissue and nerve of the joint have decayed, because that is the reason for the contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Where the abscess is between the main limb, and if you wait until it has died, if it harms the main limb; or if it is between the foundation, if you pierce so that it dies; and it should not be that you pierce an abscess because one believes digestion to have been completed, fire, since the one that is between the foundation will rot within, and a fistula will form, and cannot heal for a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the size of the opening of the abscess perforation which is dead according to completion, and this is when the pain is eased, and the departures of fever, and the diminishment of pain and redness, and the tenderness and the aggravation of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and it should be necessary that you make a seat for the perforation in a place more dependent on the abscess, and where it opens up; and let the perforation be long or short according to the body's length; and if the abscesses are between hands or feet, joints or nerves and arteries, and equal places where there is no pain.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	When the limbs are swollen, by some cause of inflammation.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in the groin, if it needs to be let out, leave the perforation open until the inflammation is completely resolved, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it in front of that, the vein will be damaged by the infection from it, and will become filled with a large amount of filth; and perhaps the lips and the inside of it will harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if an abscess is pierced according to the size of the body, according to what the limb has need.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is fitting to treat small abscesses with small punctures, small perforations; and large abscesses with large perforations, and many openings according to the resemblance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is fitting to make a cut, and cover; when they become as loose as a cloth, and have softened, then it is fitting to do so as we do for boils: and if there are those that are split into three angles, and those whose perforation is like the honeycomb of bees; and if there are those where one makes an oblong cut, and others cuts in different sizes and shapes, similarly.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who do not have a head, as an abscess is soft and superficial, it is necessary to pierce them completely; and when the abscess is large and has collected great pus, and you pierce it, if you don't take all the pus out in that hour, but only take a part, then stop the wound the day after, then take no more of anything on top of it; do this many times, so that the whole pus comes out; and at the same time, if the patient is weak in virtue, or an old woman, or a young child, or decrepit old man.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	But if you expect that the patient will be saved every time with the outcome of the pus, then you will not be disappointed.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then beware of this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced the abscess, if it has led to a wound, and examine whether the wound from the abscess is small; and if it's a clean cut, then apply tents made of linen or old cotton; and if there are big abscesses, and many ulcers, then it is necessary that you put one tent in each so that they come into contact with each other; and if you have pierced the skin near the abscess, and you've bound it tightly, then fill it with old cloth or a woolen dressing soaked with moisture, and bind it on the next day; then apply ointments until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if you come from blood, bring anointing with cool and clear water and cold oil, and wrap it around the limb covering it many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the blood persists, bring a government and a cure, and the powders that I have in my hands in this book, and if it is now winter, and the limbs are swollen with pus, so if you must put on bandages and cover them moist with wine and hot oil; and if it's still, and the limb is charred, then it is advisable to place moist bandages of water and oil, or wine and hot oil, every third day, as we have said; and then remove the abscess and clean it and cure it, as seems fit, until it is well.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this is what you must know universally in the treatment of abscesses: or if you have said how to proceed before the treatment of abscesses, and see here the chapter.
des soros	of sorrows.
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where small abscesses come from the head, and are like threads, just as a spider's web, or like the wool of a goat, there is also much resemblance.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are fat ones and threads where there is moisture, just like pullets (young chickens); and there are also those that are hard and stone-like to cut, and there is no doubt about it unless the artery makes it worse.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the marks on the neck are such that if you know how to use all the instruments called "entremoissoires", because of their shape they come after, what kind of thing it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then they do it on top of the long one.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is empty, then they scorch it without leaving any of that moisture on, because it returns again when you leave nothing; then they dip cotton in ointment Egyptian, if it's present; otherwise, in water and cloth, and apply the wound, and let it be until the next day; and those who stay through the night will come out.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then, as before, the cotton is reapplied, the second day, and the wound, until you know well that it will not stay through the night; then treat the wound with ointment suitable to its condition, until it heals.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscesses hold out firmly, then they cut according to this shape, on top of the long one; and you remove the hair, and scorch from all parts, and apply all your treatment to heal the wound where it lies; and if the arteries cause a counter-attack, then do as I have told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And do also thus with the abscess if it is pus-filled, and to cut it open and to cure as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the size of the pus-filled abscess will be cut and drained if it is lighter, because there is little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if some of these abscesses or heads do not have any moisture, and such future abscesses that I copied from the head of an old woman; and found the abscess to be as hard as a stone, rough and white, and could not break; and if one had ever heated him with fire, then it would have been better to make a wound like a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses that come or heads, wherever these which come to the head of children and roots of the ears, cut them open to the fullest extent, until the bowels emerge; and treat as it is appropriate.
des scrophules	Des scrophules
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times abscesses occur in the neck, and under the armpits, and near the liver, and sometimes they appear in other places or at the joints, and are very painful, and often joined together one with another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly in its own chest cavity, just as the swelling and abscess at the neck, as we have said; and the symptoms of these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are those that contain moisture, and those that are malignant, and they do not wish to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In that one then, where you see a person with good disposition in the fingers, and is similar to the color of the flesh, and is mute from every part, and is not rough around the neck or near the artery or the vein, and is not deep; it is fitting that you copy it up, and scrape off every part, and let the two lips turn red like onyx, if you have need to do so, as we said in abscesses of the neck; and take small pieces, and be sure that you don't scrape the nerve or the vein, nor make sharp turns, lest your hands fail, and see too far ahead, that you do not copy more than what you should.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	If you prick the vein or artery, and it does not stop bleeding, put vitriol on the wound, or any powder that stops the blood, and tie up the wound; and let it be so long as the abscess is healed, and the pain subsides, and start to dry out.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the pain is gone, it returns to its place, so long as you complete it; then seek for your right index finger to see if there are any small swellings, if they cut and burst.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	But if there is a great vein swelling at the root of the scrophule, it is not advisable to cut that scrophule at its root, but tie it with two strong threads and let it drop down quietly, without causing harm; then apply the wound with wool soaked in Egyptian ointment, and cure.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	If you cover the whole cranium, it is advisable to assemble the two lips of the wound and now sew them, before any swelling remains from the great size of the skull.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	if it is advisable to treat at the root of the, and apply force, and sew as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those craniums that have swelling, pierce at the spot where it is open; and pierce as was said before, depending on the situation, then apply poultices with ointment and similar things, so that what remains of corruption is destroyed; and when the wound is well cleaned, apply poultice ointment until it is cured.
de squinance	of inflammation
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancient people spoke and said about the cutting of the throat's shape; but I never saw anyone in our land who did it, and this is their writing.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those who have ulcers, it is necessary to cure the cut in the throat called "epiglote"; and do not give aid for this reason, because all veins and small parts of the patient are at risk with an ulcerous wound in the mouth, or in the throat, or on both sides.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the sickness is in the channel of the small part, it is necessary to cover the epiglote to escape the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is therefore necessary, when we want to cut the epiglote, that we cut it beneath three circles or four one small cut through and across, between the two circles or according to the size of the cut in the syphus, not in the cartilage; and thus it is convenient to section the epiglote so that there is no sharp edge, and the bone is long without hurt.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	Instruct the masters to extend the skin of the neck to its entire length, then cut it as long as it comes up to the chin; and remove the warts of blood, if you see any, and then strike at the root, just like we have said; and demonstrate it by cutting a section from the gland of the chin which is torn apart by the broken limb, and by the failure of the voice; and leave the wound covered with one piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed for which one doubts strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound on the root, and remove all flesh to the cartilage; then administer medicines that produce sweat until he is sane.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	But it should not be done until the throat is completely frozen, and the patient is judged to be dead, and the disease spreads.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then take care of the throat because the patient cannot raise it, and he breathes through the wound, and so is kept from death; and for this the ancients ordered to leave the wound open until the malady has passed, and it has passed after three days or four; and then they commanded to sew the wound and cure, until it was cured; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young girl took out her knife and stuck it in her throat, and cut some of the fatty flesh there; and I was called to cure her, and I found her just as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound, and I found the blood that had come out of it, and I realized that she hadn’t cut her vein or any other vein by chance only through the throat, and the blood came out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I have hesitated and sewn the wound, and healed it so that it was healthy; and it did not happen to the young girl that she would be red of voice, and return after her condition; therefore I say that in the cutting of the epiglottis there is no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat.
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called a "hernia of the throat", and it is a large abscess in the colour of a jay's, and it is very common in women; and it comes in two kinds: natural and accidental; where the natural one has no swelling.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental one is in two kinds: for one it is like fat tissue, and the other like an abscess that comes from an artery; and there is fear, and it should not be touched with fire except in small children, where it is proved and searched all around the interior: if you find it so as fat tissue, and have no reason to worry, then cut it as we do, and pull it out at its entire root, unless it has none; and search well, and cure it as needed, until it is completely healthy.
des nous	From us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many sorts of us, from which I will tell you all the similarities; and it is necessary that I say all the difference between one thing and another.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that inflammation is when and fever remains, as long as the evaporation has not been completed, and until it is resolved into pus; then the fever and heat are cured.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With no sign or indication of heat, fever, or pain, it contains the sycotic (fleas), which are its own sac and have a color like that of the flesh, beginning as if in a vessel, and becoming large; and they vary according to resemblance, or hardness, or moisture, and being very much like what I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of no one, that you examine and inquire first about all the instrument called "entremoissoire", as its form will arise or chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the way to inquire about abscesses as I do is that you grasp or take more moist than what you find in the abscess, and turn your hands little by little, until you know when the instrument has pierced the vein, then so it will be according to the size of the abscess; then pull out the "entremoissoire", and be careful not to burst.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If the abscess is cut open, as if its color were, so that you do as I have said with other abscesses; and if after opening the "entromissoire" there does not come more moist, know that it is greasy, then make a cross on it, because it will heal; take hold of it with pincers, and lightly scrape off each part and beware to cut out where you are treating it so that it heals well with the nose.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if it stays still, it will return to its place many times; and if it stays for a short while without causing any harm, apply the wound with some corrosive powders sharp and hold it steady with things soothing to the abscess, and cure other wounds until it is healed; and if it hurts greatly, cut off both cheeks of the wound, and cure that which causes the inflammation.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein bursts against him or causes another thing to happen while he is hasty, and you apply the lead of vitriol broken, let it sit for two or three days, until the wound has started to heal, and rests from the swelling of blood; then return to covering that which was left out.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Behold the forms of the interstitial strumae, which are three in kind: large and small and tiny; and among them there are three quarters called "albaret" and one called "breb", and they come in three kinds: great, medium, and small to enclose fistulas; and are also like needles used to sew stitches, made of citrine thread, iron, or silver, which turn yellow, and are more effective at filling the dark black hole for encasing the corbuses of fistula; and come in three kinds: large, medium, and tiny, according to the width of the perforation.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of ulcers are many in resemblance, as you see here: great, medium, and small; and if they have two lobes in three manners also; and if they have three lobes, and are in three manners; and if they have two lobes, and a single lobe only, and are in three manners; all this is necessary in its place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The chief of these wounds are caused by cuts, and of such kinds as there is one that does not cut through just one part, but rather scorches the surface, because that is why you do not cut into the vein or nerve; and of these incisions are the abscesses returned in handkerchiefs, so that the patient does not lose them when opening the abscess; they come in three manners: great, small, and medium, as you see; and one should use no more force than in the joints, such as knees, arms, and nipples, and arrows, and similar joints; and at times another small instrument is made, resembling scorched fingers, according to this form, because one stains the blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and put it in no place at all, for whoever has performed operations on the veins and arteries, and in no case returns to this great form.
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Never do the breasts of any men swell when they begin to be corrupted, until they resemble the breasts of a woman; and they remain swollen and inflamed, and whoever wishes to cure them must follow this form along this line from b to g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	then burns the fat, and applies a medicine paste made from burnt meat, then sews the two lips of the wound to the skin, and cures until it is healed; and if the nipple is swollen and tender, as in women, it is cut off in two places above, with two similar incisions; for one will cling to the other at the end of both, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from line b to g. Then burns the skin between the two lips, and removes the fat, and applies what we have said about dressing and powder, and what is necessary in the cure, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not fully made, because the patient does not want to rest, or for the deterioration of blood, then it is necessary to fill the wound with wet cotton cloth in a corrosive ointment; and leaves it until the remaining part and fat are consumed, then cures until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	Of abscesses from the arrows
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	Abscesses that come from under the arrows are hard swellings or have ribs, and when there is much moisture in them.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	These then that contain moisture should be cut according to this shape, from the line 5 to the line 8:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the entire bow that is in the abscess is empty, apply the wound with fine cloth, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cloth, and treat with ointment as much as necessary until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is like swellings of scrofula, treat it as we have said for cutting into swellings, and if the wound has an arrow sticking in it, apply cauterization as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	Of the cut of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is cut, and the skin is sewn up on top of it, if there are many abscesses, and this also happens when you pierce your vein; and if you feel pain in your two hands, you feel a strangulation; and when it's for the vein, you have to be careful not to appear; for it is foolish to cover up this abscess, and myself know that when it's under the armpits and around the necks and near the throat and in many other places, it is very great.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.
