It is therefore necessary to remove the iron cure, and the one with a head should also do so, and for the one with an artery swelling, cut above the skin on the long side; then sew the stomach as tightly as possible, and open the artery completely; then push a needle through under the skin, and pierce it to the other side, and tie the artery with two threads in two fingers, according to what I have taught you when extracting the two arteries in the temples; then keep the patient tied between the two strings of an assistant until he stops bleeding; then cure the wound by pressing, until he is healed; and if the abscess is near the vein's width, it is necessary that you tie your hand with the amount of the abscess all over the skin, then push a needle through the skin you are holding in your hand, and pierce it, and tie the two threads so that they go from one side to the other; then tie the abscess as I have told you, or tie the string of one of two parts on the two fingers of the head; and if you doubt that the threads will not be tied, then put another needle through all the thread under the entire abscess at the incision of the first needle, and tie the threads in four fingers; then cut the abscess until it reaches its end, then cut off its surplus, then cut off the excess with care and leave what is tied; then put on a soft cloth soaked in wine and oil, then continue curing wounds and ointments until he is healed.
des apostemes des ners	They are abscesses of the fingers
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	And abscesses come to the artery and vein, they come to the fingers when they are swollen, or by too much work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more often in the joints and in the toes when they are swollen, or because of too much work, and similar things. The abscess comes to the joint, its color is like the color of flesh, and it's prone to death; and when it's strained forcefully, the patient feels pain, and it's not so bad as for the body, but below the skin; and it hurts well from all parts, and does not go forward or backward, neither above nor below, and the one who is in joints should not be bandaged with iron: by chance it may cause contraction; and he who is on the head or forehead, cuts the skin with a lancet.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, if you have a pair of tongs, and cut them in its root; and if it is large, if you suspend it to the onychine, and skin, then scrape, and remove the bone and assemble the wound to the costure, and wait until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	of great boils hanging down.
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	There is no time for it to be in the belly and not in any other part of the body, and it is a disease that is called "fungus" by its resemblance to mushrooms, and has subtle roots, and large boils; and there are small ones and very large ones; I saw one man who had two bellies, which were just like fungi, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had fine roots, and were split open, and rotted away from moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	Inscribe these on the skin and you will find in one 18 ounces weighing, and in the other VI ounces, and the wounds from the incision are such that if you look, see whether the patient is moist, and the color of the armpit is pale and moist and has subtle roots; then cut the flesh with a sharp instrument, and be present in your presence when applying the cautery to the fire.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For at cutting comes many times too great bleeding of blood, and if you do not take care, then hasten to cauterize; and if you see the patient fearful and full of fear from the incision with iron, then tie a strong thread well-made, and fasten the armpit as we have said, and let it be two days; and then restrain, and cease to strain the thread until it cuts the armpit, and feel by it the work; and if the roots are large, then take fear to cut myself into the belly, but you can well cover half of it, then cauterize so that it does not come back; then cure the wound, and guard that you do not cauterize the thickened part which is red, poor in sense, and full of gall.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	It's an enchanted wound, and I came to this cure for chancres afterwards.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the boil is formed.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the boil comes from cauterizing a wound or a cut in the scrotum and is located on the abdomen and contains several boils, similar to other cases, or from blood that bursts from veins or arteries according to what is in front, or from vomiting; and if this is due to the cut through the scrotum and from the release of the boil, it has a color similar to that of the flesh, and is a light thing with pain, and opens to various issues.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is from the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when you press on both sides so it returns, and then comes back, and by chance, if it has scarred, and becomes larger at the entrance of the bath and for great effort.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	Et se c'est por moistor, c'est legiere chose, and open well when you press it with your hand, do not constrain; and if it's for blood, then open by these signs of large and hard apostemes, and fix according to a certain quantity; and if it's for windiness, so it is soft on the toucher, and wounds are such that you regard whether their appearance is for the blood of the artery, or vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If it's necessary to leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	Because there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter of apostemes for the artery and vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is for the intestine or the gallbladder, you should command the patient to let it descend and be stretched straight, then stitch around the whole wound; then command him to rest in your hands, then go toward the place that you have marked with the staff; then cut a quarter of the aposteme on top with all the necessary unguent; then tie it tightly around with a strong thread or a cord of strong silk firmly, and leave loose the tightening; then expose the quarter of the aposteme above the tie, and pour your balm on it, and quench the intestine; if you find the bowel tied up with the thread, remove it, and pour the intestine into the empty abdomen; and if you find the gallbladder, if you pierce the liver, then cut the excess flesh; and if the artery or vein contraindicates you, go well toward it, then return to your work and take two needles, and pour two strong threads, and pour the two needles into that which you made pierced previously; then strain the aposteme in four leus above the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and let the liver rest as long as it will allow, and cut off the dead flesh by itself; or pierce when it appears subtlely and becomes dry, then cure whatever is necessary for that, and stitch the aposteme as we have said; and extract the sanc or moisture that you find, then cure the patient of what he needs, and bind him with a bandage.
dou chancre	A skin sore
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have discussed the similar characteristics of a chancre, and how to treat it with medicines, and how not to use iron treatment; and we say that the chancre develops in the armpit, and great care must be taken for its cure; and they said that when chancre is on you or can be pulled out like chancre from the nipple, and in similar places, you should remove all of it when it starts to appear; and when they are large and old, it is not good to approach them, because I have never seen anyone cured by this method; nor has any one ever been cured before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the open sores, when they are on you or can be pulled out, as we have said, it is that you do not purify the sick person of black bile at all; then make him healthy if he has shown signs of overabundance, then make the patient well again by taking a good dose to make an open sore; then put your ointments or chancre on him, and wipe off the head from every part, and leave nothing but bone in every part; and let the wound heal completely, and expect that he will recover in good health, unless his flesh begins to rot at the incision of the artery or vein, so cauterize it until there is no more blood; then cure with another treatment until he is healed.
de ydropisie	Of dropsy (or edema).
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	For we have said in the division, the similarities of dropsy, and in what manner the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each similarity, and the cure which is made by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: if it is pierced with a single needle; and should not one touch with iron in these two similarities: this means tympanites and hyperostosis, because it's a mortal thing; therefore when you give medicine to this dropy similarity called "eclites" of medicines, and the cure does not benefit, examine whether the patient is weak, or if he has another disease than dropsy, such as constipation and belly pain and similar things; for we should not touch with iron, because there's doubt; and if you see a patient who is strong and healthy, and only has dropsy alone, and is neither too thin nor too old, then do thus: lift the patient up straight under your hands, and the assistants press the belly towards the lowest part of the feet, then take out a spatumile (a type of needle) according to this shape.
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let them pluck from two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	Cutting at a point and let it be not so enter that he can come just into the intestine when you insert it, and do not be able to stop it; then look if the drop of blood is gathered towards the intestines: if it is fitting that you cut in this place of the third part above the joint; and if the drop of blood is for liver disease, so should your cut be on the left side of the third part; and if it is for the stomach, so should it be on the right; and do not let the patient lie down over the wound where the superfluous fluid flows to the weak place; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and inject, and lift your hand at all the space between the skin and the sac as if you were scraping until the quantity of an angle or slightly inside; then pierce the sac so that the space comes to eight, and this is the drop of water, then take it out, and pour this instrument of which this shape is.
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	It is like a silver chain subtle, and it is made of iron or bronze light, and there is a small opening in the below part; and on one side, three openings; and two on the other side, and one on the other; and the nails are cut as a pen, and this is the form of the incision that scribes shape the pen:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue. If you are in doubt about the patient, and you give him a lot of medicine, so that the cure applies to his sepulture or fine sand, and after much sweating or bathing and by the sun, and if he drinks from a vessel, then the cure of medicines desiccative should make him healthy, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after extracting the medicine, just as I said before.

Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	There is never a child born without some kind of defect in the genitals, or if there are defects, they are small, or it is not in its proper place.

de la circoncision	About circumcision.
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a hindrance to healing like other wounds; all matter depends on our willingness and the will of the child, for it is proper to perform this work especially in children, as it is more necessary and less painful for their health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	The ancients did not speak of circumcision for their children, because they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired by experience.

de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already said in the division of stones and their extraction together with medicines; and I have said the difference between a stone embedded in flesh and in urine, and its signs, and where one must operate to cut it down; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that stones embedded in the bladder are found more often in children, and this is a sign that the stone has jumped out of the bladder like urine does in its subtlety; they open the incision, and scrape the patient's penis, and let them bleed many times, and then become inflamed; and with great frequency they form ulcers; and are lighter on healing in children until they are four years old, and are much more painful on elderly people, and are like those who are between puberty and old age; and the cure is easier for those who have large stones than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to treatment, it is necessary first to clean the patient with a cloth, in order to treat all the blood that has accumulated inside.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For this does not come up when seeking a stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the hands and feet, and bind them down so that the stone descends into the fontanelle, and falls down somewhere without coming up again; then seat him between your prepared hands, and his hands will be below his knees, so that the vessel is all sloping downwards; then seek out the stone and touch inside it; if you feel the stone in the space, now hasten to cut at the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not come out with the toucher down to its entirety, moisten your right index finger with oil from your left hand, whether the patient is sick or has your left side; and pour it into his fundament, and seek out the stone; and when you feel it in your right hand, apply it to the neck of the vessel; then press on with your right hand, and pour into the fault where you see cutting.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and he commands him to stretch out his right hand to the elbow joints in the upper part, and with his left hand to pull back the skin which is under the elbow joints in the part where they make the belly; then he puts on the speculum, taking care that it is the form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And they make the piece that is between the elbow joints and the foundation, not in the middle but on the inner side of the left shoulder joint; and it should be straight above the stone, and both ends should meet at the foundation, and so the belly cut through it, if it is wide enough, to accommodate, and inside should be narrow, according to the size of the stone, not too large; by chance the press might push the bone that is at the foundation, making it jump out during work; and know that there are parts of the stone where angles and edges exist: if it has a sharp edge to get out; and if it has parts below, like a glittering thing, round and smooth, with a light issue.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, then you should soak it, and make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For the two things that happen to the patient: either he dies, or his urine comes out and the limbs cannot be sutured; but always try to treat with the thread, or by dressing with tongs, until you treat it by pieces; and when you have completed your work, apply the wound of pitch and aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it, and put above it a moist cloth in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to calm the abscess hot; then revive the patient on his neck, and do not untie the bandage for three days.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you untie it, so that the limb is moistened with oil and water, then treat him with ointment of defernion and ointment of basilicon until he is cured.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	If the base of the abscess is cut and corrupted by pus, and congealed in the bladder, and it keeps the urine retained, which is known in this manner without separation with the urine: put then your dough into the wound, and extract that sanc, for if it remains, the bladder will be corroded, and spoiled; then lift the wound with water and oil and silk, and help him with all the ways you know, until he is healed; and it is fitting that, in every cure, you bind the two thighs, and assemble the medicines above the body.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	If the stone is small, and it is located in the urethra, and fixed there, and the urine cannot come out; if the doctor follows what I said so far, then you excuse yourself from cutting the tail (tail of the penis).
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proven this thus.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Before you begin to cut with iron, according to this form and so that it is at three angles fixed in one piece:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take the thread and tie it around the end of the stick, so that it does not come out in front of the bladder; then insert the foret gently into the vein, until it reaches the stone; and turn the foret to your hand on the stone little by little, until you can pierce the stone from the other side; if it comes out soon afterwards, then press your hand onto that which is left behind of the stone which is inside the vein.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it breaks apart and the urine comes out, and the patient is cured; and if you cannot do this for any reason which impedes you, then tie the thread below the stone and above, then fasten the vein straight to the stone between the two threads, then pull the thread out, and release the thread, and clean the wound with the icy solution that is in the wound; and care for it until he is healed.
de la piere des femmes	About the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It is not often that stone occurs in women, and if it happens once, the cure is bitter, and it is forbidden for three reasons: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that there cannot be found any woman who knows how to expose herself by mirrors, especially when she is pure.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third way is that it cannot be found any woman skilled in this art by hands; and the fourth way is that the stone of a woman is more embedded than the stone of an man, because it will make a deeper incision, and great fear comes from it. And if necessity demands it, you must find a midwife who knows well, take care to touch her true, and if you do not find one, then seek a subtle mirror; and present yourself before her with respect for the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and she commands that she does what you command from the investigation of the stone; and look very well whether the woman is a virgin: then it is convenient to push the stool out of its place and seek the stone. And if she finds it, she constrains her to do so in the same way as before her stool, and she commands that she presses her left hand on the bladder form.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	She finds it, so it is fitting that she moves it from great to great from the entrance of the bladder up to the lower part of the thigh; until it comes to the root of the calf; then cuts on the bone in the root of the calf opposite the middle of the femur where the bone appears and feels the bone in that area; and does not move the joint above or below the bone, and fastens the first joint a little; then pours hot water into the joint, if you feel the bone is very close to the wound so that the bone can come out, and notices that many kinds of bones are: namely, small ones and big ones and rough ones and smooth ones, long ones and round ones, and those with ridges.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	If you know the signs to recognize the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	Et if the patient does not rise, so put vitriol on him broken, and hold him one hour until he is stained red; then return to his work, until the pain subsides, and you have bleeding that I told you in the extraction of stones for your help in your work; and if the patient does not rise, and it's from the artery that has been cut off, so put powder on the wound and the stricture of tenters and bendles, and do not start again, and leave the wound to be, lest by chance the patient die; then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the wound is cooled down and the pulse returns, then return to your work, until the pain subsides.
de hernie carnouse	Of cataract
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	The water ram is nothing but an assembly of moisture or white scab, which is under the skin at the joint, that contains the blood; and it is called "syfac", and never truly in the flesh of the blood, if one thinks it's another liver; and that is the leather of the tendon between the white syfac that we have said; and this happens rarely or not.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this water ram is due to weakness that comes to the joints, and it spreads out that material.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the joints, and this moisture has many colors: or it's declining to yellow, or it's without red, or black, or white, and more; and these are the signs of recognizing this assembly, because if it is the white syfac that we have said, then it is the abscesses returning, little and long like a liver, and does not open the joints, because there is moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	If he has moisture in the own flesh, then the abscesses are found with one part of the vein and because of that it is thought to be another wound; and if the moisture is between the skin and the fat, it will smell bad; therefore, when you see know the color of the moisture, prove all the surrounding area, for that's how the form was before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	Therefore those who come after the surrounding area judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we cut with iron, it is prudent to let the patient be according to their power and the replenishment of his body; then take some of that fat and sew it onto him on a high place, and have them tie it up tightly on his left side, and command the minister to keep it on his right side, and stretch the rod over one of the two ribs of the shoulder; then take the pincushion soaked in blood, and cut the skin of the shoulder from its long joint down to its nail, and make a straight incision through the fat up to the white substance, and scrape it off gently according to their power; then pierce the plain white part with a needle, to the width of one large puncture, and draw out all the blood, and then put on your bandages, and tighten the skin upwards; and do not touch the skin of the shoulder, but only the fat; cut it all in the same way through and through, so that if you don't cut it well, it will return to the wound; and if the vein is forced out to your hand, then sew it up again when you have completed the work on the fat.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	If you find that the blood of the cauterized part has become corrupted with another disease, it is fitting to cut open the surrounding vessels in doubt about the slowing down of the bleeding; then cut the clot at the top of the vessel, and extract the blood, and cure as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	If the wound is assembled in two parts joined together, so that they are two separate branches; then cut off the other part as you have done the first equally, and apply the bleeding, and put in the wound a moist linen soaked in rose oil; and put over another moist linen soaked in wine and oil, and place above both clots, and cover with doubled cloths, and fasten it up so that it is tied according to this shape:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take the two cloths, and apply them to the skin with woolen padding according to this resemblance and assemble them by sewing in the neck of the braies, and one of the fingers presses on the foundation just above the back, and the other at the part of the nail; and the third finger up against the two angles, and so all assembled the restreinture in the loop of the belt; and it is sometimes treated with this cauterized branch instead of iron for the height of the wound, where you take a subtle cautery spoon, and cut the skin over the clots, and burn them as we have said, so that the white substance that contains the blood is revealed; then take the cautery according to this form, and pierce it with the nails, and scorch it with this subtle cauterizing heat:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	Instruct all manner of cuts you can do, until you have looked at all; and keep the fire from touching the eye; and know that this work is more salve; and be cautious of bleeding and wounds; and take care of congealing of blood; and if nothing causes you harm, or an abscess, swelling of the wound, or anything else, cure what harms you according to what was said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	If the patient is afraid and will not wait for this operation due to its horror, perforate the abscess as I told you, since when you are certain about the signs we have said that water is laid down, if you seat the patient on a high bed; perceive the incision in the lower part of the body from top to bottom wide, and make the perforation deep into the long body; and let the wounds be large enough so that all the blood flows out; then put cotton over the wound, and bind it, and leave for the remaining blood to flow out; then cure until the wound is healed; and if the thin linen does not allow the blood to come out of the mouth of the wound, if it suits you to put a quill or the instrument with which one treats the dropsy, since its form was as before; and expand the wound wide enough, and know that the blood returns, and is assembled after six months or when it has passed through, and when it is assembled just like before, and so will pass the patient's days.
de l’aposteme des coions	From the root of the abscess
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	That in the cutting of this root there is fear and many deaths, so it seems to me that it should not be left alone; and I will tell you the injury and similarities of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say then that most abscesses come from the body, and even from the liver; and this happens for many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is to say that this happens from the superfluous acid and water which is spread out in the liver or by percussion; and its color according to the color of the body; and it does not feel any pain, but rather an abscessed injury; and sometimes there are abscesses heavy with gallstones and rough in color, and some come from nowhere else than an artery or inflammation of the vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is not due to an artery, if you look at the disposition of the abscess, when you press with your two hands; and it does not suit that you touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	He who is swollen with blood is recognized by the disposition of its appearance, when you touch it gently with your two hands; and one can well make a mark on this resemblance, and on the other marks; and that you strike the exact location of the vein, then stretch the wrist upwards, and pull out the suspension from all parts of the vein.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the vein is already swollen with these marks, then it suits that you treat the vein, and strike it; and if it is blocked in the wrist, or within the vessels, it suits that you release all that space, and strike around.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the scar is behind him, so that you copy it all, and remove the wound, just as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your operations are completed, apply the wound of flaxen cloth moistened in rose oil and wine, then treat another patient until he is healthy.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscesses of the throat.
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess that has been swollen up, like a swollen tongue, with the softening of the throat, and the patient suffers greatly when it ruptures; and the treatment for this illness is as good as, or almost as bad as, what was done before, since we are following the same work.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	Instruct the patient to place himself on the elevated siege, then lower the suspender of the limbs below the knees to the nearest part of the body, and stretch the muscles; then cut with the spatula trenching large through the traverse of the vessels, until they are uncovered, and then burn from each side, as we have said in the extraction of arteries that are near the temples; then put a needle where there is a double thread, and bind it to the first part where the vein comes, and bind directly to the other cheek; then cut straight on the middle, according to the length of the body, and remove the corrupted moistures; then cure the wound as we have done for others when they are bandaged with bows, so that no vessel can swell up again; for by this there is no harm, and all the vessels come back to their normal state, if you treat them properly.
de la routure dou syfac	From the work of the cauterization
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The symptoms of this wound occur because of the section that comes from the cauterization, or the extension on the abdomen in the area of the ribs, because the intestines drop down from that wound to one of the sides; and this wound is either due to the cauterization itself, or the extension, and come about by two kinds of causes: either by percussion, by a blow, by burning, or by lifting an existing hurt, and by similar things. And the signs when there is an extension of the cauterization, are that they come on little by little, over a long time, and do not come suddenly; and the abscesses become equal in size until the end, because the cauterization presses the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is from the cauterization that they make a sudden onset of pain at the beginning, and there are various appearances of the abscesses under the skin close to, because it comes from the intestine and the body through the cauterization.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never again take out the intestines with the ribs, and retain them in place, and make the patient suffer great pain, especially when they are pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron cauterizations because it is painful.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And in this work, you are to command the patient to pull out the intestine into his hand inside the wound if it can be reached; then sew up his belly between your hands and tie his knees. Then cut the vein on top, and scrape off all the fat from the joints for a long time until you get nothing but bones; then push the needle into the space that is under the joint of the elbow; between your thumb, which is above the white part that is under the skin, and between the second white part, and behind the elbow, and lift the knee behind it. And command the minister to stretch the knee high, and release what is tied behind the tie; if you find no intestine or a hard white part, push it into the belly outside; then take an awl with three large threads made of four filaments each, and insert it into the back part of the fat after the joint, then cut the threads that appear from it until there are four threads left. Then assemble them one on top of the other in a cross shape, and sew the skin where we said is under the joint of the elbow with a strong tie made of two parts; then wrap the threads around the intestine and secure it firmly with two parts, so that no servant who nurses you can enter into you, neither a spear can penetrate through. And place the second tie according to the first one for two fingers long, and after all put on tight the skin which is under the joint of the elbow the length of a thumb; then cut in the part that is without bones or bowing, as we said before; then apply moist linen soaked in oil, and put it into wounds, and insert the tie we mentioned.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And at some point, it is cautered with white styptic that we have said, after the incision, by doubt of its decrement of blood.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this happens often, and let the ligature remain so that it may fix on him; and if it lingers in the chair, if it is moistened by hot water, and puts up what we have said, until it fixes; then treat the wound with another treatment, until he is perfectly healthy.
de hernie carnouse	of a hernia in the groin
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this case, I have never seen anyone who dared to do the cure with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is done in this way: like the joint where the bone is assembled, in such a manner that you fasten the straps after the waist, gently upward and downward; then cut at it, and cure the abscess that forms, until the strap falls; and cure as we have said, until he is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; 
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When you cut the hairs, if they sting and heal the wound, so that it becomes healthy.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The scalp is constricted and has no appearance in the incision; the cautery is more moist in this place, and closer to health.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the joints.
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	It often softens the skin of the joints in some people, because the flesh inside is softened and can be seen; it is necessary to treat it thus: when you want to cure it, you must make the patient lie on his back, and cut the softened skin where the skin is natural; then assemble the two lips with a bandage, and if you see, cut through three costures or four firmly; then cut between the costures, and the cure as in other wounds, until he is healed, and the wound closes, and the hairs grow.
dou chastrement	Letting loose from fire
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	We know that cautery is mentioned in our law, and therefore I do not wish to speak of it in this book; and it is necessary only for two reasons: one is that the physician knows how to answer when someone asks about its use, and also knows the cure; and the other, because we have often needed cauterization from certain animals to help us, such as a cow and an ox and goats and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that cautery is done in two ways: either by attraction or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In that which we do by attraction, we sit the patient in hot water, until their wounds are softened and relaxed; then we press with our hand, until they become numb and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Du chastrement de taille: it is advisable that you tie the best one and press the skin of the neck with your left hand, then suspend the cord, and strike on each one after you have well stretched them; and let any small spot not be touched so close to the vessels; and this way of cauterization is more gentle than that which is done by attraction, because attraction may leave some thing from the skin due to chance, because they are seeking luxury; then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	Of hermaphroditic individuals.
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	The hermaphroditic individual is of two kinds: one is that the two sex organs are open as if they were the shape of a woman's figure, or he has hair, and sometimes no urination.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other woman also suffers similarly, and has a lump on her finger like a nail.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the cure for fever and hunger is to copy the charred skin in such a way that you treat it as other wounds; however, in the second manner, there are men whose urine shoots out from their fingers, and they have no cure.
de la tentigene	of the tumor.
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	A tumor is a charred skin on the natural part, so ugly to see; and some women have it as large as a hand, and that's the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary to dye the excess of the tumor on your hand or some other part lightly; and don't apply too much pressure, lest bleeding comes from it, then treat with another treatment until it heals; for a certain kind that forms near the mouth of the throat, and the tongue, and sometimes bursts forth, and is like a cow, therefore they call it "cough disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you must copy it, just as we have said, and the treatment until she is healed.
de erratique	Of error
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Error is when the nature of a woman is not perceived, or if she is barren; and it is her nature by birth, or it happens to her by illness that has come upon her; or it is because she has been assaulted, or has had some sort of abortion, whether it's done in front of the mother, on the breast, or in other places, and because of this they cannot conceive, and childbirth, and sometimes they may have no flowers; and knowledge of this comes from observing the fall of a child.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If it is an abortion that is close in appearance, so be it for your two or the right.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is swollen with pus and it is close to two livres (two pounds), then run, and do so: place your two fingers together, and the woman be above on her back, spread out her legs; then straighten the two pounds, until the subtle swelling is reduced, and the stoppages are over; then take wool, and the powder in oil, and put it upon the lump, and have the woman lay at home each day, so that she will not heal.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the swelling is hard and dense, it is suitable to cut with a small spatula resembling a leaf of myrtle.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the stoppages are made of charcoal, let the swelling be compressed and cut; and apply medicines stained with blood, as is used in cauterization, dragon's blood, incense, a large quantity of wine; then bring in a cloth of linen wide enough so that the wound will not heal; and do this for a long time, and bring in a tent of dry linen; and treat it with other cures until it is sane.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when in the marrow comes a piece of bone, if you cover it accordingly this manner, unless it is an enchantment in the abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For when there is an enchantment in the marrow, one should not touch fire.
des emorroides	from hemorrhoids.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that do not usually occur by accident, and when old hemorrhoids develop they become painful; we have previously discussed the signs and symptoms of them, and I will explain here which ones respond to treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I said that hemorrhoids and pain in the thigh occur when they are embedded in the marrow, and if there is no sign of improvement by feeling, unless it is treated with fire.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the mare, one can feel them, are those that one can cure.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then set the altar with tongs, and strike it at its roots, then powder on medicines restraining blood, if it burns and cuts like dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then pour her feet into boiling water for an hour, then put her in cold water; and when she starts bleeding again, if so happens, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and grapefruit rind and galls and similar things, and then mix flour of barley with honey and oil, and apply it to her back and let it dry.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if she stains, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If it is so, if they make the patient inhale hot air at the back and at the breasts; then take linen, and apply the moisture in the juice of plantain or in the juice of hawthorn with wine, and let him inhale.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess rests, then treat the patient with ointment until he is cured; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a head as rough as a thorn, so it must be covered as I have said; and then treat him until he is cured.
des apostemes de la marris	of the marshes
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscesses come from the marshes, such as chancre and a stone-abscess, herpes, swellings, fistulas, hemorrhoids, and hot abscess, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in this division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is necessary therefore that I tell in this treatise the abscess which comes to swell in the marrow, which is not an abscess except that it resembles a boil; and if you see how the fire cautery works, then look at whether the abscesses are present at its beginning when it arrives, and filled with heat and fever, and if it becomes red then you will know.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore do not hasten to pierce, but let the wound heal until the pain is alleviated; and then put the patient on a bed, and place two pillows under his head, and two smaller pillows or so that he inclines, and support his back and assemble his limbs as far away from the leg; and spread out his knees, and tie his legs together with a good cord; then bring him to sit on the right side, and introduce the instrument used to open the marrow, for afterwards it comes to shape; it is necessary that when you see introduce this instrument, that you pierce first by one end to know the depth of the marrow, so that what enters from the instrument does not go further than it should, and does not hurt the patient; and if the instruments are large, it is necessary to cover the depth of the marrow with cloths, so that the instruments do not grieve him; and it is necessary that he put the horn of the instrument on top, and tighten the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is closed up again on its own, it is advisable that you avoid using hot iron, but treat it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
