Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	The skill is first in the delivery when she knows the natural figure of childbirth, and the signs that you see when you witness a woman push harder, and desire to urinate: then hasten the infant to come out; because seeing those signs tells you whether it is according to the natural figure, and is coming out through its head, and the second one with it; and when you see these signs, it is advisable to press lightly on her belly, so that the child comes out quickly; for when it emerges from its head, then the second one comes with it, and the blood of its superfluities is cleansed by good washing; and this which comes in other ways does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it happens sometimes on his feet, and he comes to the body or the shoulders, and the hands, or so it is, and he becomes twisted by chance before his neck, and by other foul figures; thus it is necessary for the physician that they be wise and subtle in these things, and beware of error and deceit, and I will show you all the figures on how to help him.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the infant comes to sit on his head because of natural causes, and the pregnant woman cries out in pain, and the virtue is weak, thus if you place him on a stool or women hold him; and if his nature is in oil or fenugreek, let it be cooked, and then give the physician an artery between his two hands with the small spatula that has this form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and cut the vein, and strike on one joint until the moistors in his joints are burned; and press the woman's belly so that the infant descends, if it does not descend, then it is necessary to cauterize the woman with musk and fenugreek with olive oil; then make her take the comfits and esternate, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: now the infant.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	If the two hands come out, it is suitable to reset them lightly little by little; and if they cannot enter, put the woman on the bed, and lift the feet high; then break down the bed on earth, and take care of the woman so she does not cut herself at the setting; and if the hands cannot enter and the child dies, then cut off the hands with the knife which is placed before, extract the child, and reset them equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	from the state of the child on its feet.
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes on its feet, it is suitable to push upward; and then turn slowly little by little, until it is even; then take hold of the feet and stretch them out little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it cannot stand just as soon as the child comes on its feet, because the command has said to take hold of the thighs and turn them out, so that it may jump up, if it does, God will have mercy.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not like what we have said, so the tumor grows little by little, until it follows its natural form.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	So it becomes lighter.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come like what we have said, then take musk and aloes, oil of saffron, and gum, and pound all in a mortar; and apply the ointment to the woman's nature within and avoid this application, then put her in warm water until just below the ribs; and when she is softened below, bind around with iron, and let go, and let one hour pass; then put her on the bed, then make her vomit and tie up her mouth and nose, and let her take some air, for now the child will have taken flight.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of a child's joint from its place
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, put on a belt around its waist; then lower its legs and sit down on a stool; and gently pull up its knees and arms, and place them above (the belly); and if the child does not cry out, take hold of its feet and give them a gentle kick, then lift up the belly, then pour some into the mouth; and let the child eat little by little; and command the woman to nurse the child until it comes to an end.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of a child that is born with one arm twisted outward
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	I advise that you try to return the hand: if it cannot be returned, then lift up the woman and have her walk; if she cannot walk, then let her lie on the bed with her legs bent; then give her a poultice as I have described; and if she does not conceive, then sit her down in that chair, then study how to return the hand; and feed the child according to its natural figure, and make it wean, and command the woman to nurse until the child comes.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the child on its neck, and has spread out its arms, and turned its face towards its back its mother.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	I advise that the bile should be applied to its hand, then turn it a little and a little, and let it lighten; and when it is evened out, put on the muscillaige ( possibly meaning bandages or cloth) of altee and oil, as we have said, then instruct her to move a little and a little; and when you have done this, sit her down on a stool, and instruct her to bend; and she should empty herself.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	of the same manner as it was to all that.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to this manner for all that, if the string is cut at its root, until the moistors (presumably the body’s moisture or humors) are emptied; and if the boils come on its face and on its neck, if you cut from behind the nose, so that it does not close up again, then the boils will die; afterwards pour the child into a clean vessel, as far as you have put them in, and instruct the woman to bend herself only once: then she will be lighter.
de l’issue des gemelz	From the birth of twins.
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	It is known that twins often appear, and sometimes they do not appear at all; or there are three or four: this is no extraordinary thing, for it does happen.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are extraordinary things, and they do not live if they have no name; I know that they are multiplied, and they are seized by the spleen, which is tied to the blood; and sometimes they issue just as naturally as all of us do, just as we said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they issue severely, then the treatment is as we have said, and apply gentle blows, and make it quickly and lightly what she does; and do it so that it may bring good health.
de plusors enfans	Of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Never are formed in the marigold I, II, III, IV, V, VI, VII, or more than fifteen, and they all take the shape of a child according to the measurement of their size glorious, and it is known that the barber knows all this, because by chance he has seen such a thing; so he does it accordingly as seems right.
de l’enfant mort	of dead children
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman with the dead child or womb, as I said in the division, and it does not come forth, and you are constrained to work on hands; if it seems right that you know whether the woman has a healthy nature, and no accident, and fear of death; if it seems right that the woman should be proud of her back, and her child inclined towards, and lifted legs; and the minister applies two parts of the molar to her mouth with moist oil from musk, and fennel, and linseed seeds, then the barber rubs his hands in these oils and musk, and pours them into the molar lightly, then chooses one or more of these that are suitable for her, and takes care if the fetus is visible, when it comes forth from its head; then he pokes the chosen ones between his eyes, or on his chin, or on his cheek, or near the mouth, or under the beard, or in the navel, or on the sides, and if the discharge is below the feet, he points or pierces it and to the costel, and applies one to each of these that we have said, until it comes to the empty thing; and this is the form of the molar:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Instruct the patient to take out another bone, or where you need to cut it so that the extraction is even; and then stretch it evenly in moving from one side and the other, so that the bones can move, and hold the joint fixed by teeth as in this form:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if it remains a part of one side, if the wound gets some of his two sides covered with oil, and pour them into that side, and treat the other side; and if it does not remain at all, put this bone or higher in him, and do that until he is fully healed.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes in front of the other, and he cannot return to the tightening, then it is necessary to wrap around the above drape, until it becomes whole; then cut at the joint of the foot or at the cut, and do that on the other side as well, and on both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the fever is on his feet, so that there is a light attraction and an address to the mouth of the arrow is lighter.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if he is twisted in the belly or groin, so that you extract it from the wrapped cloth over his hand; and tie the belly or groin tightly until the moistors come out, and if another limb is also wounded, and the head of the arrow remains stuck, then give him a drink with half an onion or two, and pull it out carefully; and if the mouth of the arrow is contracted due to a hot pus which has arrived, it is not necessary to further struggle, instead it is convenient to administer moist and greasy things; let him take emplasters, and cut in soft water and soothing herbs and oils.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	If the patient is on his back, and you can put him in a level position, do as we have said for the living child; and if you don't have enough strength, cut through it by pieces, and leave nothing of the second part.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done that, if they follow what we have said about the wounds on the head where blood comes from the nose; and if swelling occurs after bleeding, cut through it by restaining in water and apply other remedies.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman with child who had a child that had died in her womb, and she took another of the dead one instead.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, there came an abscess in the throat, and it swelled so much that it burst open, and great pain ensued.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was unable to translate this as I do not know what it is.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put under the plaster of strong attraction, and from it came a bone, and after some other days some others.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was surprised greatly, because that womb has no bone.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	So I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I examined the wound and pulled out bones until the woman was in a better state; and she remained thus for a long time, so that a little blood came from the bone; and I remember this chapter only because when the master physician saw an unusual thing, he knew to look for help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	Bring back to their place.
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	After this comes the form of pressing, because we have to apply books; and then again to both shoulders, twice as tightly.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	For all purposes, the horn should be more subtle in its restrictiveness, and made of ivory or boxwood; and the mouth of the instrument should have two fingers of a length, one an inch wide, and a margin as wide as the tree's trunk; and each limb should be two inches long with half a palm and no more, and these two limbs are to be bound together in the same way, firm in both directions, by half a palm or a little longer; and these bindings are to be put in the mouth of the patient to open when you turn both horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, having the likeness more subtle and lighter, is made from beech or boxwood, according to the likeness of the pincers; and has two joints bound together as you see, one palm long, and two a thumb's width apart; when you wish to open the incision with the entire instrument, place the woman on the bed, her feet towards and her legs bent outwards, then insert both bindings at once into the incision, holding firmly between your fingers; then move your hand over the entire instrument as you have done with the pincers equally, according to how much you wish to open the mouth of the incision, until you make that which she desires.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This instrument is all pointed, and it has many similar features; and when the mirrors are prepared for it, it is more speedy in action, and higher in esteem because of its quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not properly prepare the instrument before using it, because its need is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	If the secondine is retained during childbirth, it is wise to instruct the patient that she should keep her leg straight, and then have it turned outward in a suitable manner, and hold her hands closed to her mouth and nose; and if she falls through this, well so be it.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If this fails, cut the part, and make a puncture or wound, and put in herbs that can open the mouth of the child, such as camphor, anise, chamomile, cinnamon, and centaury; whichever of these are cooked or boiled in water on the fire; then put a spoon or puncture pot, and the other end in the mouth of the child, and tie so tightly that the vapors arise within the child's mouth; then have her spit out, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If his shoulder falls off immediately.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this cure and is not improved, instruct the bailiff to moisten her left hand with oil of sesame or musk, and then put it in nature, and when she finds it, grasp it and extend it slowly, step by step, so that the pain does not occur at extraction; but they must move gently to the right and left, and then treat; if it comes and is shed.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the pain is constricted, we have said the cure for vomiting, and fumigation with herbs; and if it does not improve from all that we have said, then beware lest you do not go mad while treating; but it must be the case that what is in the mouth of the pain, that you tie to the woman's privy, and bandage it with ointment tetraformacson; pourridge and put her back, and she will come from there; but nevertheless, when she vomits so greatly into the stomach and head, and poisons the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	If it is necessary, then let there be fumigations common to all: none of the ancient ones have tried fumigation with crow and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument at which you should fumigate the woman is, in retaining the flowers and the second joint if it is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is of the shape like a dog, and put the subtle head in nature, and hold the hairs large on the fire; and so let the fumigation be on the embers, and the gouttling until it is spent, and then start another.
de percier lou fondement	of piercing the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Since many children are born who do not have the foundation pierced, except that it is stuffed with a subtle splint: if it is necessary to bring them to the bath, then so let they pierce the splint in its place, and not the flesh of the infant too well, lest the dressing touch it; then put on a linen wet in wine and oil, and then apply the treatment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will stop bleeding, then place a poultice of onions in the wound and let hands lie still, and leave it until the fever departs.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And at no time does a sudden stoppage of bleeding from an unclean wound or abscess occur, if it is covered so that it may heal: whether you are cured, as we have said about the poultice of onions.
de la fistule dou fondement	of a fistula in the fundament.
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from below the fundament are nodules, and swellings that come from below the fundament before, or in the space between the two parts, if there is a fistula or multiple ones; and when an old nodulation exists, it causes, and brings forth moisture and pus, or bowels, and sometimes these fistulas burst open; and they are caused by whatever comes out of the body that the patient makes, and by chance, on occasion.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if they have fistulas that pierce just beside the bladder and just above half of the penis; and come to just above the joint of the thigh, and nowhere else on the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And so you know how to recognize the fistula continuing down towards the foundation, and not continuing: and it is that you put your thumb on the foundation, and insert a fine needle of iron or thread into the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has twisting, then you put a thin cloth or horsehair plug into the fistula until you feel the cloth or hair on your thumb; and if you don't feel it, and there is no purging, coughing, or pain, as we have said: "know that it does not perforate; for haste to cure".
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is cut across to the bladder or just across the conduit of the urine, then it comes out and cannot be closed by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it occurs just at the joint of the thigh, then the pain comes to that place; if there is no torsion and no discovery of the pain around it, then it is fixed in that place and nothing can be done by medicine or treatment with ointment; and for these cut fistulas have no cure but labor, and foolish attempts by well-meaning people who get involved.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	For the one that is not cut and is not old, there is hope for health by iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient lies on your hands over his back; and you lift up his legs to his thighs, and incline his thighs towards his belly; then pour a poultice of straw or plonk into it, if there is torsion, until you know where the pain comes from.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels pain inside their fundament, so you must put your two fingers there, if then it hurts because of the thing being punctured; and whether it is discovered or you feel between your thumb and nail the scar or the char, then you know that's a fracture; but don't work on it unless one can cure it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	But you can heal some with it, but this happens rarely; and the one who helps does so, if there is a subtle cautery applied according to the size of the fistula, as was said before; and pour in the fistula all hot, until it comes from beneath the fundament; and do this twice or three times, until you know that these fractures must be burned, which are like the feathers of a bird; and then put on moist poultices coated with butter, until those cracks cease, then apply ointment to bandage and cauterize.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is thus hurt, this is well.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If it is thus hurt, nothing else can be done to heal it; and if he tries in between, and does not pierce just as much as necessary at the foundation, and there is a thick covering of hair or wool between his two fingers and the tent, and you see the fistula where the covering comes out red; then cut at the beginning of the fistula, and drink afterwards from it, and apply the cautery after, until he comes to the head of the tent; and will be delivered from the pain, and cured. Then know those hairs that are necessary which seem like an owl's feather, and do not remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if he does not want to be healed, and you cut between you and the wound, then the cautery of fire or medicine will be applied.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery, it assembles two things: this means that there are two ways of applying cauterization, namely, the application to dry bones and the application of moisture, and its subsequent evaporation; then the cure for moist swellings in butter or in cheese broth, until they begin to blow, and then they will be inflamed in the bowels; then cure the wound of quick stabs made with hard flesh, and this is where the drying medicines are applied.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	When he is restored, if it is healed and does not come back again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if an abscess comes just as deep into the bone and is distant from the body, pour in two or the depth of the bone, and ask about it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tendons, and they are between two things, or it is near to being pierced, if there was only the way of hope and expectation by the management of one of the three methods: either you cauterize as we have said, or you cut just to the bone, or if you can, you apply plugs and cure as first; do not go too deep into the bone that you will cover the foundation that holds it, lest there be extractions in the opposite direction; then the cure, as we have said. By chance, it may heal, or the covering skin is removed after being pierced from the inside, or with some other instrument designed for this purpose; then remove that faulty flesh which is in the wound, as you can; then study to restore the wound, and to keep the fistula away from the foundation: if it happens a lighter thing to the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are made in this way; and it is when you put the tentacle into the fistula, and it is on the edge of the skin's bottom, that one takes a tentacle perceived according to this shape:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I put the twisted thread in two, and put the tentacle all along the thread in the fistula until it reaches the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is stuck in the margin of the skin's foundation inside, then pull out the thread from that puncture, as if you put your two fingers on the foundation; and take the head with the thread, and assemble the two joints together, and hold one to the other, and leave them one day or two; and bind them no more, except when the threads break those characters between them, and then cure the wound until it is closed and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not perforate, then pierce it in all ways that you can, unless it is too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not advisable to tie up the wound if it is too deep, and then treat it, as we have said, until it heals.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the wound that forms from the spicule (a small spike) of a thorn which one makes a fistula is much worse for one part and painful, and on the other part not at all, so that one should not cut it if one does not have to cut it, as you see here:
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids.
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are according to two manners: either they are within the fundament, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and in some cases there is a single one or more, and they protrude from the fundament and on top of the fundament; but those that do not protrude have little moisture, and sometimes there is a small amount of hot water or vinegar or some blood, and they have the color of flesh; and the cure for those who have them within the fundament, if you command the patient to lean over into chambers until the fundament falls off, and they can be seen, then take away the cord, or cloth, or piece of camel hide; and pull them out with your fingers, then cut them, and powder above some hot powdered medicines that are on their place of cautery; or you cauterize as it is said in the chapter of cautery, since the cure for others until they heal. And if the fundament cannot come out, then close the patient tightly with a tight bandage and harsh soap to wash what is inside the fundament, if it can come out openly; but when the patient feels it, and if the thread is formed in the fundament, then it is an easy cure; and you cut them as you see, and cure as we have said until they heal, and that they fear the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is fitting to tie up the costume according to this manner: take a thread, and pour it into an awl, and then pull the thread upwards and pierce the awl on the other side, and turn the two joints around the thread downwards from under the awl, if they are not too tight; and tighten the thread, then release it, and draw out the awl, and do so for all the others, and let one pass to correct the superfluity of the blood; then put on a moistened foundation of linen or rose oil in cerote, put on the foundation, and instruct the patient to rest; and then leave him until he farts, and when he is cut, if the cure of rubbing and other cures are sufficient, so that he be whole.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	cut very tightly around the veins or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	It happens frequently that blood clots suddenly in the intestine, and by the force of nature, when the disease is old and medical treatment is worthless.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is advisable that you reset to the point of a spatula or at the angle of an eyebrow where the scab is exposed, which does not let it dry; then treat as long as it is healthy, if it suits; and if it will not heal, re-rase it more strongly than before, until it heals completely.
dou fremit	a fist
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	An ant, a small appearance unbecoming the body, and goes all through it; and sometimes the truth is frozen, and one feels it just as if one were dead from the trembling, and comes to every part of the body, and more so in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	Instruct the patient to take a candle made of one goose quill or a strong vulture feather, and put it on the affected area until the purple circles appear all around; then turn your hand over the entire candle so that you mark all around the purple circle, and seal it with its roots, and let the area heal from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see this, do it with a candle of straw or iron according to that shape, and be subtle under and careful above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Don't pierce it, to avoid breaking the vein twice, and pressure And if you see this, cauterize the purple circle as is in front of or near the cautery instrument.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form like a bladder
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	There is no blood loss when using silver or a curved instrument, or a melted iron or tunic; and sometimes one uses these small and large instruments, according to what they are applied for.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	These then one uses in the treatment of children and those who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the small or large syringe depending on whether it is above or below in this way:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And if there is a deviation or the belly is tied, as you see, and the syringe is inside perceived; and has one hole on this side, and on the other one; and the belly is wrapped around with medicines from a jug of best or parchment, and are all perceived with small holes, and in between each hole there should be one ounce, then fill them up with a strong thread, cut thick as a finger nail, into X or where it's turned inside out, and assemble the belly like a donkey; and when the medicine is inside, if it sticks to the instrument at the front of one thread, then clisterize; and this is the form of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And so let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the head with oil or beeswax or suchlike substance, then pour it in lightly; then exert the physician's hands together on him as much as possible, until he is quite still, then extract the plaster, and raise the patient's legs to appearance, and if the medicine will come out, so that the boil comes as far as it can; and if he sleeps a night after, it is more aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you plasterize him in a disease of descending belly, and the medicine is hastened to come out, then he will resume it as long as he is sane.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are on the fundament or abscess, so that the plaster is as subtle as for an infant; and this is the form of the subtle plaster where the skin is tightly strained:
des plaies	Injuries
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said in the cutting of wounds the treatment for injuries; or you will tell us about the treatments for hands and medicines, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that injuries are diverse according to what they are made of, and according to the places or locations where they are inflicted, and why they are inflicted.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	Things are made because of wounds by the cutting of stone, the sharpening of a sword and knife, or lance or mallet or net or similar things; or what are done according to the places of the body, such as wounds that occur on the neck, head, shoulder, stomach, liver, or other members; and I will tell you about each wound, and begin with simple wounds to the head, for it will be remembered in this chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I dis that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, take care if it's from a stone or similar things, and the skin is completely torn apart and the wound is great, and you doubt slightly about an abscess: so make it heal as soon as possible the head itself if it has come with some bleeding of the wound, and be healed on the opposite side of the belly; and avoid the patient being replete with wine and fatty meat.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not heal, if the meat is weakened and he does not drink wine or eat meat: and puts on the wound, if an abscess comes up, put cotton wool soaked in rose oil alone, or vinegar suppository; and if there is no abscess, if it is fresh with all its blood and has been moved by air, powder, as I will tell you later, and his bowels have not been opened: then put on some ointments until he heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is great like a sword cut and similar, and the lips cannot be brought together by stitches, then they are sewn together, as I will say of wounds of the belly, from the seam.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to bone and skin, and it doesn't hold up except for a little bit, if you cut; then treat the wound with medicine, and apply a hard rind in its place of leather, and instruct the patient to eat coarse foods, like boiled eggs and bread, and poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find out the skin is rotten and it's not stuck to the bone, so that when you cut through the whole thing, and drain off the pus, then treat it; and if there's an artery in the wound or vein that cannot be stopped by medicines alone, and you want to stop the bleeding, if you can find the artery, and tie it with a thread; and if this doesn't work at all, then cauterize.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: and put on this powder which also makes the wound heal.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is this: take incense for one part; dragon's blood for two parts; calcined vivarium for three parts, and make a fine powder, apply to the wound, and bind tightly, until it has dried well and healed completely; and then bind it securely, so that it does not swell, because you do not remove medicine while it is healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes only calcined vivarium is used when there is no incense or dragon's blood, but the wound has been made to heal.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	But if the wound has been made to heal and it is in a state of being healed, then don’t put on this powder; but put on some digestive ointments or poulces (likely poultices) made from flour of rye mixed with water and honey until they become dry; then the cure will do other cures until it is healthy.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if a bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, if I touch you gently, then I will tell you this afterwards about small head fractures.
de la plaie dou col	of the neck wound
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is on the neck and it is simple, but there is no difference between the two of them regarding the head, but if the nerve on the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it's the nerve, then there is no other issue than to leave the cure alone and put nothing restraining on it, because it hurts at night and makes them recoil; and putting anything on the wound does not hurt, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and the continuation of the wound is with the brain, which is in the higher members; but if you have medicine, such as calmed charcoal in sweet water, and anointed with rose oil, and boiled again in sweet water, and other stones from mine according to this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound is large, tie with bandages first, then apply treatment until it heals.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	If the wounds are very deep and a vein is cut close to it, or an artery is severed, then apply pressure and sew, because bleeding comes. If the espinice of the throat is cut, or the jugular, and it needs to be guarded because the meat is swollen, tie the vein close to the neck, but only on the surface, not touching the neck itself, but rather remaking it according to its natural shape; then apply immediate pressure, and let it rest for some time, then treat with ointments until it heals. If the wound has pressed into a bone, then cauterize; and if there are pieces of bone, cut them off entirely, because you cannot have any left, and leave only what is infected, so that it may open up and heal itself. If the wound is fresh, then powder over the powder I told you.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is an abscess, so too as I have said in his chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of arrow or sword wound
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a gunshot wound or stab wound and the wound is deep, then look to see if there are openings at the wound site: for it is said that such wounds are mortal; and if they are not deep, and the wound is fresh and has only blood, do not put powder in it, nor bind it tightly around the wound, lest you cut it further, and make it worse. But instead tie a soothing ointment to it, and bind it twice a day. If you have no ointment, put fine cotton wool on the wound to absorb the moisture, and let the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more; if there is no spasm, nor pain of heart, nor other signs of death; and when you see the bones are in good disposition, then it is said that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Instruct the patient to apply poultices and other treatments until he is healed; and if he cannot heal or recover, then know that there is an abscess. If you treat it as you must do.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is an incision from a sword or knife, and it is simple, on the front, side, or back, treat according to what is in front of you. If it is large, suture; and if it is small, apply powder; and if it has been driven into the bone and cut off pieces, as needed, remove the dead tissue if present; and if not present, let the wound dry out, which will ease the extraction of other wounds from the same members as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	A falling or bursting of the stomach.
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IVI manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I have a small wound and no matter of the intestines is removed, and there is a great need to treat it, this is one of two methods: either by the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen due to the heat.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, cut it in one of two ways: moisten a sponge or one half of the cloth soaked in water alone, or you cook in boiling water with vinegar and spices, and remove the intestine until it inflates; and at no time do this unless the vine is restrained, and it is softened so that it can be deflated.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the inflammation depart, moisten the intestine with water or cook it slightly, because by this the entry is made easier; and if it cannot enter, then make a small cut in the instrument with which one strikes the hemorrhoids; and the first cure is softening that makes the size, so that none should be cut unless there is great necessity and it cannot be done; and this are the instruments to break it: tear inside in the chamber and do not close, and see how it is shaped:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines jump out, so you put it back again according to its natural form in its own place, if you have the power, for this is useful.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is in the lower part of the belly, so you should put the patient on his back, and lift up his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the lower part of the belly, then lift up the head and loin more than the parts below, and thus, as I said, apply to wounds that are large or small.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, tie off what is exposed, then take a needle or more in your pitiful hands that are holding all the bleeding to one hand, and sew the lips together; this is the common way of suturing, and it is done by pricking an awl or several times, according to the size of the wound's length, leaving two fingers' breadth from the top of the wound, then making a strong thread tight; and piercing the two layers of skin with the two layers of suture underneath, as far as you pierce them, so that they are sewn together in four parts; then tightening an awl's thread around two parts, sewing the two layers of the wound together at once, and then leaving two fingers' breadth again, then making another awl, then tying the thread just as you did the first one, not stopping until the wound is completely closed; and these needles should be medium-sized, neither too small nor too large, because the small ones cannot penetrate all of it, and the big ones can't fit well at all; so they should be medium-sized.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I let the intestine go then it was twenty-four hours later and the wound had healed for fifteen days, and the cure, and I was sane.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And they had thought that he was dying, but it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with medicine, because I was in the forest where one could not find anything or any medicine; and I put cotton wool twice a day on the wound, and washed it with honey water until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you the two proper ways of sewing: take the needle and thread from the other side until this one; when it has pierced the skin straight through, if you prick with your finger or cut, and then pierce again on the other side from the one that was piercing; and the feeling of this sewing is like sewing as a tailor sews clothes, leaving one part of the skin open and covering it up on the other, until the whole seam is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second manner of sewing, which the Gauls call properly, is like this: whoever sews, they assemble the two parts in a natural way, and they call one of their chief onto another chief, in such a manner: prick an awl or a needle close to the chief with the sinew, and pierce it alone, leaving both knees of the chief; then turn the awl, and make it pierce from the other side until you reach that place again, leaving both knees of the chief; then pierce one and another from the other side, into two other knees of the sinew on the other side; and this is the second manner of sewing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	The Gauls are said to have spoken this word, and no one testifies to it, that we must sew the belly with two needles, if there is thread in each; and you must push one needle from one side and the other from the other side, in the manner of those who sew corsets; and know that when a rupture occurs in the belly, the sewing is more grievous than for other bellies.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is like that of other wounds: and it is that when you find the fresh wound with all its blood, as long as the arrow has moved it, so remove the intestine, and the cost; then put on powder rubbing charcoal, and if the arrow has moved it, put on any ointment present, until the wound heals; and pick the thread, and sew the suture, and the mirror; then cure the wound like the others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, so put on it, as soon as they come to be brought out, cotton wool, and move II times a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	But you have no need of other medicine in addition to these circumstances when the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound will cause commotion to the main members, then it is wise to apply a light linen cloth soaked in hot lard oil or rose oil, and put it on the abscesses, and under the joints; and if he feels pain or rot in the bowels, and it often happens, so you should bring out the clister of black wine tede, and similarly when the rot comes from inside the intestine; and make a hole in it, and look that when it is the large intestines, it is easier to heal than the small ones.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine which is called "jeun" cannot heal when it is rotten, and this is because of the plant matter that is in it, and because of the subtlety of the entire body, and its proximity to its natural state.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.
