And if the zirb (arrowhead) jumps from the wound, if you put it back again as the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it becomes old and turned black or dark, it is advisable to cut out the one that is black, for there will be no bleeding because of the veins; then strike the one between the ligature, and hang the two heads down from the lower part of the wound until the arrowhead falls, and the pain subsides.
de la routure dou boueil	of the burn from a blow
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is swollen and the wound is small, if it can be restored in some men, because I have seen that one man was killed by a lance to the stomach; and it was injured and became an abscess, and as a result of this, there was expulsion and ventose (gas); I put him into treatment according to what I know, and did not cease from subtletizing until he was healed, and his pain subsided.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him heal, I doubted that the sick had a malady in his stomach; and there was no harm, but he improved in good condition, eating and drinking; and some experimentors said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it must be tied in this manner: take firm bandages to large testes, then assemble the lips of the wound, and when the firm bandage has covered the mouth, put the two lips on top, so that they tighten his mouth; and then strike the head, and so it stays if he cannot untie it; and then apply another firm bandage in this manner as before, until the wound is completely closed; and seal the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, and there is no inconvenience to the patient, and it can be tied to the intestine with a fine thread that has been taken from the intestine of an animal, in this manner: take the head of this fine thread from the intestine, and then tie it to the head of this fine linen thread twisted, then push the thread into the needle, and sew the intestine, and pull back through the route; and this way of sewing is not inferior than according to the art of marriage and hope; and if the wound is great and wide, especially when it is in one of the intestines’ small passages, so that there is no strength nor health, except subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or if it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Any wound or abscess that becomes inflamed with age is called a "fistula", and especially when it is swollen and has a discharge.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	Et fistule is according to the nodulation of the skin that is free from hurt and rough, or one does not feel pain, and it is also like the hair of a bird; and sometimes clear bowels, and sometimes thick; sometimes little, and sometimes enough; and I have talked about this in the division of wounds, that every wound which is not healed, and there is no flesh, is caused by fire only through one of the VIIII causes: it is to know, by the smallness of the flesh or bone; or by malice; or because of what it has a tough flesh inside, and on the lips, which does not allow the flesh to grow back; or there are too many bowels; or the blood is poor, and the medicine is not good in the cure; or because of that which corruption is a manner of pestilence; or because the property in the region is late, the digestion is delayed, and the health is late, and escapes by nature; or there are women or bones: and I have shown all these causes, and signs, and cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary that I inform you of the treatment for fistula which is done by operation of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	There are fistulas that occur in all the limbs of the body; because there are fistulas that come from great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the scrotum, or to the intestines, or to the bladder, or on some of the ribs, or on the spine of the back, or on any joint of the hands or feet; and since some appear in the property of the principal member, and have similar symptoms.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are in this manner are of a diseased nature, and there is nothing but labour and ignorance; and if there is any fistula which does not appear at first like one that I have mentioned, and you have faith in the cure, and you see it work out, take a bowstring or an iron probe, if the fistula is straight, if not; and if it is crooked, search for a subtle attempt to penetrate it, because the probes bend in the tortuosity of it; and if the fistula has lost fingers and you cannot see well enough to search for it by prodding, search with one of the missing fingers, because the moisture is cut short on one of the missing fingers, and makes it foul; then look carefully at your power, so that you know whether there are bones or nerves, and tell truly to the patient how they feel under pressure from your hand, and where they feel it; and when you have certainly known where it is, and whether it is near a joint, nerve, artery, or vein, among those I have mentioned, then make an attempt according to what I have told you, and cut through with force whenever possible, until the bone has been freed from the fistula; and then treat it as long as it is healed, and if the fistula does not heal by this method, cauterize it as we have said; and if the bones are corroded by the fistula, make a cut.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	The patient or his representatives should not grieve over a vein that is bruised or swollen, as we have said; and if the bone is uncovered, and there is corruption and gangrene, then remove it just as long as the corruption remains visible, until all of it has fallen out, then cure with remedies such as arrowroot until he is healed; and if he does not heal, and his bowels are affected, since before, know that you will not be to blame for this: if uncover and ask as much as you want him to go to the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore him; and if he is in such a state, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If this is not the case, know that the corruption has gone too far, and you will not be able to do anything for him; if there is no other plan but to treat with the weight of nature; and if there are small, corrupted bones, and you can extract them with pliers, if the instrument is suitable for this, and if there are many bones, extract all of them, and do not leave any one behind; and if moisture causes a counteraction, and there is no fear or error, strike and apply medicine and charcoal, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	It was a youth under XXX years old who had pain in his leg from a cause that came within the body, until the materials arrived at the leg, and fled from a large abscess, and had no reason to open; but by those who were blind with their folly they opened it so much that the abscesses burst, and a lot of material came out, and a fistula formed, and many people thought he was dying from the wounds and moisture in his body; and for two years I saw him treated by many, and there was no cure in the art of hands, until I was summoned, and I went to see his leg and the medicines used on it, and what corroded by the abscesses had a great effect on his body; and the flesh of the youth became red, and had the color of citrine.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I applied a tent in one of the abscesses, and then I searched for all the abscesses, and found that some were meeting at other parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I me have failed, and I cut in one of the wounds until I discovered a part of the bone, and I found it corrupted and infected, and came to be the corruption inside the bone; I saw what appeared from the bone, and I thought there was no other corruption except for that which I had taken out; and I began to restore the wound with medicines for a long time, and could not heal; and then I recommenced, and discovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, and I saw it again, and then I took it out, and I thought of healing the limb; but I could do so until I cut into one palm of the bone, and the wound healed rapidly, and it did not happen again except for fear of the weakness of the patient, who cannot bear, and for the fear of death that I had in him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the evacuation of blood often takes place, but it brings no harm and the person recovers entirely, and in their place an iron-hard cartilage forms, and they are of good disposition and have no harm or ill effect whatever, neither at rest nor when coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, if you wish to do it this way: take a ligature, and strain it at the head of the bone which opens, and command that they stretch it up; and put another ligature of linen larger than the first one, and tie it above the cartilage which has opened the bone, and stand the chief, so that you treat the corrupted cartilage below, and uncover the cartilage above on the limb where you see it open, so that the bone does not bleed the cartilage; and put a splint or a table below the bone to cover up the corrupted cartilage; and let it stay for as long as you can see and feel the corruption, and let it stay again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	Et se li os est corrumpus, and n'apert mie, and li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;
dou feu	Out of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The cuts will occur either because of something inside, or because of something outside; and when you have treated the wound with medicine as a cure for the corruption by means of medicine treatment, and it does not profit at all, then one should cover that limb up to where the corrosion is coming from, so that the patient escapes death or the evil consequences of the fault in the member; and there are signs such that the members become black, and it seems like they have been burned by fire, and after being blackened, the corruption spreads to other parts of the body; if one covers them up, and this is due to a stroke caused by venomous animals, as a scorpion from the sea and lizards and similar ones, if the wound is in the head on both sides, then you must strike there again and do not give any space for it to come back near the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	Et s'elle vient jusc'a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne vienge jusc'a bras; and if it comes just above the hand, if you hit the joint, so that the corruption doesn't come just before the arm; and if it comes to the arm, if you cut at the elbow; and if it passes over the elbow, this is death, and there is no use with fire, only the amount of its virtue; and thus do as long as the corruption comes into the bone: if it comes to the first joint, hit after the other joint; and if it comes into the bone, cut all the bone; and if it rises in the knee, hit at the joint of the knee-cap; and if it comes above the knee-cap, there is no other way but to kill the patient dead; and the manner of cutting or soothing the member is such that you must tie it up above and below, and extend some ligatures one towards the lower end, and others towards the upper end, and serve the flesh which is between the two ligatures at a span wide, until the bones are uncovered; then cut or soothe.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, and let it stay for as long as possible so that it forms a big swelling of the bowel; and then cut and pierce, and pull out the bowels, just like us barons; and the skin above is just as subtle as I am embroidered, and will not run into the bone or the nerve, and this illness is called "sain", and is not called "fistule"; but if it is so long that it comes to the bone in a straight line, then it is called "fistule"; and the skin so is that you cut through it all at once, and even when it is subtle, just like us, and will not be cured by its corruption.

de l’aposteme de l’ungle	Of the abscess of the foot
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Gangrene is an abscess that forms under the foot at the heel, or hand, or by chance in other places; and when it becomes old, and if one does not take care of it, it comes to be an open wound, running and oozing blood until it reaches the root of the foot, and by chance all the way there; and comes the corrosion just at the bone, so that it brings great pain and stench, and the wound becomes large and swollen.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés. Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain from a sore throat

des vils	Old age
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	The big veins are swollen with blood that is melancholy and superfluous, which come to other members of the body; and more happens to those in the legs who walk on their feet and work and carry loads. than to others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary that you give them no enemas of bile, and then cleanse the spleen with basil.

de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is bound or tied in the legs, in hot areas where there are no herbs or trees to grow, and on earth where there is no moisture; but by chance it may be found elsewhere in the legs, and this happens because of putrefaction that comes from below the skin, like a snake entering inside the body and moving outward between the skin and the flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante. des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms that are born between the skin and the flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "disease of the ox", because it often happens to cows, and it is a small worm that is born between the skin and flesh, and goes through the entire body, moving up and down, and causes pain in every limb until it bursts out from under the skin or falls out, and makes pus; for it contains porridge of some humors, such as worms and serpents and lice and intestinal parasites; and doubt is cast on its malignity, because when it moves through the body, it rises to the head, and sometimes gets stuck in the eye, and destroys it; and this happens often.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you are treating and tending to this patient, it is impossible to do so when they have fever: therefore, then it must be that you tie the limb above and below with a strong and tightly bound ligature, then strike above and treat with it, and if the pus is flowing in at the shoulder, and you do not see it, then cauterize with fire on top, until it dies; and the greatest harm it causes is that they run out of oil, as we have said; and if you see it coming towards the ear or near the oil, then restrain below it with a spell form, then strike above, and treat with it; and it is necessary to use the patient with purgative body medicine soluble for the bad humors that are forming, and if they become putrid with rotten meat.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain which comes from overexertion
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes to some members, moving from one member to another; and I have seen this what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I went to see a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein on her arm; and after a while, I saw it rise as a worm into the shoulder, faster than anything, like living silver when it cut through the limb at another place; the pain left that limb, and stuck in the shoulder, and then a little later ran all over the body, until she came to the other arms; then she told me she was writhing in agony around the body, as I saw her.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was much surprised that she moved thus from member to member, because I had never seen this disease in such a manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Tout voie, I have seen many who have wanted to move from pain of their body to another, but I did not want it, as I saw in the woman; and I thought that was why the women had a thin body, and uncovered breasts, and because of this appears the windy constraint; and they do not appear according to this reason to those who are strong, and have moist bodies and uncovered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see someone being treated for this illness, and the patient feels that pain, if it is opened as we said, immediately cut above and below hastily, and then strike so that the windy constraint falls out of the body; and cauterize the body; and if you do not see it in your eyes, then the cure for those who are afflicted with windiness, such as fetid pills, serpentine pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	from the arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are different, according to their appearance and according to the nature of each person's body or where they pierce.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of their forms is that there are those with large points, small ones, and pointed tips, and soldered ends; and those with two angles, and those with tongues, and those with pieces, and such that pierce in one member according to two manners: either in the principal member pierces like the brain, liver, heart, pancreas, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When she therefore pierces any one of these members, and the signs of death appear to you, which I will tell you later, it is necessary that you take out this arrow, because death comes after in many dispositions; and if this bad sign does not appear, and the arrow is not properly pierced, then take refuge, and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the vein bursts and pierces the bone, and it sprouts a new flesh above the brain, is what causes scotomia and sickness and inflammation and redness in the eyes, and redness of the tongue, and convulsions and mixing of understanding, and vomiting of blood; and by chance, it happens without pain in the nose, or ears; and by chance, it happens to the words and voice; and it appears as if the wound is moist and white like a fly, and similar to burnt charcoal; and if this sign appears to you, then hold with the cure, and take out the vein when it's not present.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the vein when it bleeds or blood, is that it is near the left nipple, and feels like it's been pierced in something hard, not empty; and by chance, the vein turns black as pus, and comes out cold and sweaty, and fainting: this makes you doubt if the person has died.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	The sign of the arrow that does not bleed is only without any scum falling out of the wound, and its throat is swollen, and the patient's face turns red, and they gasp high and are chilled by the frost.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow is discharged into the covering of the shoulder, so that it strikes one of its small bones; and it causes great pain and much gasping; and all its limbs move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow hits the stomach, by chance so that it falls from the wound any indigestible meat.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow hits the stomach, and it falls into nothing but air through the intestine, without any hope for the treatment or extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	If the blood vessel ruptures into the bladder, and urine comes out in a stream and the patient is forced to go outside, and they feel great pain: see that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, if they are cut and bruised and swollen and the shoulder and elbow and groins and axillary region and spine of the back and flanks and groin and thighs and limb, as the condition is: they are safe according to many opinions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery and it does not cause harm, as I will tell you, for that reason: that you may do the same.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to the man at home with an arrow stuck in the thigh or shin near the knee: I tried to pull it out, and pulled it from the other side under the fat of the ear, and was made whole without much pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And tie around a bandage that is tied to the cut in the oil of the grape under the paper so that the bandage is tight and you can only reach as far as the point towards the fist, and the bandage was big as an arch Turkish, with all these iron legs since now, my ear has healed, and no bad accidents have happened to me.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And tie a bandage around the neck of a Christian, and it was an Arab-style bandage for the ears; I shaved the beards, and handled it carefully so that I could tie it, and the Christian healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And tie a bandage around the belly of a man who was fallen or had been thrown into the wind, and I thought he was dead; but after 30 days had passed, without any improvement in his condition; I cut up the bandage, and tied it again, and nothing bad happened.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	If you see a man who has an arrow stuck in his side or back, and the wound is closed; and the arrow remains inside him, and he does not feel any discomfort in his natural disposition, nor finds any trouble in any of his natural movements.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And see another man who has an arrow stuck in his face, and the wound is closed; and he suffers thus for a long time with great pain; and there are many other similar things.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And I saw an arrow stuck in the man of princes, the king, who was hit in the left side, and was declining to the right part; and the arrow had been lodged there for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I found the wound extremely narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I don't understand what you want me to do.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I sought to feel the swell of his belly at that point, and I didn’t sense anything; and he felt pain and swelling behind his right ear.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put the swab on his hands daily, and solved the wound directly, and he remained so for a long time, until he felt the swelling in his neck that day; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I put medicine on the wound, a corrosive water, daily, until it was dry, and I tried it, and felt the head of the swelling which dried up in his neck; then I adjusted through the opening of the wound by that medicine, until the head of the swelling appeared visibly; and after passing well through 4 months, and then bursting open the wound so that I could pour out blood from one side and another, and it wouldn't come out; therefore I didn't stop trying to subtilize and devise methods with instruments, until I took one day the tongs were well made, according to the shape that came at the end of this chapter, as I was doing, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And they judge that the cartilaginous tissue around the nose cannot be restored: I restored it then, and the wound was healed, and the patient's illness was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or I have told you the quality of extracting arrows: so put your care on what I do not say, for the books cannot know everything; but the wise masters understand well little of anything, and they work well on what is present and failing, making new work and using new instruments, at the removal of foreign things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not enter the body into the member where they are inserted except in two ways: either by the natural opening or by some other way; and that which enters through the skin, is an arrow entering flesh, and occurs sometimes now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	Instruct the patient to let her sit until the wound is fully cleansed and appears well; and also if she has been stuck into an artery and cannot come out, let her sit so that it does not heal in a short time every day, but rather let her sit until such a time as the swelling subsides; and then she will come out, and if she does not come out, then pierce through to all of it, for a subtle thing is needed, till the swelling subsides, and then take her out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if an arrow has been stuck into the bone of the head, and is going straight down to one of the two halves of the brain, and because some of the things I have said to the patient: if you do not treat it, but let her sit until she appears well after some days, for if the arrow comes straight down to such a place, that’s death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is fixed only in the bone alone, and does not come out at the same spot, and the patient stays there some days without any new accident, then it engages itself into the treatment.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is completely stuck in that way and cannot come out for sure, then administer tartar to the inside, as I told you; then treat the animal until it becomes healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is returned to the animal's body if it cannot be seen, and the wound has covered its entire length; and if you feel it, if the string has any suitable instrument attached; and if you cannot stretch the skin around the wound, and if there is no bone or nerve visible, so that you can see the extent of the wound; and if you can't pull out the arrow because of the tightness of the skin and the depth of the arrowhead, then carefully extract as much of the arrow's bone as possible from the hole until you can remove it; and then break or bend the ears of the arrow so that you can pull them out more easily.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it once, so that the pain is gone from both sides until the limb is put back in place, then try again, for the extraction (of the bone) is painful.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if they take the blood counter to what we have said of the cure in this chapter; and you are warned not to cut near the nerve and vein, and put on engine so that you can treat the arrow wound carefully, or quickly, or firmly, or gently; and put the patient according to how he was when the arrow hit him, because it is the greatest help that there is, and if you cannot do so, then put him according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, or if it opens up something with it, or the skin is swollen in the direction where you see or feel it: then put on tight clothes, as long as the tongs can take hold, and then pull out: if it's stuck now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, so turn your hand around completely, until it enters into the bone, and then expand the bone, and pull.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it will not come out, so leave it in place for a while, and then continue to extract it until it comes out; and if there is an arrow stuck in it, if you pour water all over the arrow, and if it is inside you, see how much of the arrow enters into your hair with the instrument head; and then pour more, and if the arrow has entered into your hair, so pour into the instrument with the point inside, to facilitate the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow has entered into it, so it is fitting that you copy all of its length within or where the venom is, if you can, then treat the wound as it needs.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Instruct the patient to cover it up if they vomit or pass or in the belly or in the bladder or on the chest, and it is near; and you can cover over it, if it has been touched; and protect the vein and the nerve, and then draw it out, and then sew the wound, if it suits you; and care for the patient until they are cured.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the tongs used to remove arrows are like the beak of a bird, and thus we have this shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And they come in many forms: great, medium, and small, according to the amount of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The form with the handle attached to the hair is like the feathers of a bird, to push into the tip of the arrow, as it is in this shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of the nails for pressing and stitching is thus:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of veins on the body common
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	Veins that cure are thirty-one, because there is one chief sixteen, namely: two branches after the ears, which are called "herbech"; and two arteries in two temples appearing; and two veins that are in two eyebrows of two eyes, which are called "aspire"; and a vein on the forehead; and a vein at the top of the nose; and two tendons around the neck; and two veins above the lips, which are called "augeherich"; and two veins below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins that cure commonly are five in each arm: one is the cephalic, and is on the left side of the chest, and they call it "vein of the head"; and the median is called "fast", and is composed of the cephalic and basilic, and they call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic is on the right side of the chest, and they call it "vein of the stomach", and is above the fold, and that is the one that cures, which appears clearly on the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the artery is the one between the auriculate and anular, and it has two vessels; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one is below the coracoid process of the left shoulder blade, and the second is on the tendon of the left knee joint; and the third is called "nese", which is in the other side's knee joint; and in the other leg there are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The vein that is behind the ears helps with cathartics and migraine; and its quality, as I tell you, is that you raise the head of the sick person, and rub the soft or rough cloth on the veins; then tighten the patient's neck with a string, so that the two veins appear behind the ears in two opposite directions: when they do, and you feel the pain behind your thumb, then press in; next take the lancet, and pierce below the vein right to the bone, then raise your hand to the entire vein, and strike and cut both the skin and the vein well twice, so that you see the blood; then strain and tie, until it is healed; and I have said incision and cautery previously in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The sickness of the vein on the front is worth as much as the sickness of the head with ancient facial diseases, and emigraine, and redness; and in those who have strained their neck by twisting, so that the vein appears; then take the instrument which is called "sawyer" in the form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point on the vein, and pierce upwards from your hand, or with another thing, and let the wound open according to the amount that you see; then release the patient's neck, and tie the vein so that it is sane, and never again bleed with a large flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not fitting that the flames should be too large; and to cut cleanly, because the bone is close, and by chance, break the flame when it is subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The sick people of the two veins that are in the two ribs should be aided by holding the eyes and the tingle and the redness and the orifice in the oil, and for the diseases of the face; and the qualities of their sickness are such that the patient twists his neck from any tie, as before; then the healing, and it is the healed through a hollow, a little long, a little wide, because there is no char.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the splinters are subtle, in case they break; then do a cut of blood, as much as you have need, and then tie up tightly, and tie well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The sickness of the vein at the neck is very good for ague, and for a severe sore, and for diseases of the face, such as emigration and redness that comes on in the face, and especially when it is old; and the qualities of the sickness are such that the patient twists his neck, then twists his vein to your left hand, and take the subtle splinter long, and stick it into the space between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well there, and if you do not go too much further, and make a cut of blood according to your need, then tie it up for one night, because it is very quickly restored; and this is the form of the splinter:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The sick from two gouty shoulders help themselves by straining the artery, and at the beginning of surgery, and with much illness, and emphysema, and corruption, and herpes, and it is said that the qualities of the sickness are such that the patient cuts out his throat on one side and the other, just as we have said; and so the master stands above the head of the sick person, and the sick person sees in another seat, then heals the vein with a small incision, tempering it until necessity is met; then refashion another in the other vein, then loosen the bandage, and tie down the veins moderately, that the patient does not strangle; and let him go just to morning, so that the wound may be healed.
de la sainie des leivres	Of the sickness of the feet.
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The sick of the veins on the lips are aided by coal in the mouth, and by corruption of gums, and tearing of lips, and they do not heal.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of the vein is such that one must sit the patient in front of you, and strangle his neck as I said; then turn the lip, and look at the veins, of which one is on the right upper lip and the other on the left lower lip, recognizable by their being black and having fine black veins: strike therefore both of them and if you do not recognize them, and are in doubt, strike the larger of each part, and likewise do for both the veins that are above and below, for it is the same manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the vein below the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The sick of the veins which are below the tongue are helped after the pain of the cephalic head, and it is at the constricting of the neck, and with illnesses of the eye, and with illnesses of the mouth; and the qualities of a good healer if they are such that they put faith in those who hold them before the sun, and lift the tongue, and look under each side one vein black: then heal both and the other, and do not walk too much because below they are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins that are cut according to common practice are treated in two ways: either with a pointed stick at the entire warm miter, or olive oil subtle as if it were torn flesh; and they are called "aneasil", and are large and subtle according to the size and tightness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The famous mercurial form is so renowned, and it is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the vein cheeks plain with large blood clots that contain large clots and trouble; and this is the form of mercury olive.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more subtle in application, and it is for healing the small veins subtly, or with subtle blood clots of citron.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The basilicon remedy, which is one of these veins, aids greatly in diseases below the throat, and around the neck, and around the liver, and stomach; and it is necessary to the lord that he heals quickly, and he should take care of the artery beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery, and bloody discharge comes out, then it is necessary to cauterize, as I have said; but the mercury should not be pinched too hard, but rather cut like a knife.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	In case the basilic is not open clearly, it should be extracted, and another one changed or if there is any rain on it, or you heal in its place with wine poured into the arm: it opens clearly; and it strikes the flame again as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you see a swelling on the vein, it is also fitting to extract the arm, touching the vein as long as you know the pulse; then mark the vein with thread, and then tie the arm, and strike the vein with the flame again; and be careful not to cut into the artery when you see the vein swollen, for that is the artery: avoid it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see a swelling rising as high as the urine of an infant, and it is not red or subtle, take this to mean that it is without the artery: hurry up then, and put on your dress long and tightly, then remove your dress if there is no stain, for this has happened many times; tie the arm, and leave it like that, and do not move the ill limb; and be aware of fear, and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	If they are not stained and he vomits, and his medicine is not present, then cut the artery if it opens, because the head of it is withdrawn; and stain him without.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a piece of gum, and make it, and take one half and bind well to the other until tomorrow; if he vomits, this is good; if not, then as we have said, take the powders that stain blood; and staining is not hurtful for those who are in worse disposition due to small wound of the arm, and with the power of the band of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The venous illness in the middle is aided so that they treat blood on the head above, and on the body below, because it is composed of basilic and cephalic, as we have said; and it is fitting to the lord that he warms himself for the nerve which is below, and if it is pressed too hard into a point, and it heals the nerve, and it swells and they become healthy, but by chance it cannot heal; and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in anyone for its subtlety, it is fitting to take care of the healthy ones with the instrument analgesic; and withdraw the nerve to your best.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if he has a vein between the two nerves, then pull it out long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The headache remedy is to apply blood to the head, and to aid the eyes; and it is wise to anoint with olive fire or myrtle fire, because it is the safest of all veins, since it lacks nerves and arteries.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	In all cases, it is wise to seek the lighter remedy he has, and not be troubled if one must try it for the first time, and then resume; and by chance his legs swell up in some men, but he will not be distressed.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is according to your opinion.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about healing is that bloodletting should be done only to maintain health and to remove coming illnesses; and it can be done in one of the three veins: head, fast, and basilic; and if one chooses to bleed at the beginning of praying for Lent, in autumn and winter after eating, when the sign of repletion appears; and one must bleed on the first day or the third, after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The sick person who is served has no specific treatment determined, but rather when need arises in the morning or at night, in all hours and at all times; and it is not advisable to treat children just before their 14th year, or women carrying only four months' fetus.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	It is not advisable to treat the elderly who have passed their 60th year.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And if anyone wishes to be treated in any manner whatsoever, then it is advisable that he has a light bowel movement through an enema, if he has many times retained feces, so that the veins do not constrict the intestines with unnecessary superfluous parts; and does not heal those who are too fat from meat, or who have dysentery, whether severe or mild; and if they are troubled after colic, vomiting, and a decrease in the stomach, and numerous times of urination, and travel, watching, and working, then subdue the humors, carefully without excess, by foods and drinks and medicines, so that you may know the price; then take an bath, if nothing is forbidden, to subdue the sickness, and heal from the wound on the third day, just as we have said; and beware that day of work, and pain, and luxury, and such-like things; and be quiet and cheerful, and be treated higher than those who are sick, and rub his arm twice or three times, then loosen the bandage in the middle, because when it is too tight or too loose, he cannot cure him without; and then rub it with oil, until the veins swell and feel; then pour the enema of a small amount of old oil into the vein on his left hand, so that the vein does not burst and fail to be touched by the needle.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that burst like strings at the veinier, and there are such that are full of windiness, so when you put on the flame, it retreats into flames, and cannot open the vein, and thus is one of those; and if they sew the vein, then the wound is too tight, so therefore the surgeons should be advised in these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens for the first time, it's good; but if not, then restart again on top of that or hastily below, if the veins are not puffed.
