Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the veins are puffed and the patient fears, let them rest for one or two days, and do not tie the arm: by chance an abscess may come; nor enter into the bath, then restart the treatment whenever it pleases; and if the pus is small, carefully cut through with subtlety and you doubt that it will not produce a lot of blood as you see, so be sure in the same vein to cut directly at the flame; for this happens many times when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the inflamed leg, do not start again with the dressing, and put some lard oil on it, for it lightens the body with the wound, and is moistened by the lard; and thus administer lard oil to each dressing that you make to heal the veins, so as to stop the flow of blood through the wound; and this same thing must be done three times a day, when putting on the lard, so that it does not penetrate too deeply into the leg; and yet with subtlety and without force when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess comes, which happens often at the same time when there is no treatment other than applying to it until the vein opens up, you must hasten and put on the leg a moist sponge soaked in water and with a bit of wool; and restrain for one hour; and it's necessary that you do this after the issue of the wound from the vein, and if it remains on the leg after some days without any sign or color, it will not be bad; and if you see, put on something from aloes or mirror dissolved in calamine juice, a medicine.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times have an abscess and appearance at the wound of the basilica; thus place your hand on it, and if you find the joint swollen with the pressure of the hand, then that is a bad sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	So avoid putting anything on it which we have said, because by chance you cut into an artery; but instead make it dry for a while to firm up the joint, then apply another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each person according to the quantity of their virtue, and the color of the wound.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if it is not black, then let it be released until it turns red; and if you see it thick, let it be released until it becomes subtle; and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is fitting for the one who is weak and feeble, and needs extraction of blood, that they be made a larger wound, and have wider sores; and for the one who is feeble, do the opposite, and it will help them recover quickly and frequently, and must be recovered by cutting across, not with force; and this manner of healing is safe from the deterioration of blood and the spreading of nerves, and is more beneficial than cutting both short and long.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for the one whose pulse must be taken during healing, it is fitting to give them a moist pain in juice of green apples; if he is hot, take out the blood three or four times; and if his complexion is cold, take sweet bread before the healing, moistened with syrup, or with aromatic syrup of sugar mixed with spices, such as pepper, cannel, ginger, and cloves, a fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if the palm is affected, after a great amount of blood has been lost, it is fitting that he drink a weak broth made from charcoal and fragrant syrup, and use other things we have said in the division or chapter on syncope for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to take out another limb, and heal himself again, it is fitting that when he is weakened by great blood loss, he should recover little by little, according to the continuity of his virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who wants to take out another limb after the first blood loss, and he has a strong constitution, then he will recover in seven hours after the first bleeding, or in the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wants to heal himself on another part, should he be able to heal himself the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, and made come fever; if you must treat a great quantity, and enlarge the wound so that it reaches the breastbone; then when you reward all the conditions of healing, and put your hand on some fingers when they heal, so that death does not occur in the same place, and this happens many times when the nurse is careless; and do not dare to untie the arm, and make the wound open a second time, until it is closed, for you press hard on it; but if it is curved, then extend the arm quickly, because it would be bad; but let it heal the second time; or if there is a point of flame on it, so that the vein is frozen due to blood loss, and put some thread in the wound and water, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is pulled out, let it go and do not hold it tightly, so that the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if the wound needs to be treated again, on the same spot, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein on the arm is healed in place of the wound on the head because it was composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the way to heal the wound is that if the patient puts his hand in hot water until the swelling subsides, then ties it loosely so the vein appears well; then now he heals the wound from across, not too long nor too short; and if wounds are wide, and heals well near the joint of the hand, and cannot come out, then put the hand back in hot water, and let the wound heal in the water, until you have enough; and if it healed so, do not put the hand back in hot water again, for it is more healing in winter than in summer; and healing from this vein is better than all other veins, with no artery or nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The sickness of the left hand is equal in value to all diseases of the heart, and this is the way: strain the hand, and pour it into hot water, until the pain ceases if you see; and if it heals from the side, and if you copy it all over, do not grieve anything; and do not move too much because the nerves are now completely numb with frost, and then put the hand in hot water again, if they are not frozen in the wound, and do not come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have cut the wound as much as necessary, put oil and sinew to close it quickly, and so do each of these things.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The sickness of the left hand is equal to the disease of the mouse, and do it just as I told you over to the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The sickness of the spleen is worth more than all other diseases that are in the body, as with illnesses of the stomach, and retention of flowers, and disease of the rains, and of the kidneys and old joints, and similar illnesses.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the qualities of his spleen are that when sick patients put some stone in hot water, and rub on the vein until it bursts, and lie above the joint of the foot; and if the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot they move a great deal of blood; then heal it first or else it becomes larger again, or at the ankle, that one will be worth.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you heal it above the foot, then be careful of the swellings that are below, and cut to open as when cutting, so that the flesh may be made thin.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if it cannot come out, so he puts his foot into the water, and leaves well to empty the vein.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the wound is first time clean, he repeats it again above a little because his foot is salt; do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and do so with the sponge of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The salt of the vein on the calf is at the ankle, and its pus is worth the pain in the hamstring, when it's for draining.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And if the quality of its pus is such that the patient takes a bath, and extracts it above the ankle four times by twisting, because otherwise the vein does not open; and if it opens, then he cleans it in all ways you can, across it; and weighs that you copy it, because his salt is sour, and it is very swollen to human hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	If you do not find it true, then a rain of blood will come from the opening or from the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and beware of the wounds; and do as much care to the wound as you see, and then release the ligature, and put on cotton and bind; for she is now healthy.
des sainies de ventouse	From the venereal sicknesses.
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	The venereal sicknesses are made of horns, or pitch, or glass; and there are two ways to do it: either by wounding and drawing the blood, or by wounding.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this wound-making which is done by wounding and incision of blood is done in 13 ways: or it is made with fire at once, or with fire; And the one who makes a wound by wounding and extraction of blood is done on 13 parts of the body, where one is in the whole of the head; and two are around the neck; and two on each side of the neck; and the wounds under the chin; and the wounds on the shoulders; and the wounds above the ribs; and the wounds on both arms; and the wounds on both legs; and the wounds on both ankles; And it does not treat with blood but only for small veins that are spread throughout the flesh, and because of this, no one is weakened much, just as one makes a vein treatment; and it should not be done at all, nor with fire or sense of fire, in any disease that comes from overstuffing, until all the body is empty.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	Instruct the patient to ventouse when necessary for illnesses or due to habit, bring it forth every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and frequently in between times; for there are those who, when they must have ventousing, become heavy-headed; and such as find redness and swelling on their face, head, neck, and eyelids; and such as experience a drop of blood in their mouth, and withdraw their tongue, and feel pain; and there are those who dream, and see blood and wounds and such similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	When we see these signs, and especially when it is in the middle of the month, we command to ventouse after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The fever of the mouth aids in relieving the gripiness of the head … that comes to the eyelids, and it should not be done after all evacuations of the body; and this ventousing is in place of the evacuation of the cephalic, and it should not be used by those who have hot temperament, or who have catarrh, because it causes great harm; and for that reason, it should not be used by the watchful, nor those who have cold headaches.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover from this often become blind, and for that reason it is fitting to place the vacuum a little further down by the suspicion of blindness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The vacuum of the neck is in place of healing of the head and throat, and for this reason it is fitting to tighten the chest with a pinprick, and to make a cut in the channel of the groin, and to toast, and to fill; and they should not apply too much pressure, because if they hold it too tightly, it leads to blindness or stomach pain or bowel.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The vacuum to the right of the neck is equal to the pains in the head, and eye pain and migraine, and strangulation, and pain at the roots of the teeth, and is in place of healing of the throat; and it is fitting that you command the lord that he presses his hand so that it does not cut the artery, and does not take action prematurely.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The windings under the lower chin value to a disease of the mouth, and to corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and they are in his sicknesses of both left lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The windings under the shoulders value to a disease that comes from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The windings under the sides value as much as three veins of the arm, because it brings forth blood from those great veins; and instruct the lord that he must not make a deep incision, for the limbs are bare of flesh, and know well beneath nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The winding that is on the buttocks value to hemorrhoids from the fundament, and to various diseases, and it is necessary that the wound be large, and of earth, in order to properly treat it; and if it were subtle, it would break; and thus cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The body sores on the legs heal quickly, because they attract blood from all over the body, and are worth the old pains of rain, and of marasmus, and of inflammation; and they weaken the bones after a long time, and bring weakness to more severe conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to put on the ventouse is that you place it first empty, and suck it in perfectly, and then put it hasteningly, and move it equally, and do not stop doing this, until you see the vein red and swollen, and appear the red color of the blood; then fasten, and remove the ventouses, and take care of the disposition of the body, because there are those who have taken a chariot, and clear pores: if it is necessary to wound only once, and it is good to make large wounds, and a little deep ones.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the wound is not large, so it must be hurt twice: once to subtilize the way of the big wound.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the wound is very thick, it must be cut a third time; and when we wish to treat small wounds little by little, we should suffer only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want much of the wound, we should repeat often; and if the wound is thick, we pierce into it, and when the skin is torn apart so that one can see immediately, cut at him who has a large hide and tough skin, and whose pores are open, and anoint them with vinegar oil, or sweet almond oil, or oil of currant seeds; and if it's on ivy, on cresson, or camomile, or other similar things.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the swelling is big and cold, so take olive oil of marjoram, or balsam, or anise oil.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if that person has healthy skin and large pores, do not put oil on them, but instead wash it after the water rose, or cold water, or elderberry water, or cucumber water, or porcelain berry water, or other similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, lift them up with similar remedies, such as mint water and sumac.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have big swellings, lift them up with old wine vinegar, or elderberry water, or anise and camomile decoction, or other similar remedies; and do not wish to be treated with enemas before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath for one hour or two; and do not sleep after the evacuation, and must wait until it can be evacuated again, when it should be evacuated and when it is swollen.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And watch out for those who recover are choleric, and if they do not become too hot and inflamed, it is suitable to take cold things, like pears, grapes, and lettuce at ease, and similar things; eat a little, and drink broth of chestnut, and moist meat.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those with a cold complexion, should drink syrup of honey, and fragrant wine, between old and new, eat little, eat pears, pheasant meat, and small game birds, and pie; and on the day when they will become hot, he must drink more than eat; and it is suitable to give some people honey or mustard once a year, before or after their convalescence, to comfort the main members; but be subtle about this, for it is not suitable for those who are already hot to drink.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles qui sont mises sur le foie, et sur la mice, et podagre, et sur le ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que pour atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sur les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sur le ventre et sur la boude pour amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l'opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sur le foie et sur la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont vuides pour sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d'aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c'on emplisse la ventouse d'aigue chaude sole, ou d'aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the vacuum administered with fire is thus:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And two fingers of width and half a palm from front to back, and on the costal side one inch inside, as if to puncture an arrow, and is made of flax, soft in front so that it does not bleed the patient when placing it on the member; and at the middle has a stick of wood or iron through it, to hold a bandage in place, and are large and small according to the diseases and age of those who take them; for the vacuum of children is different from that of adults, and the thin ones are worse than the fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And thus you put this vacuum on the member: take a bandage of wax or linen and place it around the ventilation tube through the stick that is in the ventilation tube, so that the heat is at the bottom of the ventilation tube and does not burn the patient; then put it on the member, and tie the fingers we mentioned above, so that when you want to let go, the vapor goes out and take off the ventilation tube; and take up the linen as before, and rewrap frequently if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the case of someone who suffers from pleurisy, with aching, without any swelling or bruising, it has no advantage to be brought to bed, unless he is filled with fever, and put on that limb alone, and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	The swollen ones are only brought to bed in limbs where you cannot put ventouses because of the smallness, as with lips and gums, and similar things; and if their discharge is foul, like pus or filth, then take them away; and put one into a sweet fluid, until they become familiar with it, and have nothing in their bowels; and afterwards, let them be opened from vein and ventouse, and then rub the limb until it's red, and put on swollen ones; and when they are full and flushed, if you can put a ventouse on, do so, because this is very good after.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If they do not obey the cautery, instruct the patient to let the shoulder be elevated, and then wet, very well, and then expect; and if their shoulders are too sore after the body has been washed with cold water, put a linen cloth on them, until they are stopped up; and if there is much discharge, put vitriol crushed or vinegar, and similar things, until it stops; or you put on the shoulder, half of melted frozen flesh, and leave it until it dries on the shoulder, so that now it will stop; and if you have more need, take other poultices.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the poultices do not take effect, then rub the shoulder with fresh pus, or prick it so that the discharge comes out; and put it on, and as soon as they feel the pus, they will dry up; and when you see them stop bleeding, sprinkle some powder of aloes and silk broken, or ash, so they will stop now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	The Book of Injuries begins.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, for restoring fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, my dear son, that the art of this chapter has never been found in the ancient books, nor have you read any letter about it; and for this reason, our science is lost in our land, because I have not found a good one; and I know nothing else, except through the knowledge of the ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have treated their science, by experiment, and by my daily practice; and here, I have described what is contained in this chapter, condensed at the end, and shown clearly the forms of the lesions that must be applied, as I have done in these two preceding chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say in the prologue of this book about the sums of speech and the chapters or where the wise man puts his understanding, and keeps silent for so long that those who have experienced it will learn and acquire this noble art, and teach others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	When any fracture or dislocation or twisting or laceration occurs in the body, it is advisable to hasten and save the patient from one part and another, if no other remedy works, due to weakness of the body, or sickness, or old age; or if the swelling is excessive, or cold hands, and chills caused by cold, that is to say frostbitten fingers, and not drink wine, nor eat fatty meats, and do not stuff oneself too much with heavy foods which fill the veins with blood, until you have no doubt about a swollen joint or an expansion of matter in the limb; if you return the patient to their usual government when they have been ill.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	When the broken bones begin to heal, it is fitting that the patient be nourished with foods that cause great swelling, such as those which have viscosity, just like bread cooked in water, and ris, and testes, and piez, and pance de vaiche, and oefz, and fish, fresh ones, and large wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For swelling caused by this nourishment appears sooner and happens more quickly than the break itself.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And you should know that old and worn-out bones cannot be properly mended or soldered according to their nature due to the dryness of the limbs, nor those which are too soft, like the bones of small children; but there is no cure. Instead, place a large splint over the broken bone until it heals and joins together with the limb as it was before; and do not neglect its work entirely, and for this reason they must nourish with great food, just as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And you know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	But the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the leg or foot, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	Because there are fractures that occur at the joints, and others caused by cutting, as if with the length of a pinhead to write.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And when there is a fracture with an open wound, and a fracture with a small split or crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each type has its own specific tool and instrument in restoration, according to what is remembered by the patient's experience; and it is known that the fracture of the bone is perceived by this that the limb twists, and opens well due to absence, and feels like pressure on the palm; but if there is no twist or lump, and the patients do not feel great pain, unless there is a point of fracture; but he can still have a twist, split, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not necessary to move your hand, but put on medicines that come after this, and then tighten now subtlety.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the break that is in the arm, and are two parts of a joint, he must now put equal points, just as it comes; if it comes swollen, then let him wait for one day, until the swelling subsides; then put it equally to what you can easily measure and feel, and know that the restoration of this part is lighter than the restoration of that which has pieces; then tighten it, if necessary afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, and it is two parts, then it is either by hand or by piece, or on a small member, or by two cords, or by one cord and the hand; and put the limb according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the limb are cut off, you must restore them in their proper place, at each joint, as much as possible, and take care that through your treatment there does not come a new lesion or pain to the patient; and add well the two heads of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And the patient feels well in his hand if it seems that he is not at all: so carefully, and do not strain him too much, nor press as those who make it come by their own labor cause a hot and constricting contraction to the member, just as we have wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is stiff, if you carefully tie up the patient so that he does not move, neither watching nor sleeping, nor moving, nor in any other way; and be well careful that the limb is firmly tied so that he feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	But when he feels no pain, it is not quite stiff, and you must carefully put him in a certain disposition so that he feels no pain; and be careful that he is put straight, lest twisted positions come about while he is restored to health; and the qualities of the broken limb are according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	The part of the body that is broken is different in size and form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Small members, such as fingers and toes, require wrapping with soft and delicate cloth; and larger ones, like the knee and thigh: require wrapping with a wide and strong rope, because big ropes compress the whole big member, and restrain it from all parts equally, so there is no gap. Then tie tight stockings, three turns or four according to the limb, and pull the hand tight on the entire rope, then go above the break and tighten less, until the break opens a little; and soften the rope little by little, so you get a great part of the healthy part; then take another rope, and turn it back onto the broken leg; then go to the lower part of the break, and tighten moderately, not too hard nor too soft, as we said in the first sentence above; then put between the ropes stockings or cloth, until they are all equal, then tie everything from above with a band, and then put your pins well-made on top, if there is an abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	If it has an abscess or swelling, then put on a dressing to soothe the wound with hot salt, and if one cuts into it, and leaves it for some days; then strain out the swellings, and cut from its width of one-third inch cane resin, or of wood used in making cleaves, or palm fronds, according to this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the bandage placed on the break be a little larger and wider than the others; and be of the same length as it requires for the small or large limb; then strain out the bandages again just as you did at the first wound, then tie above the break with an avenging thread, just as you did in the first wound; tighter is over, less so; and it is advisable that the thread be medium, not too thick or too thin, and of linen fine, for if the threads are big, like I have wanted in making works of the fools who make their bandages with corded linen threads, and this is a great error, for the bandage cannot be even if it is too subtle, and does not suit at all that there should be between each bandage less than two fingers' breadth.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is wounded by the arrowheads after the bandage is applied to their wounds, then put soaps of linen or wool under them, so that they do not bleed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a fracture, and the nerves are broken, I will tell you the cure after this.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not advisable to strain or pull apart all the broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	Because when the limbs are large, it is not advisable to put nails in them on the first day, but rather after five or seven days, or longer according to the healing of the abscess at that time; and here is how the ancient surgeons used to restore fractures, dislocations, and twists: take flour that stays by the walls of the mill, mix it with a lot of eggs, make this concoction not too clear nor too thick, and use it, for this is the common way to restore a fracture in many cases, and myself have seen it restore fractures in both women and small children, because it was neither too cold nor too hot.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Other method of splinting restores the break and dislocation and twist: take beeswax and lanolin and ungument and asafetida and gum arabic and mugwort, 10 parts; mira and aloes, 5 parts; alechil, 7 parts; and make a powder, and mix with honey of wine; if the complexion of the flesh is hot, use this plaster, because it is of good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and saves many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of splinting that values the twist: take mugwort and visnmalve, 10 parts; mira and aloes, 7 parts; acacia 6 parts; Armenian bole 10 parts, grind well, and boil with wine or honey, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way to bind and apply plaster is that the jointed bones should be separated from their limbs, and alleviate the ensuing pain; and use bone putty, and cure the break with the bone; take a new linen sheet, and mix in oil easily and gently, and place it on the limb.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Plaster casts do not restore the joint, but they are good for soothing abscesses and properly healing pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way of plaster that restores the broken bones is to take dried fig leaves and earth leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way of plaster for restoring the break in the bone and to alleviate the remaining abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take the root of vimesmallow, camomile, violet flowers, wheat flour, one part from each; and grind, and mix with wine, and apply to the limbs, which is warmed up by mixing with wet coriander water or water alone, and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to treat with more force than the first, when an abscess comes back to restore the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take the roots of vimesmallow, and sesame seeds, balaustine, melilot, and sansuce, and violet flowers and camomile flowers from all one part; and grind, and mix with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Iporcus writes in his book that you should not put oil and wax on the broken limb to restore it, except for this method alone, and he says that it should be between too dry and too damp.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that one must place the broken limb above, to restore, things dry and warm, like mirrors and ointments and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to heal the wound and relieve pain: take mallow or horse chestnut, or goose feathers, and gum tree, and make them equally so, grind them, and make a paste, and put it on the wound.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then remove the dressing a little later, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor that they feel the bone out of place; if it does not remove by itself with their hands every day, but the pain comes to the limb, or prurites, with rest, swells, then hasten, and remove, and put on a new dressing now; take light linen, and an sponge soaked in moist sea water, and plunge into the water, and lift up the limb, until the itching ceases, and the pain is calmed down; then let it rest for an hour, then put on dry linen, moistened in water or olive oil rosé, and tie up with a bandage, so that you are sure of no pus forming; and rest the inflammation of the limb, and remove the pain, then resume gentle treatment, and add a little dressing, and do not strain it too hard as before; be subtle until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	If you see that there is an abscess on the cheek and redness and pain and swelling it has set in all over, and you have to apply plaster and tie it up again if it happens again, as you did with the first part.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	If this does not occur in the member as we have said, and you do not untie it after three days or four or five, but rather leave it for twenty days, according to what is observed, until the fracture heals, and approaches the joint again; then loosen it more than before, and increase its flesh, just as I have said; and if you see that the leg dries out more than necessary does not happen, understand that there cannot be a rupture, therefore do accordingly: arise from the hot water immediately whenever you untie it, every time on a third day, and with a little bit of oil; through this work therefore cut off the swellings in the member, and apply hasteningly what the foolish physicians do, who leave the member crooked.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various kinds of breaks
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many kinds of breaks, and various forms, and the causes are determined; for there are breaks that are caused by the force of a sword strike, and where the bone is crushed under the weight, just as it is under pressure or a blow; and because of this, such a kind of break is called «haichure».
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	When the sword strikes the bone from above to pierce it, and is called this kind of break «absolute», there are two kinds of wounds corresponding to these two kinds of breaks: great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if it has been pierced by a thrust, or a cut, or from the bone of a stone, or from a blow on the bone of a stone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if it has an ongoing fracture that approaches just below the skin where it is under the bone, or above the bone, and this injury is big or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there is a wound that is closed in the bone just as thin as our nails, and the fracture is small, and because of this it is called this "capillary" fracture; and if the wound was made or caused by striking with a stone, or falling, or something similar, and the piece of bone gets inserted into the joint, and the little bones are like those of a cauldron when they melt onto the cauldrons.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens to many of those who have moist bones, like the skull of an infant; and it occurs in all these kinds of fractures, small pieces are separated as if they were stones. And I will speak for him.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And know all kinds of breaks by removing them, and investigating, and by the corruption that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The similarity of hair is known through this: when you discover the bone, and you stroke upon it, if the break is opened.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the break, be careful for accidents in the patient, and if you see no evil accident, such as vomiting of bile, loss of intellect, swelling, paleness, fever, and the eyes protruding and reddening, and other similar symptoms, then it cannot be cured without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an impossible accident, and you expect a recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	When the patient comes to you for the first time, and it is in winter, it is fitting to remove the bone in front of the 14th day before the moon.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if this is the case, hastening to remove the bone in front of the 7th day instead will bring about corruption of the tissue underneath the bone, and come the accidents that we have stated.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the break of the bone comes just next to the membrane covering the brain, it is fitting that you cut through the broken part in this way: and take the patient's head, tie him down, and uncover the bone in all directions as much as possible, and in the shape of the wound more conveniently than you can, and if blood comes from uncovering the bone or the abscess, then help with what is needed, and it is that you fill the wound with moist drapes soaked in oil rose; and let the wound rest until the abscesses are quietened down, and be sure of the bleeding stopping; then begin to remove the bone, and this is done in two ways: one way is that you cut through the incision tightly beforehand, and it is like this:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then you must break the other limb more than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have to do a number of cuts differently, some are three and others are wider, and they should be pointed, and made of iron in shape, and work lightly so as not to hit the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and thick, it's best that you penetrate through it, so that with cuts you can administer instruments with tapered points, not by cutting deep as to make it go beyond the bone of the chest, and must leave a margin or a circle on the point so that the point does not go beyond the bone; and you should have more of them, each one in its own place of the space of the bone, so that you can have tapered points for every test; and this is the form of the three kinds of tapered instruments:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The thing that is pierced into the bone when it breaks is such that you put on the inner side of the bone, and turn to your two hands until you see that the bone is pierced; then set the tarry [tournure] elsewhere a little after, and do it all around, and then strike at the incisions the space between the joints, and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you take out the bone from your hand, or from any of the instruments that you have, such as pliers, pincers; and guard that you do not touch the brain or the sinus.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and taken out the bone, and it is found that some part is left behind on the bone at all other instruments resembling an incisor, but it should be more thin and subtle than those other incisors; and if there are no small bones or scales remaining, then take them lightly with one of the instruments; and then cure the wound as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And other ways of work are this because the Gauls say, which is more wise; and his words are very strong, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, at this place or where there is a fracture open, so when you have uncovered that part, you will put below the head of this incision, lens-shaped, because it is this shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, and it is the damaged part in both sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then with a small hammer above, so that you copy the bone lightly all around, and take good care of the protection of the fabric that is under; if it is scraped against the bone, so carefully cut the bone, because cutting well causes no harm, but fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the break of the bone does not penetrate to the skin, and the bone is broken only above, and there are small pieces, so it covers again that roughness, and removes the scales with a subtle rasp that you must have in various quantities, in order to fit each one as comfortably as possible, according to the work and figure of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you choose before many raspers, and after more subtle ones, and do not stop doing this until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other delicate hair cuts and small breaks, it is necessary to adapt the fit according to its direction; and this is a thing that no one has replied to those who have put their study into this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the abscess is uncovered, it is necessary to apply a linen strip soaked in oil rose according to its quantity, and rub it on the wound; then take another doubled strip, either twice or thrice, and soak it in wine and oil rose, and place it over the first strip; and do this as lightly as possible, so that you don't crush the abscess, and afterwards apply another ligature, and do not tighten it too much unless the abscess begins to heal; and leave it on for one or two days, until the abscesses are appeased, then remove it, and administer medicines such as rose roots, wheat flour, and incense powder, and other similar things; and make a powder of these things, and apply it to the wound, and administer additional medicines with mastication; beware that the wound is entirely clean, lest you leave any discharge, or allow any bowels to be bound up, for when bowels are tied on the skin over the brain, they burst and cause great evil for the patient; for when something mordant is placed on the abscess, it poisons from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Precaution first then, if no other accidents come to the patient as we have said, because it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if no other accidents come to the patient only because of the medicine we have placed on it, which has virtue, then it is fitting that you take a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and in vinegar I bind, and put it on the wound; then apply the cure of cures as he requires, until he is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the neck are broken together, or one by itself, because they are two bones; and the lower one is cartilaginous, and does not break unless it bends or twists, and then becomes sound.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is fitting that you pour your small dose or powder into the broken part, and place it inside your index finger, and in the pouch, for safety, until the bone comes back to its natural shape; and do this gently, so that the patient does not feel pain by your operation.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	If the break is in the upper part of the neck, and it cannot come down to its place, so that you put an equal weight on the head of a straw a little bit thick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If the break is in two parts, do it again and hasten to restore the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or fifteenth, when the apothecary's cauterization has been applied, then put a cloth of linen over the neck area that has been broken.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Where you put the other part, if the break is there; and let the coverings be as thick that they fill up the holes in the neck.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And said a restorer that we must moisten the coverings in butter, and move each person daily.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem good to me, but it is necessary that they be moist in the preparation of wool and powder of flour; then leave the tent, until the bones are hard, and the cartilages hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes you should replace the tents with chicken fat in its place, and if it has a wrapped cloth on it, and holds the wound, and blows the sick person into it, then make a small incision to see.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess comes to the head while you are working, apply hot or wet cotton in oil rose, or in a poultice of dayquil.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.
