And if the abscess does not come, apply plaster without delay, made of semolina flour and incense powder, conjoined with chicken fat, then place light cauterized cloths on it, and do not bind the wound; and if the wound is small and broken into little pieces, take out the instruments that are suitable for this, then close the wound and care for the surrounding flesh and joints, and sew so that plaster and ointments are suitable for this; and if there is no pain in the abscess, apply the treatment of tents, and put pounces of vinegar, until he is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	About the jaw fracture
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is fractured under, and there is no wound to prevent it, and the fracture is only present, without breakage in others, if one notices a slight swelling.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is fitting that if the fracture is on the right side, you put your right index finger in the mouth of the patient; and if it is on the left jaw, put your right index finger into the hand on the right side, and gently push the fracture inside, and tie off with a bandage.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is displaced upward by two parts, it is fitting that you extend the second part so that they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movements of the teeth happen, or breakage, so that an iron or silver thread is strained, then put on the broken mandible cote, and put on the double drapel; and put on the double drapel with a well-made stake, or a piece of leather long and wide according to the mandible, and tie it above the mouth as you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light viandes.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, if you remove it three times, and then put back to its proper place; and apply plaster on top, with powdered flour of arsenic or fine powder, after you have extracted the cote; and put on the plaster a light linen cloth, and if the plaster dries, and the disposition of the patient does not change, let it remain until he is healed; often the healing takes place in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess comes on a joint, then follow what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if it has both a break and an open wound together, reward with none of the bone that is extracted; for such subtlety of extraction is more suitable.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then enlarge it according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you have extracted all those bones and it remains empty for a while, cut the wound, if it is wide, and apply plaster according to what is suitable, in order to prevent infection, until it is safe.
de la forcele	of the gallbladder
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The gallbladder breaks more than once near the shoulder, and the break is in three ways: or it is broken and separated into two, and there are pieces, and this is lighter to restore; or there is a break with an open wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	Instruct the surgeons to set the break when it comes with an injury, so that you have two ministers, one who holds the arm in place where the fracture feels the breaking force; and the other stretches out the neck towards the part; then put equal the break on both hands, so that the form is as it should be, without any appearance or shape.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	If you must further extend it, put a round spear of cloth or linen on the patient over the shoulder, so that it is big according to your need; and gently stretch, and hold tight the spear with your hand, so that you put equal the break, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	If you cannot treat the head of the fracture outside, because it is coming in full, then it is fitting that the patient lies on his back and puts a bolster under the shoulder; and gives to the minister's shoulder downwards, so that the bones of the fracture are lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then instruct the break to your shoulders, and if you find any debris, it is necessary that you cut through them; and carefully take out the pieces lightly, and if the bone cannot be joined together for any reason, and you strike one of the incisors with it, but do not apply excessive force to this instrument, to ward off its sharpness:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it seems like a spoon, and it is not made of hair, and so large as it may be, according to the size of the bone and the power of the work; and have two handles, just as you see, and one wide and the other narrow, just as is the roughness of the wound that you have made when you cut the bones; and once you are sure about the depth of the incision, then sew the wound, and if the roughness is small, or you doubt the depth, then apply the dressing of cloths and gauze according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if an abscess comes to a head, apply it in oil of rose and in ashes and in wine, and put on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The binding of the bone, when it is painful and swollen, is that you put on the bone the plaster made from flour of the mill and of ashes and wine, and put on light strips, and place a spear under the shoulder joint, if you have need; then take a great bandage one palm wide, put double strips over the strip, the plaster; then take a small needle three fingers wide and long, and thread it through the bandage so that the top of the bandage is on the shoulder joint; and place the needle under the break, and turn the bandage over onto the neck, and under the shoulder blade and to the side it heals, and in each part you bind, and when you see that the limb holds the break firmly, and you see clearly that the needle does not move above the broken bone, so put on the binding every day, and when the ligature comes loose, then release; and have the patient lie on his back, and under the shoulder blade, for to lift the instrument high; thus he will be cured by the application of the splint to the forceful pull of the shoulder, or you tie his arm to the neck, and do not untie him in case of a bad accident happening, just until twenty days pass; then reapply the plaster if you see that it needs to be done, and bind and release it so, till he is restored; and he will be restored within twenty-eight days, and less often than many people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Of a shoulder break
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It is often the case that when the shoulder breaks or dislocates, one must not apply force to it unless by touch; if he appears as his break is formed, and repositions according to its natural shape, in all sorts of ways you can; then put powder from the mill with a lot of water, and light strokes, and put on two napkins; then put on an elbow band, not too big or small, but slightly larger than the shoulder, so that one strip of the band is not too tight, nor too loose; and then tighten the band so firmly that it doesn't move from its place, and look at the band every day; and when he is able to lift his head, if possible, so that the joint comes back into place, and let the patient rest on his side; for in twenty or twenty-five days the shoulder is restored.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	If a piece of the bone is torn away and points downwards under the skin, it should be pulled out upwards, and the bone, and do what we have said in the breaking of the abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the break of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The flesh is sometimes broken in the middle, but it happens rarely; but it breaks often in secret.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, if it inclines towards the underside, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of warmth, and swelling, and by chance vomit blood, and expose the broken marrow, and the flesh feels bad.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And restoration is done when the patient lies on their back, and you put a cloth between the shoulders, then press the shoulders, and reassemble the ribs to your hands, and subtly place it in every manner possible until the figure of the bone is as it should be; then place plaster and poultices above the subtle part of salt, or another lightweight material, and tie it up with a strip around the broken bone, so that it does not move; and turn the binding round to the back, and tighten immediately, and reward each hour the bandage, and if it loosens, tighten; and if it is desired to loosen, because of corrosion or itching that comes to the patient, or pain or abscess, do haste, and release, and shave the poultice, and address those who have come for cures; then reattach the poultice, and bind tightly until they are sane.
de la brisure des costes	of the fractured ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	It is observed that the fracture of the ribs comes only from their great thickness after the back, and in the chest area, and they bend only because they are smooth; and one feels very well during the examination with these.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the remedies are that you put equal the break, as it is fitting.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply plaster and bind with a stick if you have need.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the rib fracture turns inwards, the patient feels great pain, and sticking, as well as pleurisy, because the bone presses against the membrane; they feel pain, and swelling, and vomiting, with a great amount of bleeding, and it's a source of ill health, and the old ones have said that this was a serious condition.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if those who say it is proper to administer meat that inflates the belly, in order to break the fracture away from the bone.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this unless pus comes out of the wound.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then the blood.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that one should put ventouses on the limb, to suck out the blood, and this seems reasonable; nonetheless, there is doubt whether the ventouses attract the surplus blood at the limb due to its weak condition.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that one should cover the limb with a linen cloth soaked in hot oil, and put tourniquets between the ribs to straighten the joint, then treat the patient with the cure of bleeding, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu'il ne puet soffrir par l'os qui point la toile, 
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient to place damp cloth wrappings in rose oil upon the abscess, and apply it to the wound; cure as long as the pus flows, and bind with linen above the cost or where it must be, so that the cost may heal.
de la brisure dou col	of the broken collarbone.
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	There is no fracture of the bone in the collarbone, and it does not occur when he bends; and also there is a fracture of the spine on the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when it happens that there is a fracture and you see whether he will be healed or not, if you see his hands softened and swollen and dead, and they cannot move nor stretch, and when you press them with an needle, if they do not feel.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Those who have died from more severe dislocations, and if they are silent and feel well when their joints are strained and not moved, know that the bone joint is saved, and that patients recover, if it is put in treatment.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if such a thing comes to the back of the spine, and you see whether it heals or not, take care if the bones are softened, and if the accidents are near the hands, and on the back, they suddenly drop into place without will; and when you have put it back onto its own stomach, it drops into place with will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is put back onto its own back and it wants to be healed, but cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that death comes upon those who do not labor in their own treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to pass, then it is a lighter thing.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is to reward him if there is an abscess hot, if he puts oil of rose or oil of milk on the spine, as long as it is appeased; then put a comfortable and dry plaster on top, bind with a string, and command the patient to rest; and do not lie down on that side where he feels pain, until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if some bone is severed, it is appropriate to cover the wound; and take out the bone, then assemble both lips of the wound, if they are large, with a seam, then treat with ointment in a salve, as long as he is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called "the keys of the cow", pour into his pouch from your left hand, and place it equal to the other hand to your power, then put on the plaster and the stake, if you have need; then bind him, and if there has been a bone severed, if you make up, take out the bone, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the break of the shin bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It often happens that the shin bone is fractured, and if it has been, even if only a little, then apply some pressure to the head; and stretch it out long, and incline it towards the padded part, and the pain will come to the patient in the same way as a puncture, and swelling.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you stretch out your hand above, until you are above the fracture; and see what the fracture is and its shape; and if the fracture is only at the head alone, then apply an even cast, until it takes on a natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, or it inclines towards the inside, then have the patient lie on his stomach, until the restoration of that fracture has been made known.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	When you have made it even, then place a splint on the splinter, and put a stake of wood or bone on top, and bind the break so that it does not move; and apply the splint to the lower side of the ribs until they are even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to lie on his healthy side, or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess comes in the foot, do not touch it, until it is smoothed out, and put on what we have previously mentioned; and then return to restoration, and bind as necessary, unless there is any other adverse occurrence, and this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of a shoulder dislocation
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder joint is that which is between the clavicle and the head of the shoulder blade, and if it is broken, then one must restore it according to one of two methods: one method is that you take a stick of wood plaited in the middle knot, following this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And join as two shoulders to two joints, and bend them upwards, and tie the patient on one side; then put the man in bed with broken arms on his chest, until he comes to the aid, and has made an arrangement for a splint of wood, then bend upon any heavy thing or have it stretched out by the servants; then set the mirror on the breakage equal to its hands together, until the breakage returns so as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And another way is that you serve the patient on his bed, and tie his hand to his neck; then command two servants to pull up the part above the breakage with their hands, and the others below by all its joints, and stretch out each one to their side.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more difficult, then tie the joint below the breakage, and above the breakage, and stretch each one of the servants to their side.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	If the shoulder break is near the head of the shoulder, so it should be put with the middle tie under the joint, and the other one towards the bone; and thus if the break is towards the bone, it should be put with the lighter tie, without labor, until the break is even on its own and on its side; then put the break in such a way as it needs, and hold tight, so that abscesses do not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	If abscesses come, do not tighten it until the seventh day, and put on a moist linen in a warm place and in oil rose, until the abscesses are calmed; then hold tight, and the way to hold it is that you put plaster on the break, then assemble the arm onto the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the breast; and put a bandage, and hold onto the shoulder and the arm, so that the arm stays in place, unless any thing prevents it, or if the bone is not set.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	If you doubt that the bones do not move, then use stakes, and put a larger and stronger stake on top of the break, with two stakes spaced in between each stake, so that each stake is as large as it takes to pass through three parts of the break; then strain across the stakes, just as I told at the beginning of this chapter about the break.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the stakes placed and strained across them, just as we have said, when you restore the broken limb, and doubt the abscess is cut out, leave it closed for seven days, just as we have said; then examine each of the seven days whether inflammation has come or life returns to the limb, where the swelling does not come, or the redness cannot come to the member because it is too tightly strained.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the advice, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if such an accident does not happen, then the limb should only be dressed with linen cloth in a similar manner, every hour of the day or night, until the fracture does not move, or is mellowed out; for if it adheres by the virtue of medicine, and gives back to the patient food that we have placed before him, in this way that the food be at first subtle; and when he begins to take it again, so long.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the arm and leg should be reset in forty days, entire; and therefore one must dress and administer bath and medicine to alleviate.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	If the bowstring is twisted and stuck, so that it cannot be untied for one or two days.
de la brisure du bras	Of a broken arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "fossicle", one being small and that one enclosing the pouchet, and the other large, and that one below, towards the little bone; for by chance, it is only the larger fossicle that breaks alone, or only the smaller one, and by chance both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones break, restorations are light, and recoveries, and when the larger bones break, recoveries are bad, and more grievous than when both together broke.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only the small bone that broke alone, you must gently extend it, and set it even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	For the great frost, they must pull it harder; and stretch out to the cussin, and put his pouch higher with his hand than with others, and draw his petis below with greater effort than with others, so that the patient crosses himself above himself, and stretches to the cussin in front of him more high, lest the patient suffer no labor; then extend one's outstretched arm to the part below his hand, or at the joint, and another minister to the other above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then put him in the mirror, according to his best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the breakage there are pieces, each one put back in its place; and if it has no matching part that can be held together, and you cannot restore it to its proper place, then make a bone cast, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	If they have a break with a wound, I told the single healer about it; so take care.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	If in the beginning of restoration, abscesses burst forth, then I apply a dressing made of wax melted in oil rose and white beeswax; so that it is neither too hard nor too soft; and tie the dressing on top gently until the abscesses are calmed down.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then apply the wax, and I put an emplaster made of powder from the mill with a lot of lard, so that I place the splints, and so that the splint of the break is set more firmly, and just a little larger than the others; and know that it must have six splints or more, for such dispositions: whether the break is in one of the bones, or in two; and tighten above the break more than elsewhere, and always less when removing, as I told at the beginning of the chapter; and so be the coverings that are on top of the break soft and moist, not too hard nor harsh; and let the thread, from which it is strained, of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, just as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the limb and the joint after some time.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if some bad accidents happen to the limb, such as a prick that comes to the limb, it is fitting to raise the limb in hot water, until the prickling subsides and the pain is alleviated; and let the limb not be too tightly enclosed.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then tighten the binding, and if the ligaments are loosened and the bones deviated, it is like a similar case, so address it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the swelling cannot come to the limb because it is too tightly bound, so that it can be freed, it is fitting to loosen it a little, and let it remain for some days, until the swelling subsides, and then tighten.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said will come to the patient, then do not bind or release anything within twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	and if they are to be bound, then stretch his hands to his neck, and so that his necks are even, and ward off movement and flexion, and let him sleep on his back; and know that this break is restored in thirty days or in forty-five, and perhaps in twenty days, according to the composition and constitution of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the hand fracture
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	know that at the back of the hand there is little fracture, and it often comes to nothing but inflammation many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	and when the finger of the hand is broken or inflamed, it is fitting that the patient should press crosswise, sitting straight before him equally; then put his hand above the outstretched palm, and extend the bent fingers, and set the broken bones in alignment, as long as they are well-set; and apply plaster and splints, unless an abscess comes, then place a stake according to the quantity of the limb; and so cover it with one yard of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	If the fracture is in the tendons within the belly of the palm, then make a splint of drapery and instruct the patient to wrap it around his broken palm; and then bind with a rope of leather, so that its thickness is as great as the palm of the hand, and binding him, as he should.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	If the fracture is in the finger, then it is advisable to put a splint above and another below the palm, so that the hand is straightened and upright, and then bind him all around with the hand, and secure the ligature between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	If the fracture comes to any of us on either hand, if it is swollen, then make it equal, as you can; and bind with the palm, and if you see, put a straight little splint to lift the fracture, and do not move. If the fracture is in other fingers, such as the index or another, make it equal, and tie with the healthy finger next to it; or tie them all together, so that they may bear weight, or put a splint above, as you have done for the swelled one; and take care in restoration and placement of the abscess, and heal those who come, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the shoulder breaks
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The bone of the shoulder is often broken, and this can be seen when it turns in front and behind; and restoration is done by fastening the joint above the break, and the other below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient becomes pale in his face, then stretches out each of these medical attendants to their equal part; and this is when the break is mended into the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is close to the root of the shoulder, then there are either one of the ligaments towards the bone, and the others below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And also if it is close to the joint, and then so are either the ligaments of the joint, or extension below; then put on the mires the bone equal to its two hands, until it be according to its natural figure, and then apply the plaster, and the bandage, so that abscesses do not come.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	If it has an abscess hot, let it be calmed then return to its work and cure; the treatment is done in that manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap the wound with a bandage double in II or III, and keep the swelling up, then turn the leg so that the heels touch at the root of the nail, and pour I long thread between the thigh and leg, loosen under the knee, and tie tight above the knee; then put above the wound stitches, and put an iron on the bone of the leg; then wrap with soft cloth eight times between the leg and thigh to tighten the bandage, then start tying tightly III twists or IV above the wound; and as you go up more above the wound, and less the tightness; then take out the II threads that you poured between the leg and thigh, and tie III nails that are above, then return below at the knee so much until you see at the feet; and tighten, if it does not move from its place, then leave it so, and if it comes no more swellings or inflammation or similar things.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	In case he has it, if the dislocation occurs, and addresses what comes to it, as we have said many times; and if it has pieces of bone that cling, he must be careful, if possible; and if not, he must break the limb, and treat with force; and the cure just like we have said, until he is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And at no time is the cube broken as if we were putting needles into it, in the shoulder and arm; for all ways of restoring such a thing do not relieve the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And so it is known that the cube can be restored in three or four days, or slightly more or less, according to the diversity of the complexion.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the groove of the gallbladder
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	They say that in the hollow of the groin there is often a break but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	But if it breaks, then it's not just a cut or a rupture, but rather an opening or a wound, which causes all pain and feels painful.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is as follows: one must put even the ones that are swollen on both sides, until they are assembled again; then apply the plaster, and if you have need, place an oval instrument in it, and tie it so as it should be; then treat all the dispositions we have spoken about for other breaks, like abscesses and similar things; and put into each accident what is suitable for him, until he is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the leg fracture
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Says that in the leg there are two bones, because one is called by right "mustelz", and the other is called "foscile"; and all other fractures occur as it comes to the arm, so that the restoration is like that of the same arm, and all wounds are made. And if both bones break together, then turn the leg from every part.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the subtle bones break, turn in front.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone breaks, there is great pain and you see it well; and turn below.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Therefore apply extension, and place it level, and tie the bandages equally; but however, if the break is ugly, and there are many pieces, then apply less extension so that it is lighter and easier to bear; and arrange according to your discretion.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, so take two fingers of fleshy cheeks that are purpled in the thigh from one side and from the other, and be long enough from the knee up to the joint; then wrap them around both ends of the leg, and tie them in the middle as well, and at this tying, do not allow the leg to move to the right or to the left, and thus it is good; and no one should apply more than two fingers of length to the thigh, and if it's hard, and you put it on for support, and properly done that in the break where there was a wound; and move each limb every day to see if it has an abscess or any other accident; so the cure as long as he is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the bone of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the knee there comes no break, but sometimes when a bone is on its foot it breaks and causes a wound, and in some cases only swelling.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if it has a bone break and you see the bones protruding one over another, if you put the patient's foot on the ground, just as if he were walking, and then put your foot on his side, so that the bones are lifted up, then press them together until they realign in their place; then apply plaster and strips, and put a small tube filled with powder into the space of the bone, then tighten it to the present state, and other things which you have need of.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, if you release the bandage, for you will find that the bones are evened out, whether they are broken, or swollen.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	Et s'il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is necessary that you not forget the other things I have said about other fractures, since we have spoken of them; and heal each accident as it suits.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the bone at the finger
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman is broken, if it becomes swollen, then incline it to the back part of her spine, and tie it behind; then fill in with fluff the nature of her illness of cotton, and put just as much as I said; then bind the woman's back, lift up the back piece by piece, and then let the cotton come out; when she wants to urinate, if the cotton comes out, and when she has urinated, take it out again, and do so for seven days before: if it is restored, and you see, take a vessel of wool, and tie one end of the wound with a rope, and pour all the vessel into her nature; then breathe into the rope tube until the vessel is emptied inside: nature will come back to the break; then fill with cotton again, and let it be so for some days, till it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	When the bone of the elbow is broken, or in a woman, so it heals like we have said about the bone of the hazelnut; and these close fractures are not concealed by the study and use of that person, and I will enter this in my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the breaks signify that there are more dangers on the right path of restoration, then therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose gizzard and put it in the wound; then wrap cloths around it, and let it remain for three days or more, and he will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of breaks with wounds
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is to be believed that the one who has breaks with wounds, especially if it is great, like the bones of the shoulder or arm or similar ones, will be healed now, if the remedies we have said testify to this.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healthy, then apply vitreous (glass) to it, for if you have nothing else, do so again on the same day or the next day, unless an abscess forms.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if an abscess forms, then leave the restoration for the next new day, until the abscess is allayed, and do not touch it or set it again on the third or fourth day, for you will cause a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone break is found near the joint of the shoulder, it is fitting to tie (or set) you lightly on the tip of your finger with a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not fitted to put it equal to your hands, then take that instrument made of iron, which has 7 or 8 fingers long, and its width according to the quantity of the wound; and for this, it is the duty of the surgeon to imprint 3 or 4, as needed in each cure of a fracture; and let it be small and not too tight, so that it does not bend under compression on the limb at your work, and be thin before, and thick from the middle towards the front, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And call it "palainche" because the heads of the bones should be put on top of the head of the bone that is visible; and the injection is done once, until it returns, and they are evened out one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	But if the break is subtle and the splints cannot well take hold of the bone, it is advised that you copy the head of the bone, until the splints have a good grip.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	But if you cannot restore the bone as we have said, then copy it with an instrument that is suitable for this purpose, such as a knife or needle, to your best ability; then take what remains stuck in the bone of roughness and small scratches.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is restored and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that he is not in his natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If it is so that it is in its place, then moisten the drapery in vinegar black, and carefully put it there; and do not put more on the wound than oil or anything else, lest it make porridge and corruption come; then administer salves when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover the covering all at once, according to the quantity of the wound, and be careful that the wound is not constricted with the break; and many times these foolish physicians have done this, and have brought the patient either death or corruption one time, and are the most harsh and rough among other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is great or infected, and you doubt that more accidents will not come upon it, as we have said, and you find pain in the limb, so that you should not put on salves; but instead cover with hard cloths, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after the first day or the second day that the bow is stuck to the wound, so keep what you put on top of it in all wine, and apply soothing salve for wounds, as a salve tetrafarmacon and similar things.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you dislocate the limb twice a day, morning and evening, until it is cooled and cleansed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be tied in a way that the bow can move freely along its edge lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if every day the wound does not heal, and it only gets worse again with new bowing, see that there are little pieces of bone, for this reason you must want to treat the wound with poultice, and remove all these useless parts that come from the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	If a fistula comes to the liver, or another kind of corruption, then it is wise that you cure it, according to what he says in his chapter before this.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and opens on the limb, like the ribs or the shoulder, and other similar bones of the great members, do not treat me, because often it results in death, but let him live until he dies; by chance he will pass away after twenty days or thirty, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of those who come from the stool (feces).
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	They come many times after the health of the break, especially when it's near the joint, and this is a strange thing to see with the figure of the limb; and by chance he cannot do his limbs their own work.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Instruct the patient therefore to let his limbs be fresh: if he is administered medicinal substances, such as aloes, incense, and mirrour, and sarcocolle, acaice, and similar things, so that you take none of these things or all together, and mix them with vinegar medicinal or with abundance of wine or with oil; and place it on the wound in poultices, and apply well, and do not untie it by hand for days; and then untie, and renew another one until the nodulation is removed; or you tie up a piece of wool finely made; because the properties of the wool are such that it removes all swellings above the members; and if the nodation has been converted into hardness like stone, and it requires removal, so that the copse under, and make the appearance apparent; or you bring back to any rasour, until it is removed, and the cure as long as it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	A limb which is weak after the garrison.
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is restored and stays after the weak and subtle limb, it happens for many reasons: because one thing is that he was tied too tightly, and did not tie as well as he should have; or because there are too many ligatures, and cannot come to the limb; or because of many inflammation; or because of too great movements, but not in its own hour; or because it has little blood in his body, so is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and make his body soft, until there are many times its original size; and administer baths, and give him joy and relief; then put powder on the limb, so that the powder brings great swelling to the limb, and the inflammation often appears with watered-down blood, until the swelling ceases in the limb; and return it to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	One tortured limb after the health.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the bones break open, and the form of the limb is ugly, never trust in false remedies that say you must break the limb completely; for many fools have done this in our land, and this remedy is wrong, and it leads to great harm, and sometimes death. However, if the nodules and torture are fresh, it is better to wait until they form pus of hot water or cook herbs like thyme, and roots, and melilot, and similar things; and you make them apply a softening medicine, just as aqua vivens does well, and take the muscillagium of thyme, and mix with lard or olive oil of sycamore, and make it apply; or you take fatty figs, and grind them with fennel of colly, and similar remedies that ease the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the nodal joint is loosened by constant friction and prolonged rubbing with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And move each limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortuosity is old and hardened, like stones, and it needs to be loosened with iron, so that you can cover just at the bone, at a subtle incision, lightly; and put on a cushion and study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	This begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes upon, if it can be now set in place again.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For when it is late, if the swelling increases, and by chance if he sets it on a pin; because that is not advisable to move him until it subsides: many times have caused vomiting and other pains; watchful, when it happens, make the patient recover, then let him go, until the abscess is calmed; then raise the limb with hot water and oil, then gently move each member as the cure comes in its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have prescribed the chapters for dislocation of the head joint at a price.
des mandibules	of the jawbones.
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Often the jawbones are dislocated in such a way that they have a little bone of their own and become soft for a little; or they are completely dislocated, hanging down to the chin, and causing the patient to swallow saliva from the mouth which he cannot hold, nor close his mouth, and stammering with the words, and being unable to speak properly.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When small dislocations occur, they return to their original place by multiple movements.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is whole and completed, you should immediately reset it with haste, and do not neglect it; in such a manner that the ministers make the head of the patient moistened with a mixture of some of his hands into the root of the dislocation of the lower jaw inside the mouth, when the dislocation is two parts; and if the other two are from both hands, they should be avoided so that it remains even; and instruct the patient to loosen his mandibles, and move them from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the mixture is put even, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it returns to be griewed, especially when both mandibles are assembled, apply hot water and oil as long as the reset is made lightly; do not neglect to set it again, just as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	Instruct the patient to let them return to their normal state and let the mouth clot naturally with softening; then place wet cloths soaked in rose oil made of olive oil and beeswax on it lightly; and tie it gently with moist threads; and put the patients to sleep on their back, with their arms between two pillows, so that they do not move neither with their right nor left hand, nor try to make any effort, but take gentle food until the pains are gone, and the mandibles are covered; and then bring them what they want lightly, and do not work on opening the mouth to eat or drink, until the mandible is well covered and healed.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be put back in place within an hour and are not converted to their original state, then fevers and chills appear accustomed, and by chance vomiting appears with stool.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then know that it's destruction; and many have died from this in seven years.
de la forcelle	of the shoulder
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	the shoulder cannot be moved along the ribs inside and below the skin, and is dislocated every time without fail, and it hurts very much.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is that the sick person lies on their back, and stretches out his arms; and then presses the forearm to his palm, and it returns; then puts on the plaster and bandage, and tightens it; and the head that has been turned outward cannot be moved again; unless not, and if it dislocates again, then he should reset it in its place, as we have said; then puts on the plaster and bandage, and tightens it, and commands the patient to rest until he is healed; and thus, at the same time, are restored the hips of the saddle, when they are returned to their place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	The head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	There are three ways the shoulder joint can be dislocated: one way is that it dislocates downward from the upper part of the arm below; and the second way is that it dislocates from the lower part of the elbow; and sometimes it dislocates upward, which happens rarely, and never above the shoulder or within the neck; and more often downward toward the joint itself, just like those who have little strength, for they fall immediately; whereas those with strong bodies take longer to fall, but eventually do.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes it happens to some people that they strike or crush the shoulder with an abscess, and think that this is a dislocation because of the swelling.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is therefore necessary that you try it out, as long as you are certain about it; and then begin the treatment.
