Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known that dislocations occur when they are pulled towards the joint, and you will notice a difference between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find manifest differences between them; and you will find at the head of the shoulder an indentation, and below the joint at the bony prominence the head of the shoulder, just as if it were one bone; and the patient cannot bring their hand back to its original position, nor move any part of the body; and similarly, if it is dislocated upwards, it will be manifestly visible at the top, because you find it manifestly at the joint; and this kind of dislocation is not difficult to treat when it is new, or if the child is ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	Instruct the patient to lift his hand up high, then put your fingers under the joint, and lift the joint up high with force in its place; and the ministers will lift the hand and extend it up high, because it is placed underneath; if it happens suddenly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said after a day or two, it is fitting that the patient be bathed in hot water; and he should be administered an aromatic and soothing treatment, like a decoction of alums, fenugreek, and mallolth in hot water, and be given medicine. Then, set the patient on their back, and put a towel under the joint at a length equal to a foot, not too soft nor too hard, then place your fingers on the top of the shoulder joint, and gently lift it; and treat the patient's hand. And another minister should pull the head of the shoulder if it does not move downwards; for now the shoulder returns completely, and you see if it is restored according to this manner: and thus you make the patient be present with a man who is larger than the patient; and stand upright against the costal side, and pour water over the shoulder joint of the patient from under, and lift the joint up high, so that the patient hangs in the air; and another minister treats the patient's hand downwards towards the abdomen.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	If the patient is too light, then he will lie with him on any heavy thing, and the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And it is done in another way: and it is as one strikes a long nail into the ground, so that the joint moves like a piston, not too big nor too small; then put down the patient, but if he has wrapped himself snugly under, and the limb is bent on a long stick; then extend his hand towards the opposite part in such a way that the joint returns to its place quickly; and if it does not return for all these things which we have said, do this cure: take a nail of two arms' length and four fingers wide, with the head reinserted in depth below the shoulder.
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Instruct the patient to lie on his chest under the folded cloth, so that he does not bleed; then put the bandage on the patient. And extend one arm above the fist of the long one, and tie the assistant's hand on top of the fist, and the arm to the head of the hand; then put the arm above the barrow of one straight line and broad, and so extend the hands downward, and leave the body hanging from the other side: the joint will now be aligned.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is so in any manner, if it pleases you to do so, then put under the bandage one sparrow of wool equal, then put on the plaster mixed with powdered flour, with incense and myrrh from the bees, above all the shoulder and around; then pull out from under the bandage immediately, and turn the ligature onto the plaster, and encircle the hand at its neck, so that the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	Instruct that it is necessary to treat the patient little by little, until the limbs are comfortable, because he will heal faster; and then treat more after 5 days or 7, and move him; and if it is firm and not softened, it is cured.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is swollen due to moisture or for another reason, it is necessary that you administer cauterizations at three points, as he is placed in front of or on the cautery desk.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do this and he dislocates after 7 days, and the joint does not stay in place, and cannot lift one arm above, then you will know that the nerves at the top of the shoulder are injured or compressed or softened; and you will know that the joint has never been fixed in its proper place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that occurs at the elbow and knees, or behind, is done by impulse and stretching of hands, and it serves another joint, and one should treat until he is whole.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing there comes a gretez at the member, and late in movement, then use the patient many times, as long as that gretez is alleviated, and returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the shoulder.
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	It says that the joint of the shoulder is dislocated at points, and returns to points; and if it has been dislocated from all parts, and itself in front and behind, for there are no reposements, because one sees well and feels well; and a dislocation occurs according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick hand with the healthy one, so you can see it open.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	Because the joint is swollen, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder in any way.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is therefore necessary to set it so that the abscesses come out when it is applied, because if abscesses come out while it is being applied, then it will be painful to bring it back; and by chance it cannot be restored in its entirety, especially when it is at the back; for this is worse than other dislocations, and brings greater pain, and by chance death may also occur.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And when it is restored, in the way that one can bring it back, then you extend his hand to your two hands; and spread out his arms, and stretch out his fingers accordingly, from top to bottom, and push into the joint as far as possible, both above and below, so that the joint moves again to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, so it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and from the root of the palm he feels the cost which is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not return to its place, then give strong extension; and let two assistants extend the arm, and two assistants hold it so that it does not move with extension; then turn the arm from each side, once you have wrapped a double cloth long and wide around it; and when the mire fixes the jointed joint in his hand, he feels no oil to rub the joint, then burst the joint, until it returns; and when it is in its place, put on plaster sec with some of egg white, and bind tightly, and hang the arm by a cloth round the neck of the patient, and let him rest for a few days, then release.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	If the joint is firmly in its place, then untie it and let it go; and if you see that the joint does not tighten properly, then reapply the plaster and tie it again, and let it be for some days, until it is tightly set; then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	If he feels pain after the joint has been put back in place and it tightens up, then bathe him and rub him well, and press firmly until he is relieved; or put on a poultice made from fatty lamb skin, and let it be for one day and one night, then remove it, and bring him into the bath; and when he sweats, rub the joint temperately, then put on the poultice again, and then in the bath; and do this twice or three times until he is cured; and if you see, put on a poultice made from fatty fennel cooked with butter, and strain it onto him; so that it will return to its original shape.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand is dislocated, and when it returns it is lighter than all other joints. It must be returned to its place immediately, in the same spot where it was dislocated, so that the swelling may go away, or there will come a severe inflammation.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And if the return is such that you place the diseased hand on a table, and stretch out your fingers, and straighten the wrist, so that it puts its palm on the appearance of the joint, and presses it hard until it returns to all parts, you must first look whether it is well placed; then put the patient's lower back of his hand on a table at extension and return.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	If a dislocation is at the back of the hand, he instructs the patient to put his back on his hand over the table, and the operator puts his hand over that appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it now returns, then this is well; if not, if the straining of plaster poultices appeases abscesses, he should let him continue in that way again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	If he cannot bear it, and you cannot put him back after some days, the joint will remain twisted; and there is nothing worse for the patient but that his hands are swollen, and he cannot strain anything anymore: then you must know that the nerves have been cut, or the arteries; otherwise there is no other remedy except to cut away by cautery in that case, and perhaps it may not amount to anything else.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	When the hands are at rest, put on the plaster that we have said, then strain and let it be in place for three days, then take it off and leave it as is.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not move well and it has no inflammation, then apply the poultice of hot water and rub until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the wrists
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	There is no case where the wrists are dislocated to any degree, sometimes on one side of the wrist or on the back of the palm or belly; therefore, if they are displaced, and the joint is put into its place by being held in one's pouches until it recovers, then support the head of the wrist, and move it towards the part where it is dislocated; and leave it for two days, and then reset it on the same day; and do not bind it, as we have said, and set it free once a day, and make it move, and tie it in place; and do this frequently, until it becomes tight, and do the same, if they are dislocated to the belly of the wrist, and do what you have done before, until it is healed; and do the same, when they are dislocated on another side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Due to dislocation of the shoulder skin
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the skin of the back or neck is dislocated, or if there are multiple dislocations, and there is no treatment, for fear of death, the patient rushes to their grave.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the dislocation often occurs spontaneously, not voluntarily, and cannot be held in place, and many members become swollen, or both legs or two arms; and many times the skin is pulled to four parts; which when it is pulled to the back is called "gilbositez"; if the gilbositz has come from childhood: if there is no treatment or healing of the whole.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from falling or percussion, or similar things, the ancient ways of treatment with great words, bring no great benefit; but I have shortened it according to my intention, and have made instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I dis that in the goutiness that comes to the foot in front, no gain or health is gained; and also that which comes directly into both sides, and cannot be cured with fire unless it comes to the back, as I say; and it is that the patient should lie extended on his face in one straight line, and have straining below him, so that he does not bleed; then drive one nail into the head in the earth firmly, and another at the ankle, and tie a strap behind the legs of the sick man, and another at the hams, and knees, and ankles; and two servants will see the straps, one to the head and the other to the ankle, among the two nails; and they should be well closed, the nail as we have said, and the mallet meets its palms on the stake firmly, until it revives.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return by this cure, take a table of three arms long, and sharpened so that it appears, and the patient is in pain, and pour the head of the table into the joint, then put the middle of the table on the spine; and place his feet on the other end of the table, and press well, until he returns to health; and if you see, do it at the elbow that turns towards the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And so you will fix two stakes at the head of the patient's arm with one hand long and at the feet of the other two hands long, each stake having in between them an inch of space; and on each stake there should be one pin over it and under, a palm-sized piece of metal; and on each pin there should be one pin turning, or the stick bends, so that they do not move; and between each two pins there should be another pin turning, because the sticks turn, and there should be in each turning two palm-sized pieces of metal to turn the stick; and then tie the link which is among the crossbars to the head, and the other link to the feet to the other sticking pin, and each of the servants will turn their stick at the entire length, and the master will put the spine equal as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, 
des dislocations de la hainche	Dislocations of the hunchback
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	The joints of the hunchback and shoulder joints come only from dislocations alone, not at all like other joints; and the joint of the hunchback is displaced according to four parts: inside and outside, and in front and behind; and more inside than out, and less displacement in front and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of dislocations inside is that when you join the diseased leg to the healthy one, it becomes longer, and the patient's knees are more open than the healthy ones, and they cannot double their knee movement in the fire; and it is the joints that are located near the inflamed abscesses, because the head of the shoulder joint comes out.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the signs of he who suffers from this defect are such that these accidents are contrary to those foreseen.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of he who has this before him are such that if his leg is completed well; all pain, do not double the knee with suffering, and if you want to make him walk, he cannot beforehand, and holds back his urine, and swells the groin, and when he walks, passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of he who has this behind him are such that he cannot stretch his knee, nor double it, and because that leg is more bent than the other, and the groin swells less, and the head of the chest bone is at low level beneath the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The signs of this dislocation are such that if you remember such dislocations in the past, and they remain according to their nature, there is no cure; and it is not advisable for him to have any confidence.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in that one who has the fresh dislocation, and it is of four kinds of dislocation, so hasten to return the joint, and push it inside and forth, and move at the right arm and left; by chance if it returns, and there is need for no other cure.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, so it is fitting to bind the leg with four strong bandages, or at one tie that binds above the knee; and one of the other ministers extends his hand in such a way that he pours water over his hands below his waist, then tightens a soft cord under the belly; and another ties the head to the neck; and stretches up and down all together once, until the patient is lifted off the ground once, and remains standing.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common for four reasons, and if dislocation has returned, as we have said, this is very good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If this is not the case, it is advisable to put treatment on its semblance When dislocations are in the swollen area, it is advisable that you lift the patient onto his healthy side, then place a bandage at the root of the scapula, and the one below the angle, then tighten the bandage towards the angle and the fleshy part; then take hold of other assistants with your arms, and wrap the big bandage around the sick shoulder, and stretch it in front: if it returns to its place now; and this method of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot tighten it in the manner that we have said, it is advisable to tie both feet of the sick together with a strong bandage on both heels, and on both knees; so that the sick leg is extended two fingers more than the other limbs; then suspend him by the head of a stick, and above the ground two hands wide; then command one assistant to wrap around the scapula, and have other assistants hang with the patient, who wraps together to form the jointure, because the joint returns now immediately.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocations are in the absence of, so grieve the patient, as we have said to one who has gout, and tie off the limb itself properly, and on the bone also; then put two stitches, one on the head and one on the other on the joint; then insert a stick between the bones into the malady with the shape; and make planted moist cloths around it, so that the patient does not bleed, then stretch each of these ministers to him, and tie the limb with his hand tightly to the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, that's good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, put on an ice. I.e., a table, and press it as we have said in the gout, and grieve the patient on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when dislocations occur in front of them, it is suitable to stretch the patient’s leg quickly, and as I have said; and place his pain above the angina of the malady, then press with the other hand, and stretch across to the groin.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if dislocations occur at the back, it is not suitable to stretch the patient downward or lift him up on the earth, but rather that he should be as he was before the dislocation occurred, just as we have said in lying down on the two hocks; and so be placed with his face up, and the ligature extended as we have said before, and it must not press on the joint at the table; and will be to the point when the patient stretches out his legs, and they will be even; then add the splints, and apply the plaster, and the straining of a bandage, so that the hock does not move; and if he rests three days or four, then he is removed, and the plaster is applied again; and if you see that they are even, as before, and then leave it for three days; then remove it, and let him walk well, until his limbs become comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of a joint of the shoulder
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The joints are dislocated in three ways: that is to say, inside and outside, and at the back; and do not occur on the front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you command the patient to bend his knee to his groin, and if he does not stay there, know that he is dislocated; and the restoration of all such is that you have him sit upright, and stretch out his leg if he can, and place your back on his face, and put one foot under your feet; then take hold of his joint in your hands, and press between them, and bend both sides of the joint together; and another minister extends his foot, until the joint returns to its normal position, and the signs are that he is able to bend his knee again lightly; and apply plaster on it, and have him rest for three days or four, then take off the cast; and do not work the patient too hard, until his limbs are comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limbs are not at all moved by that, stretch them greatly, just as we said in the treatment of hemlock, so long as they remain safe.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the foot dislocation
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The feet are sometimes swollen, and sometimes completely inflamed, and they swell inside and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And if the signs are that the ankle is swollen and tender before the place where it is inflamed: gentle movement is lighter, and he must be stretched lightly in his hands only when he is swollen.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is completely swollen, it is convenient to seat the patient upright, and pull gently on the leg, above the ankle; then take the foot to your right hand, and then to your left twice, then stretch it up, and pour the foot into the top; and do this twice, as we have said, pouring and taking the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, when it does not return again, because it will come back; and if it cannot come back in such a way, then seat the patient on his back on the ground, and firmly press the passal between his knees, and tie strips around him so that he does not bleed; then pull the tendons gently, and other ministers extend the foot to his hands or to the ligament above the neck; then stretch each of these ministers equally, and the passal should be pressed tightly between the patient's knees to hold the patient when one stretches it; then place the mire equal on the dislocation at his hands, and other ministers pull the healthy leg downwards, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when she comes to a point, so she applies the plaster and bandages on top, and the wound forms, and binds the foot to the leg, and watches out for the nerves above the ankle, lest they become too tight; then leaves it for two days or three, and if the binding is moist, takes off the plaster; then releases it on the third day or a quarter, and ensures that the patient can walk again in four days; and if he walks to the end of the term, this is not a guarantee that he will not dislocate further.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes to a head, so you must calm it, just as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	of the two.
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When both are dislocated, so they must be extended with work, and it is a light matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Et if the dislocation is in any part of the back or foot, it is fitting that you make the patient sit on a level plain or on a table so right, and put your foot on what appears from these joints, then press down with your foot firmly, until it settles; and when it is even and does not open up anything, put under the plant of the foot a table at two heads, then strain and firm it, and let it stay three days, then release it; and make him rest, until he is well.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation, and you try to restore it, many times the patient dies: do not be presumptuous in treatment, unless you are skilled in the art and have used it for a long time, and if you are not pitiful, merciful, and cautious, do hard; use soothing medicines at the beginning of things, and let the patient be in God's hands, unless you see no hope of recovery; and when you see hope, reset the member to its place now, as soon as the abscess forms; and when the limb is set, administer soothing medicines again, and treat the wound as it seems fit, with dry ointments; and if with dislocation there has been a fracture, and small bones have been broken, treat them, and do what we have said about simple diseases; and beware of entering into fear, according to what I have said, for this is your fate, according to your Creator, and by the wisdom that arms you and your body.
Amen	Amen
